_Thought for 1m 16s_

## Zeta A result: actual exterior-pair source expansion

I treated the Zeta A instruction as the targeted test:

\[
\text{derive } f_\rho(t),\quad
r_\rho(t)=f_\rho(t)-f_\rho(m)-f_\rho'(m)(t-m),
\quad
\rho_2,\rho_4,
\]

then check whether the needed Bottleneck-C identity

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}
\]

is forced by the actual one-pair zeta source class.

The instruction is exactly the remaining rescue route identified in the handover: the formal local package already fails unless actual zeta-source rigidity excludes the \(r=u^2\) model. 

---

# 1. Actual one-pair source

From the draft, the one-pair phase-derivative contribution is

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

Set

\[
a:=1-\beta,\qquad b:=\beta,\qquad x:=2m-\gamma,\qquad u:=t-m.
\]

Then

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(m+u)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+(x+2u)^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+(x+2u)^2}.
\]

Affine subtraction removes only the \(u^0\) and \(u^1\) terms. Therefore the post-affine Taylor coefficients \(\rho_2,\rho_4\) are simply the \(u^2,u^4\) coefficients of this expression.

For one summand

\[
\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2},
\]

the coefficients are

\[
[u^2]\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2}
=
\frac{4c(3x^2-c^2)}{(c^2+x^2)^3},
\]

and

\[
[u^4]\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2}
=
\frac{16c(c^4-10c^2x^2+5x^4)}{(c^2+x^2)^5}.
\]

Hence the actual one-pair post-affine coefficients are

\[
\boxed{
\rho_2(\beta,x)
=
4a\frac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
4b\frac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\rho_4(\beta,x)
=
16a\frac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
16b\frac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
4\,
\frac{
a\dfrac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
b\dfrac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}
}{
a\dfrac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
b\dfrac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3}
}
}
\]

whenever \(\rho_2\ne0\).

---

# 2. Immediate conclusion: no intrinsic jet-locking identity

The required Bottleneck-C cancellation would demand

\[
\frac{\rho_4(\beta,x)}{\rho_2(\beta,x)}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

But the left side is a rational function only of the exterior-pair parameters \((\beta,x)\), while the right side is a background/local-total phase expression involving \(q_0=q(m)\) and \(q_0''=q''(m)\). Nothing in the one-pair expansion forces this equality.

More sharply: the one-pair source class supplies a two-parameter family of ratios \(\rho_4/\rho_2\). It is not locked to a universal expression in \(q_0,q_0''\).

---

# 3. Diagnostic special cases

## Critical-line symmetric case: \(\beta=\tfrac12,\ x=0\)

Then \(a=b=\tfrac12\), and

\[
\rho_2=-64,\qquad \rho_4=1024,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}=-16.
}
\]

The required identity would become

\[
-16
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

That is not a source-theoretic identity. It would require a special external relation between \(q_0\) and \(q_0''\).

## Far exterior-pair regime: \(|x|\gg1\)

Since \(a+b=1\),

\[
\rho_2
=
\frac{12}{x^4}
+
O(x^{-6}),
\qquad
\rho_4
=
\frac{80}{x^6}
+
O(x^{-8}),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}
+
O(x^{-4}).
}
\]

Again, this ratio is controlled by the exterior-pair distance \(x=2m-\gamma\), not by the Bottleneck-C expression in \(q_0,q_0''\).

---

# 4. Consequence for the local obstruction

The frozen top-row coefficient recorded in the draft is

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For \(i=j\), cancellation requires exactly

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

Zeta A’s calculation shows that the actual exterior-pair expansion does **not** force this. The single-pair source supplies

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
R(\beta,2m-\gamma),
\]

with \(R\) a nonconstant rational function. Therefore the desired identity can hold only on a special tuning locus, not as a structural zeta-source law.

---

# 5. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Zeta A does not find the hidden jet-locking law needed to rescue Bottleneck C.}
}
\]

More precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual one-pair expansion is compatible with free }(\rho_2,\rho_4)
\text{ behavior up to the rational constraints above.}
}
\]

This does **not** yet prove a literal zeta-source counterexample, because that belongs to Zeta B / Z2: one must show that actual exterior zero configurations can realize or approximate the bad \(r=u^2,\ q_0''=0\) formal model. But Zeta A removes the most direct rescue: there is no pair-internal identity forcing

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0.
\]

My recommendation: Zeta B should now test the realization map

\[
(\beta,\gamma,\text{other exterior data})
\mapsto
(\rho_2,\rho_4,q_0,q_0'')
\]

for local freedom. Zeta C should proceed under the assumption that the local obstruction survives.

## Zeta Global A — aggregate tail coefficient derivation

I am treating the active source atom as the **actual exterior functional-equation zero-pair atom** already used in the one-pair source formula

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

That atom already bundles the \(\beta\) and \(1-\beta\) symmetric partners. Conjugate ordinates, multiplicities, and any exterior cutoff/truncation are handled by the source index set and weights. This matches the Zeta handover’s one-pair setup and the current instruction that the only remaining rescue is a global zero-tail identity, not a one-pair locking law. 

---

# 1. Source index set and weights

Let

\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}(m)
\]

be the set of exterior source atoms relative to the current local patch. An atom

\[
\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}(m)
\]

is a functional-equation zero-pair datum

\[
\alpha=(\beta_\alpha,\gamma_\alpha)
\]

with multiplicity \(m_\alpha\), distance

\[
x_\alpha:=2m-\gamma_\alpha,
\]

and one-pair post-affine source

\[
r_\alpha(t)
=
f_{\beta_\alpha,\gamma_\alpha}(t)
-
f_{\beta_\alpha,\gamma_\alpha}(m)
-
f'_{\beta_\alpha,\gamma_\alpha}(m)(t-m).
\]

Write its midpoint expansion as

\[
r_\alpha(m+u)
=
\rho_{\alpha,2}u^2+\rho_{\alpha,4}u^4+O(u^5).
\]

The actual source weight is

\[
w_\alpha=m_\alpha\chi_\alpha,
\]

where \(m_\alpha\) is zero multiplicity and \(\chi_\alpha\) is any real exterior-window/cutoff factor used in the finite-tail construction. If no cutoff is being used, \(\chi_\alpha=1\). There is no additional sign from the one-pair phase derivative; signs enter through the jet coefficients \(\rho_{\alpha,2},\rho_{\alpha,4}\), not through \(w_\alpha\).

The collision amplitudes \(a_1,a_2\) are not zero-source weights. They factor through the promoted Bottleneck-C carrier and supply the first \(\delta\)-edge; they do not change the source-tail moment algebra. The handover explicitly records this bookkeeping correction: the amplitude \(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\) already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge, so the active coefficient is the frozen internal coefficient. 

---

# 2. One-pair coefficient recalled

For source atoms \(i,j\), the frozen top-row scalar is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{ij}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

This is the scalar controlling the \(S\)-component of the concrete top row

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]

The handover records the same active row, its \(S\)-coefficient

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7},
\]

and the same favorable phase-gap integral formula for \(\nu_{21,7}\). 

Define

\[
R_0
:=
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}.
\]

Then

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{ij}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{R_0}{144}
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

---

# 3. Aggregate double sum

The actual exterior tail is the linear source sum

\[
\eta_{\mathrm{ext}}
=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}}
w_\alpha \eta_\alpha.
\]

Since the active row is quadratic in \(\eta\),

\[
\eta_{\mathrm{ext}}^2
=
\sum_{\alpha,\beta}
w_\alpha w_\beta
\eta_\alpha\eta_\beta.
\]

Therefore the actual aggregate scalar is

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}
=
\sum_{\alpha,\beta\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}}
w_\alpha w_\beta
\nu_{21,7}^{\alpha\beta}.
}
\]

There is no structural exclusion of self-pairs \(\alpha=\beta\). The local countermodel and row formula already allow \(i=j\); excluding self-pairs would be an artificial projection, not the quadratic expansion of the actual total exterior source. The prior audit also treats the \(r_i=r_j=u^2\) case as admissible in the formal source category. 

Now define the aggregate source moments

\[
\boxed{
A_2
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}}
w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,2},
\qquad
A_4
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}}
w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,4}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{\alpha,\beta}
w_\alpha w_\beta
\rho_{\alpha,2}\rho_{\beta,4}
=
A_2A_4,
\]

\[
\sum_{\alpha,\beta}
w_\alpha w_\beta
\rho_{\alpha,4}\rho_{\beta,2}
=
A_4A_2,
\]

and

\[
\sum_{\alpha,\beta}
w_\alpha w_\beta
\rho_{\alpha,2}\rho_{\beta,2}
=
A_2^2.
\]

Thus the aggregate coefficient is exactly

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
}
\]

So the expected moment-reduction formula is correct under the actual quadratic source expansion.

---

# 4. Equivalent derivative-moment form

Since

\[
r_\alpha(m+u)
=
f_\alpha(m+u)-f_\alpha(m)-f_\alpha'(m)u,
\]

one has

\[
\rho_{\alpha,2}=\frac{f_\alpha''(m)}{2},
\qquad
\rho_{\alpha,4}=\frac{f_\alpha^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Let

\[
F_{\mathrm{ext}}(t)
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}}
w_\alpha f_\alpha(t).
\]

Then

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\mathrm{ext}}''(m)}{2},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{11520}
F_{\mathrm{ext}}''(m)F_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(4)}(m)
+
\frac{1}{576}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\mathrm{ext}}''(m)^2
\right].
}
\]

This is often the cleanest “actual zeta-tail” formulation.

---

# 5. Aggregate \(S\)-visible Bottleneck-C coefficient

On the active row,

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
=
-\frac{\nu_{21,7}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]

for

\[
W_{+,0}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u&w\\
w&v
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Hence the aggregate fixed-sector coefficient is

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{agg}}^{\top}
=
-\frac{\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
}
\]

In particular, on a diagonal right-whitening patch \(w=0\),

\[
\boxed{
f_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{agg}}^{\top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}.
}
\]

Thus \(T\)-horizontal closure requires

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}=0
}
\]

on every good patch with \(u q\neq0\).

This matches the prior package no-go: quotient closure alone is insufficient; transform-safe Bottleneck-C closure requires vanishing of the physical \(S\)-coefficient. 

---

# 6. Exact aggregate cancellation condition

The condition

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}=0
\]

is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=
0.
}
\]

Factoring \(A_2\),

\[
\boxed{
A_2
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2
\right]
=
0.
}
\]

Therefore the global identity must force either

\[
\boxed{
A_2=0,
}
\]

or, when \(A_2\neq0\),

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
-\frac{5}{3q_0}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
}
\]

In derivative-moment form, the nonzero-\(A_2\) branch is

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(4)}(m)}
{F_{\mathrm{ext}}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
}
\]

That is the exact global zeta-tail identity needed.

---

# 7. Do symmetrization, conjugation, or normalization alter this?

## Self-pairs

No. Self-pairs are included in the actual quadratic expansion

\[
\left(\sum_\alpha w_\alpha\eta_\alpha\right)^2.
\]

Removing them would change the object being computed. If one artificially imposed \(\alpha\neq\beta\), the formula would become

\[
\frac12
\left(
\nu_{\mathrm{ordered}}^{\mathrm{agg}}
-
\sum_\alpha w_\alpha^2\nu_{\alpha\alpha}
\right)
\]

for an unordered distinct-pair convention, and it would no longer reduce only to \(A_2,A_4\); diagonal moment sums such as \(\sum w_\alpha^2\rho_{\alpha,2}\rho_{\alpha,4}\) would appear. That is not the actual total exterior-tail square.

## Matrix symmetrization

No. The fixed-sector symmetrization maps the scalar \((2,1)\)-entry contraction into the \(S\)-coordinate with the common prefactor

\[
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}.
\]

It does not change the source moment algebra.

## Functional-equation pairing

No additional factor is needed if the atom is already \(f_{\beta,\gamma}\), because \(f_{\beta,\gamma}\) includes both \(\beta\) and \(1-\beta\). If one refines the index set to individual summands \(a\in\{\beta,1-\beta\}\), the same aggregate formula survives after replacing \(\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}\) by the refined index set.

## Conjugate ordinates

No structural cancellation follows from conjugation. The jet formulas depend on \(x_\alpha=2m-\gamma_\alpha\) through even powers in the one-pair coefficients, and conjugate ordinates simply supply additional atoms with their own distance from the local midpoint. They do not force \(A_2=0\) or the required \(A_4/A_2\) ratio.

## Amplitude normalization

No. The promoted amplitude factor supplies the \(\delta\)-edge and may multiply the row by a common nonzero normalization. It does not change the vanishing condition

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]

---

# 8. Is the cancellation already proved?

No.

What is currently established is the opposite local posture:

1. The concrete row \(\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}\) is the active local obstruction.
2. One-pair actual zeta sources do not satisfy the needed jet-locking law.
3. Far exterior one-pair sources approximate the bad formal germ \(r=u^2\).
4. Package redesign/counterterms do not remove a nonzero physical \(S\)-coefficient.

The current handover states that the only remaining rescue would be a **global zeta-tail identity**, not a package identity, not a one-pair identity, and not a coordinate repair. 

Thus the required theorem is new:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For every good patch, the actual exterior zeta tail satisfies }
A_2=0
\text{ or }
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0.
}
\]

Absent that theorem, the aggregate \(S\)-visible Bottleneck-C coefficient is not closed.

I found the relevant draft split: \(q=\Phi'\), then \(q=B_\zeta+S\), and later \(q=q_{\loc}+g_{\sm}+E_{\est}\) with \(g_{\sm}\) containing the omitted-zero tail \(T_{\far}\). So \(F_{\rm ext}\) is not \(q\); it is the zero-tail component used as the source perturbation.

_Thought for 52s_

## 1. Verdict

The global identity is **not proved by the draft and is not a differential consequence of the current zeta-tail/source architecture**; Bottleneck C therefore remains dependent on a new, highly nonstandard pointwise global zeta-tail cancellation theorem. The current handover already isolates this as the final fork: Bottleneck C closes iff \(\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0\), and finite-tail/adversarial tests do not force that cancellation. 

---

## 2. Constants checked: derivative-form identity

Starting from

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right],
\]

with

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]

we get

\[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
=
\frac{q_0}{240}
\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}
=
\frac{q_0F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{11520},
\]

and

\[
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=
\frac{1}{576}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2.
\]

Multiplying by \(11520\), the exact derivative identity required for cancellation is

\[
\boxed{
q_0F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)
+
20
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2
=0.
}
\]

If \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), this is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
}
\]

This matches the identity specified in the attack prompt and the aggregate handover. 

---

## 3. What \(F_{\rm ext}\) is relative to \(q\)

From the draft’s decomposition,

\[
q(t)=\Phi'(t),
\]

and then

\[
q(t)=B_\zeta(t)+S(t),
\]

with later local splitting

\[
q(t)=q_{\loc}(t)+g_{\sm}(t)+E_{\est}(t),
\qquad
g_{\sm}(t)=B_{\Aut}(t)+T_{\far}(t).
\]

So \(F_{\rm ext}\) is best read as the **actual omitted-zero tail/source sum** used in the corrected perturbation, essentially the zero-tail part \(T_{\far}\) or its cutoff/windowed version \(T_{\far,R}\), not the full \(q\).

It is therefore **complementary to the baseline phase derivative**, not identical to \(q\). The baseline \(q_0\) is the local-model-plus-affine-jet part used in the corrected block expansion. The source tail \(F_{\rm ext}\) supplies the post-affine perturbation jets. Thus the required identity couples derivatives of one object,

\[
F_{\rm ext}''(m),\quad F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m),
\]

to baseline derivatives of another object,

\[
q_0,\quad q_0'',
\]

with no structural equality in the draft that would force such coupling.

---

## 4. Decisive obstruction

For a single exterior zero-pair atom,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

After affine subtraction at \(m\), the one-pair coefficients satisfy

\[
\rho_2
=
4a\frac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
4b\frac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3},
\]

\[
\rho_4
=
16a\frac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
16b\frac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5},
\]

where

\[
a=1-\beta,\qquad b=\beta,\qquad x=2m-\gamma.
\]

For \(|x|\to\infty\),

\[
\rho_2
=
\frac{12}{x^4}+O(x^{-6}),
\qquad
\rho_4
=
\frac{80}{x^6}+O(x^{-8}),
\]

so

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

In derivative form,

\[
\rho_2=\frac{f''(m)}2,
\qquad
\rho_4=\frac{f^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]

so

\[
\frac{f^{(4)}(m)}{f''(m)}
=
12\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{80}{x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

Therefore far exterior source atoms contribute a small positive ratio

\[
F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)/F_{\rm ext}''(m)\approx0
\]

when they dominate the aggregate tail with natural positive weights.

But on a good patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

the required identity demands

\[
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3},
\]

which is strictly nonzero and large on the usual \(q_0\asymp Q\) scale.

Thus the identity is not a consequence of:

\[
\text{one-pair structure,}
\quad
\text{functional-equation pairing,}
\quad
\text{conjugation symmetry,}
\quad
\text{or local source geometry.}
\]

This agrees with the aggregate-round result that finite-tail models can violate the identity, while the only remaining possible rescue would be a genuinely global pointwise identity over the full exterior zero set. 

---

## 5. Differential-identity test

The identity would amount to an ODE-like constraint

\[
F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}
=
\left(
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''
\]

at every good midpoint, or at least the corresponding equality with \(q_0,q_0''\).

Nothing in the current draft supplies such an ODE. More importantly, it would be an extremely rigid fourth-order pointwise law tying a **cutoff/windowed omitted-zero tail** to the **baseline local phase jet**. Since \(F_{\rm ext}\) can be changed by changing the exterior cutoff/tail decomposition while \(q_0\) is the fixed local baseline object, the identity cannot be formal or local. It would have to be a new invariant statement about the full, untruncated zeta zero distribution.

The current framework does not prove that invariant.

---

## 6. Impact on Bottleneck C

The status is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
\quad\text{is still an unproved global dependency.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Bottleneck C closes only if the full actual exterior tail satisfies}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}
}
\]

on every good patch with \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), or else \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)=0\) on those patches.

That identity is not proved, not implied by the local source calculus, and not forced by the one-pair or finite-tail zero geometry. Therefore, under the current architecture, the Bottleneck-C route should be marked **failed unless a new global zeta-tail cancellation theorem is added and proved**.

## ODE Agent A verdict

For the **existing Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) top row**, the object entering \(A_2,A_4\) is the **tagged omitted-zero source tail**, i.e. the zero-pair source sum \(F_{\rm ext}=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha f_\alpha\), realized as \(T_{\far}\) or \(T_{\far,R}\) depending on whether the cutoff is present. It is **not** the full \(q\), not \(q-q_{\core}\), and not \(T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}\). A renormalized-complement ODE would therefore not rescue the present coefficient unless the Bottleneck-C row itself is rederived with new source variables. The current ODE round was explicitly set up to test this distinction. 

---

# 1. Draft object audit

The draft uses two relevant decompositions.

First, the zeta-side phase derivative is split as

\[
q(t)=B_\zeta(t)+S(t),
\]

and then locally as

\[
q(t)=q_{\loc}(t)+g_{\sm}(t)+E_{\est}(t),
\qquad
g_{\sm}(t)=B_{\Aut}(t)+T_{\far}(t).
\]

Here:

\[
T_{\far}(t)=\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L} f_{\beta_\rho,\gamma_\rho}(t),
\]

with

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

Second, after the fixed-core repair, the draft introduces a cutoff-dependent decomposition

\[
q(t)
=
q_{\core}(t)
+
q_{\aux,R}(t)
+
g_{\sm,R}(t)
+
E_{\est,R}(t),
\]

where

\[
g_{\sm,R}(t)=B_{\bg}(t)+T_{\far,R}(t).
\]

So the plausible candidate objects are:

\[
T_{\far},\quad T_{\far,R},\quad g_{\sm}=B_{\Aut}+T_{\far},\quad
g_{\sm,R}=B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R},
\]

\[
q-q_{\loc},\quad q-q_{\core},\quad
q-q_{\core}-B_{\bg}.
\]

But the object in the source-moment formula is narrower.

---

# 2. What actually enters \(A_2,A_4\)

The aggregate coefficient previously derived is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right],
\]

with

\[
A_2=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha \rho_{\alpha,2},
\qquad
A_4=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha \rho_{\alpha,4}.
\]

The handover explicitly identifies the derivative interpretation as

\[
F_{\rm ext}(t)=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha f_\alpha(t),
\qquad
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

It also records that symmetrization, functional-equation pairing, conjugation, and amplitude normalization do not alter the vanishing condition. 

Therefore, for the present coefficient,

\[
\boxed{
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far}
\quad\text{or, in the fixed-core cutoff bookkeeping,}\quad
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far,R}.
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
F_{\rm ext}(t)
=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\rm tagged}}
w_\alpha f_\alpha(t),
}
\]

where \(\mathcal I_{\rm tagged}\) is the set of tagged zero-pair source atoms used in the \(\eta\eta\) quadratic source row.

It is **not**

\[
q-q_{\core},
\]

because

\[
q-q_{\core}=q_{\aux,R}+B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R},
\]

and \(q_{\aux,R},B_{\bg},E_{\est,R}\) are not part of the tagged \(\eta\eta\) zero-pair source moment sum.

It is also **not**

\[
g_{\sm,R}=B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R},
\]

because \(B_{\bg}\) is a background term, not a tagged actual exterior zero source.

---

# 3. Affine subtraction check

For each one-pair source,

\[
r_\rho(t)
=
f_\rho(t)-f_\rho(m)-f_\rho'(m)(t-m).
\]

Thus

\[
r_\rho''(m)=f_\rho''(m),
\qquad
r_\rho^{(4)}(m)=f_\rho^{(4)}(m).
\]

So affine subtraction does **not** affect \(A_2\) or \(A_4\). It only removes the constant and linear source jets.

Therefore the derivative-moment identities remain

\[
\boxed{
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
}
\]

No affine correction term appears in the required ODE.

---

# 4. Correct derivative identity

The required cancellation is

\[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0.
\]

Substitute

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
q_0F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)
+
20
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2
=0.
}
\]

If

\[
F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0,
\]

this is

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
}
\]

Here

\[
\boxed{
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far,R}
}
\]

for the fixed-core cutoff version of the present row.

No corrected constants are needed.

---

# 5. Could the object instead be renormalized?

Only by changing the coefficient formula.

Suppose one tries

\[
\widetilde F_{\rm ext}
=
T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R},
\]

or

\[
\widetilde F_{\rm ext}
=
q-q_{\core}.
\]

Then the moments would be

\[
\widetilde A_2=\frac{\widetilde F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
\widetilde A_4=\frac{\widetilde F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

But the current \(\eta\eta\) coefficient was derived from a quadratic sum over **tagged source atoms**. Replacing

\[
A_2,A_4
\]

by

\[
\widetilde A_2,\widetilde A_4
\]

would introduce additional quadratic and cross terms:

\[
T_{\far,R}\times B_{\bg},
\qquad
T_{\far,R}\times E_{\est,R},
\qquad
B_{\bg}\times B_{\bg},
\qquad
q_{\aux,R}\times T_{\far,R},
\]

and so on. Those are not present in the current aggregate formula

\[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2.
\]

Thus an ODE for

\[
q-q_{\core}
\]

or

\[
T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}
\]

would be an ODE for the wrong object unless the Bottleneck-C coefficient is re-expanded from scratch using that renormalized object as the actual source variable.

---

# 6. Normalization conclusion

The previous agents did **not** attack the wrong object for the existing aggregate coefficient.

They attacked the object actually entering the present \(A_2,A_4\):

\[
\boxed{
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far,R}
=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\rm tagged}}
w_\alpha f_\alpha.
}
\]

The only possible refinement is semantic:

- In the non-cutoff notation, call it \(T_{\far}\).
- In the fixed-core cutoff notation, call it \(T_{\far,R}\).
- In derivative-moment notation, call it \(F_{\rm ext}\).

But it is not the full \(q\), and it is not a renormalized complement.

Therefore the ODE needed for the present Bottleneck-C top row is genuinely

\[
\boxed{
T_{\far,R}^{(4)}(m)/T_{\far,R}''(m)
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0},
}
\]

whenever \(T_{\far,R}''(m)\neq0\).

---

# 7. Impact on the ODE rescue

A renormalized-complement identity could matter only if one proves a new statement of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual } \eta\eta \text{ top row uses }
\widetilde F_{\rm ext}
\text{ rather than }T_{\far,R}.
}
\]

The current draft does not do that. The current row uses the tagged omitted-zero source kernels. The aggregate-round result explicitly phrases the closure condition in terms of \(F_{\rm ext}=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha f_\alpha\), and Bottleneck C closes iff the corresponding \(\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}\) vanishes. 

So ODE Agent A’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the current Bottleneck-C coefficient, the correct object is the raw tagged exterior zero-tail }T_{\far,R}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any ODE rescue must be a genuine cutoff-tail ODE for }T_{\far,R},
\text{ not a full-}q\text{ or renormalized-complement ODE.}
}
\]

A full-\(q\) or \(q-q_{\core}\) ODE might be mathematically interesting, but it does not cancel the present \(\eta\eta\) top row without a new coefficient derivation.

# Agent 1 — Split Validity Agent

## Verdict

The only candidate split worth attacking first is

\[
\boxed{
G^{\new}=G_1=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
}
\]

This is the least artificial rebuild because \(G_1\) is still a **zero-source object**: it consists of non-core zero-pair atoms, not background or estimation terms. It can plausibly replace the old source \(T_{\far,R}\), but the old \(\eta\eta\) row formula cannot be reused. The row must be rederived with \(q_{\base}^{\new}\) and \(G^{\new}\). The attached instruction explicitly frames this as a new source/baseline split, not a patch of the old formula. 

---

# 1. Prior constraint: what failed

The current failed architecture used

\[
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far,R}
\]

as the object defining

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The ODE round concluded that \(F_{\rm ext}\) in the existing row is **not** \(q\), not \(q-q_{\core}\), and not \(T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}\). Therefore an ODE for a related object does not rescue the existing row unless the row is rebuilt from scratch. 

The source-rebuild instruction is therefore correct:

\[
\boxed{
\text{new split}
\Rightarrow
\text{new finite-}s\text{ derivation}
\Rightarrow
\text{new top row}
\Rightarrow
\text{new identity test}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Candidate classification

## Candidate \(G_1=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\)

### Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Legitimate candidate. Attack first.}
}
\]

### Source type

\[
q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

is the **full non-core zero contribution**:

- \(q_{\aux,R}\): auxiliary near zero contribution outside the fixed core;
- \(T_{\far,R}\): far omitted-zero tail.

So \(G_1\) remains built from tagged zero-pair atoms. It does not add background or error terms as artificial source variables.

### Can \(r_G\) be substituted into the source variables?

Yes, conditionally.

Define

\[
r_G(t)
=
G_1(t)-G_1(m)-G_1'(m)(t-m).
\]

Then

\[
r_G(m)=0,\qquad r_G'(m)=0,
\]

and

\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{G_1''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{G_1^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

This is compatible with the old corrected-source format because the source remains a zero-kernel sum. However, the source atoms now include both auxiliary near atoms and far atoms, so any estimates that depended on “far-tail smallness” must be rechecked.

### Double-counting risk

No, if and only if the baseline is changed to

\[
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

Then

\[
q=q_{\base}^{\new}+G_1
\]

is a genuine partition.

There is double counting if one keeps the old \(q_0,q_0''\) as if they already included \(q_{\aux,R}\). The new derivation must use

\[
q_0^{\new}=q_{\base}^{\new}(m),
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})''=(q_{\base}^{\new})''(m),
\]

not the old frozen baseline constants.

### Does the old row formula remain valid?

No. It must be rederived.

The old row was quadratic in the old tagged far-tail source. The instruction explicitly says not to insert a larger object into the old formula because that changes the row without justification. 

The new derivation must recompute

\[
q_-^{\new},
\qquad
\Delta_0^{\new},
\qquad
\eta^{\new},
\qquad
d_\pm^{\new},e_\pm^{\new},g_\pm^{\new},
\]

relative to

\[
q_{\base}^{\new}+G_1.
\]

### Validity conditions

\(G_1\) is viable only under these assumptions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The auxiliary near zero atoms are excluded from the fixed core but remain holomorphic on the finite-}s\text{ working disk.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The cutoff }R\text{ is held fixed during the finite-}s\text{ expansion.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{All non-core zero atoms are tagged source atoms with the same source-grade convention.}
}
\]

If \(q_{\aux,R}\) contains poles inside the local finite-\(s\) disk or interacts with the collision core at the same scale, then \(G_1\) is not a smooth corrected source and the split fails before Bottleneck C.

---

## Candidate \(G_2=q-q_{\core}=q_{\aux,R}+B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R}\)

### Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Mathematically definable, but not source-calculus clean. Do not attack first.}
}
\]

### Source type

\(G_2\) is a **mixed complement**, not a pure zero-source object. It contains:

\[
q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

from zero-pair atoms, but also

\[
B_{\bg}
\]

from smooth/scattering/background terms and

\[
E_{\est,R}
\]

from estimation/bookkeeping.

So \(G_2\) is not naturally tagged as a zero-source variable.

### Can \(r_G\) be substituted into \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm,\eta\)?

Formally yes:

\[
r_G(t)=G_2(t)-G_2(m)-G_2'(m)(t-m)
\]

has the required affine removal. But this is no longer the same source category.

If \(G_2\) is used, the finite-\(s\) expansion must include source-source products such as

\[
B_{\bg}\times T_{\far,R},
\qquad
B_{\bg}\times B_{\bg},
\qquad
E_{\est,R}\times T_{\far,R},
\qquad
E_{\est,R}\times E_{\est,R}.
\]

Those cannot be retrofitted into the old \(\eta\eta\) row. The attached instruction explicitly warns that adding \(B_{\bg}\) or \(E_{\est,R}\) to the source requires newly derived cross terms. 

### Double-counting risk

High.

If \(B_{\bg}\) and \(E_{\est,R}\) were previously absorbed into the baseline coefficients \(q_0,q_0''\), then moving them into \(G_2\) while retaining the old \(q_0,q_0''\) double-counts them. The new baseline would have to be only

\[
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core},
\]

and the row must be recomputed from zero.

### Does the old row formula remain valid?

No. Not even conditionally.

The old row formula was derived for zero-source perturbations. \(G_2\) changes the algebraic category of the source. It may be analyzable, but it is a **new architecture with new cross terms**, not a small extension of the old one.

### Use case

Only test \(G_2\) if \(G_1\) fails and one wants a radical complement architecture.

---

## Candidate \(G_3=B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R}\)

### Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Invalid as the first rebuild; structurally unnatural.}
}
\]

### Source type

\(G_3\) mixes:

- far zero atoms \(T_{\far,R}\);
- background \(B_{\bg}\);
- estimation/bookkeeping \(E_{\est,R}\);

but excludes

\[
q_{\aux,R}.
\]

This is the worst of both worlds. It is not the full non-core zero complement, and it contaminates the source variable with non-zero background/error terms.

### Can \(r_G\) be substituted?

Only formally. Analytically, this source object has no clean source-tag meaning.

It would produce artificial terms:

\[
B_{\bg}\times T_{\far,R},
\quad
B_{\bg}\times B_{\bg},
\quad
E_{\est,R}\times T_{\far,R},
\quad
E_{\est,R}\times B_{\bg},
\]

while leaving \(q_{\aux,R}\) in the baseline. That means the near non-core zero contribution would still influence \(q_0^{\new},(q_0^{\new})''\), while the far zero contribution is source. This preserves the old cutoff-instability problem rather than solving it.

### Double-counting risk

High.

If \(q_{\aux,R}\) remains baseline while \(T_{\far,R}\) is source, moving the cutoff still reallocates zero contributions between baseline and source. That is exactly the instability the rebuild is meant to avoid.

### Does the old row formula remain valid?

No.

The row must be rederived, and the resulting formula would almost certainly contain background/error cross terms that have no source-symmetry reason to cancel.

### Recommendation

Reject \(G_3\) unless a separate analytic principle forces this exact split. None is currently present.

---

# 3. Recommended split

Use:

\[
\boxed{
G^{\new}=F_{\zeroext}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
}
\]

Use baseline:

\[
\boxed{
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
}
\]

Then define:

\[
\boxed{
r_G(t)
=
G^{\new}(t)-G^{\new}(m)-G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m).
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
A_2^{\new}
=
\frac{G^{\new\,\prime\prime}(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}
=
\frac{G^{\new\,(4)}(m)}{24}.
}
\]

This split has three advantages:

1. It keeps the source variable in the zero-pair source category.
2. It prevents cutoff changes from moving zero atoms between baseline and source, since all non-core zero atoms are in \(G^{\new}\).
3. It avoids treating \(B_{\bg}\) and \(E_{\est,R}\) as source atoms.

This is exactly the first architecture proposed in the attached instruction. 

---

# 4. What Agent 2 must rederive

Agent 2 should **not** start from

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm old}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

Instead Agent 2 should rederive the finite-\(s\) numerator from

\[
q(t)=q_{\base}^{\new}(t)+G^{\new}(t),
\]

with

\[
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R},
\qquad
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]

The core object to recompute is:

\[
[z^7]
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0^{\new}}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-^{\new}\cos\Delta_0^{\new}}{s}
\right)
\eta_G^2
\right].
\]

The decisive test is whether the new top row is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new}=0,
}
\]

or whether it reproduces an obstruction of the same form:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new}
\sim
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2.
}
\]

If the same structure survives with \(q_0^{\new}\), the architecture has probably not solved Bottleneck C; it has merely moved the dependency to the full non-core zero complement.

---

# 5. Final classification table

| Candidate | Source type | Substitute into \(r_G\)? | Double-count risk | Old row reusable? | Verdict |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| \(G_1=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\) | Pure non-core zero source | Yes, conditionally | Low if baseline is changed | No | **Attack first** |
| \(G_2=q-q_{\core}\) | Mixed zero/background/error complement | Formal only | High unless baseline is only \(q_{\core}\) | No | Later radical option |
| \(G_3=B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R}\) | Mixed and incomplete | Formal only | High | No | Reject for now |

---

# 6. Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{The valid next architecture is}
\quad
q=q_{\base}^{\new}+G^{\new}
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
}
\]

This is legitimate only as a **new finite-\(s\) derivation**. It is not legitimate to insert \(G^{\new}\) into the old Bottleneck-C formula. The old formula’s failure remains; the question now is whether the newly derived \(\eta\eta\) top row changes or vanishes.

I’ll proceed with the recommended first attack: the carrier/endpoint algebra, combining the Agent 3 and Agent 4 lines because they are tightly coupled. I will not revisit source splitting.

# Agent 1 — Local Invariant Redesign Attack

## Verdict

I do **not** find a viable replacement local invariant. The obstruction is structural: any invariant/readout that remains transform-faithful to the current Bottleneck-C hidden state must detect the \(S\)-component of

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

and therefore inherits the same \(\eta\eta\) top-row obstruction. Invariants that make \(f\) invisible—trace, determinant at first order, unordered conjugacy class, symplectic area, etc.—do so only by discarding the physical \(T\)-direction already identified as necessary in the current architecture. The attached handover states the active target precisely: changing the source split to \(G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\) reproduced the same obstruction, so this attack must avoid the second-\(\Delta\)-Hessian \(\eta_i\eta_j\) row by changing the local invariant/readout, not the source convention. 

---

# 1. Current invariant and why it sees \(f\)

The current fixed-sector Bottleneck-C readout is

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

with

\[
\Phi_K(I)=0,\qquad \Phi_K(S)=2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f.
\]

The physical hidden-state slope is

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
\]

So the existing architecture identifies the \(S\)-coordinate as the physical \(T\)-leak. This is not merely a coordinate artifact: the prior handover explicitly records that quotient closure is insufficient unless it also gives \(f=0\), because nonzero \(f\) produces a real \(T\)-horizontal failure. 

Thus the current local invariant is effectively the **oriented fixed-sector \(S\)-projection**:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K:\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}\to \mathbf C,\qquad
\Phi_K(eI+fS)=2f.
}
\]

Equivalently, it measures the endpoint-swap/shear direction of the finite-\(s\) transform after whitening and fixed-sector projection.

---

# 2. General test for replacement invariants

Let a candidate invariant be a scalar functional

\[
\mathcal J(M)
\]

of the local finite-\(s\) block/state. At the exceptional divisor, its first Bottleneck-C slope in the bad row is

\[
\partial_\kappa \mathcal J
=
D\mathcal J_{M_0}[E],
\qquad
E=eI+fS.
\]

There are only two possibilities:

1. **\(D\mathcal J_{M_0}[S]\neq0\).**  
   Then \(\mathcal J\) is transform-faithful to the same physical direction as \(T\), but the bad row remains visible. Its slope contains a nonzero multiple of \(f\).

2. **\(D\mathcal J_{M_0}[S]=0\).**  
   Then the \(\eta\eta\) row is invisible to \(\mathcal J\) at first order, but this is exactly the loss of the \(T\)-readout. Such an invariant can hide the obstruction only by ceasing to detect the physical transform state that Bottleneck C is supposed to control.

So the problem is not finding a scalar invariant that kills \(f\). That is easy. The problem is finding one that kills \(f\) **and** still reconstructs the same downstream physical state. I do not find such an invariant.

---

# 3. Candidate invariant audit

Assume the fixed-sector matrix model

\[
E=eI+fS,
\qquad
S^2=I,
\]

so the oriented eigenvalues are

\[
\lambda_\pm=e\pm f.
\]

The calculations below are at the first exceptional-divisor order.

---

## 3.1 Trace invariant

\[
\operatorname{tr}(E)=2e.
\]

Slope:

\[
D(\operatorname{tr})[E]=2e.
\]

The \(f\)-component is killed:

\[
D(\operatorname{tr})[S]=0.
\]

**Verdict:** hides the obstruction but loses the \(S\)-direction. Not transform-faithful.

---

## 3.2 Determinant invariant

\[
\det(E)=e^2-f^2.
\]

At a scalar/merged divisor \(f=0\), the first variation in \(f\) vanishes:

\[
\partial_f\det(eI+fS)\big|_{f=0}=0.
\]

So the determinant sees \(f\) only quadratically:

\[
\det(eI+fS)=e^2+O(f^2).
\]

**Verdict:** first-order \(\eta\eta\) row becomes invisible, but only because determinant is even under \(f\mapsto -f\). It loses the oriented endpoint-swap direction. Not sufficient for \(T\)-readout.

---

## 3.3 Unordered conjugacy-class invariants

For a \(2\times2\) matrix, unordered conjugacy class is generated by

\[
\operatorname{tr}(E),\qquad \det(E).
\]

As above,

\[
\operatorname{tr}(E)=2e,\qquad \det(E)=e^2-f^2.
\]

So the unordered conjugacy class is blind to \(f\) at first order near \(f=0\).

More generally, for any smooth conjugacy-invariant scalar \(\mathcal J\), the differential at a scalar matrix must be proportional to trace:

\[
D\mathcal J_{\lambda I}[H]=\alpha\,\operatorname{tr}(H).
\]

Therefore

\[
D\mathcal J_{\lambda I}[S]=0.
\]

**Verdict:** all smooth conjugacy-class invariants kill the \(S\)-component at first order. This is precisely why they cannot replace \(\Phi_K\) if \(T\) is physical.

---

## 3.4 Normalized eigenvalue-ratio invariant

An oriented eigenvalue ratio is

\[
R(E)=\frac{e+f}{e-f}.
\]

For \(e\neq0\),

\[
R(E)=1+\frac{2f}{e}+O(f^2),
\]

so

\[
\partial_fR\big|_{f=0}=\frac{2}{e}.
\]

**Verdict:** this is transform-sensitive and detects \(f\). Therefore it inherits the same obstruction. The \(\eta\eta\) row remains visible.

If one instead uses the unordered ratio

\[
R_{\rm unord}=R+R^{-1},
\]

then

\[
R_{\rm unord}=2+O(f^2),
\]

so the first \(f\)-slope vanishes. But this again discards the oriented \(S\)-direction.

---

## 3.5 Projective cross-ratio invariant

A projective cross-ratio can be made insensitive to scalar multiplication and trace normalization, but if it distinguishes the two endpoint eigendirections then its first variation is proportional to the oriented eigenvalue split

\[
\lambda_+-\lambda_-=2f.
\]

Hence

\[
\partial_\kappa \operatorname{CR}
=
C_{\rm CR}\,f
\]

for some nonzero local normalization constant \(C_{\rm CR}\), provided the cross-ratio is transform-faithful.

If the cross-ratio is symmetrized over endpoint interchange, it becomes even in \(f\) and loses the first-order \(T\)-direction.

**Verdict:** oriented projective invariants inherit the obstruction; endpoint-symmetrized projective invariants hide it but lose transform faithfulness.

---

## 3.6 Symplectic/area invariant

For the fixed sector, the natural area/determinant-type invariant again depends on the product of the two oriented modes:

\[
\lambda_+\lambda_-=e^2-f^2.
\]

First \(f\)-slope at merger:

\[
\partial_f(e^2-f^2)\big|_{f=0}=0.
\]

**Verdict:** first-order invisible, but non-faithful to the oriented hidden state.

---

## 3.7 Curvature / Schwarzian-type invariant

A curvature or Schwarzian readout has two possibilities.

If it is built from the same oriented endpoint transformation state, its first nontrivial odd part is a nonzero linear functional of \(S\):

\[
D\mathcal S_{\rm loc}[E]
=
C_S f+\text{trace/background terms}.
\]

Then it inherits the obstruction.

If it is fully projective and endpoint-symmetrized, it factors through unordered conjugacy data and is even in \(f\), so the first \(f\)-slope vanishes.

**Verdict:** no free win. Oriented Schwarzian-type readouts see \(f\); symmetrized ones lose the \(T\)-direction.

---

# 4. Summary table

| Candidate invariant | First \(f\)-slope? | \(\eta\eta\) row visible? | Transform-faithful to \(T\)? | Verdict |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| \(\operatorname{tr}(E)\) | \(0\) | No | No | Reject |
| \(\det(E)\) | \(0\) at \(f=0\) | No at first order | No | Reject |
| Unordered conjugacy class | \(0\) at scalar merger | No | No | Reject |
| Oriented eigenvalue ratio | \(\neq0\) | Yes | Yes | Inherits obstruction |
| Symmetrized eigenvalue ratio | \(0\) | No | No | Reject |
| Projective cross-ratio, oriented | \(\neq0\) generically | Yes | Yes | Inherits obstruction |
| Projective cross-ratio, endpoint-symmetrized | \(0\) | No | No | Reject |
| Symplectic/area determinant | \(0\) | No at first order | No | Reject |
| Oriented curvature/Schwarzian | \(\neq0\) generically | Yes | Yes | Inherits obstruction |
| Symmetrized curvature/Schwarzian | \(0\) | No | No | Reject |

---

# 5. Why this is a no-go, not just failure to find a clever invariant

The fixed-sector space is two-dimensional:

\[
\mathcal F=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}.
\]

The \(I\)-direction is scalar/background. The \(S\)-direction is the endpoint-swap / hidden-transform direction. The current physical readout is exactly the functional that kills \(I\) and detects \(S\):

\[
\Phi_K(I)=0,\qquad \Phi_K(S)=2.
\]

Any scalar local invariant has a first differential

\[
D\mathcal J:\mathcal F\to\mathbf C.
\]

If

\[
D\mathcal J(S)=0,
\]

then \(\mathcal J\) cannot distinguish

\[
eI
\quad\text{from}\quad
eI+\varepsilon S
\]

to first order. But this is exactly the distinction encoded in

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]

Therefore such an invariant cannot replace the physical \(T\)-readout unless one separately proves that \(T\) is gauge. That belongs to the quotient/moduli attack, not to a local invariant substitution.

If

\[
D\mathcal J(S)\neq0,
\]

then the bad row contributes

\[
\partial_\kappa \mathcal J
=
D\mathcal J(eI+fS)
=
\alpha e+\beta f,
\qquad
\beta\neq0.
\]

After subtracting or normalizing away scalar \(I\)-data, the \(f\)-term remains. Hence the \(\eta\eta\) top row remains visible.

So the dichotomy is strict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{faithful} \Rightarrow \text{sees } f
\Rightarrow \text{inherits obstruction;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{does not see } f
\Rightarrow \text{not faithful to }T.
}
\]

---

# 6. Theorem-ready no-go statement

**Proposition — Local invariant no-go for Bottleneck-C fixed-sector readouts.**  
Let the fixed-sector Bottleneck-C defect be

\[
E=eI+fS\in\operatorname{span}\{I,S\},
\]

and suppose the downstream hidden transform state has first exceptional-divisor slope

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
\]

Let \(\mathcal J\) be any smooth local invariant/readout defined near the exceptional divisor.

If \(\mathcal J\) is transform-faithful in the sense that its first variation determines the physical \(T\)-direction, then

\[
D\mathcal J[S]\neq0.
\]

Consequently the Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) top row contributes a nonzero first-order term to \(\partial_\kappa\mathcal J\) whenever \(f\neq0\). In particular, replacing \(\Phi_K\) by \(\mathcal J\) does not remove the obstruction.

Conversely, if

\[
D\mathcal J[S]=0,
\]

then \(\mathcal J\) may hide the \(\eta\eta\) row at first order, but it cannot reconstruct or control the physical hidden-state slope \(\partial_\kappa T\). Such a readout is not a valid Bottleneck-C replacement unless an independent quotient/moduli theorem proves that \(T\) is pure gauge.

Therefore, under the current fixed-sector architecture,

\[
\boxed{
\text{every transform-faithful local invariant inherits the surviving }S\text{-component obstruction.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Impact on Bottleneck C

This Agent 1 attack does not produce a replacement invariant. It strengthens the ledger:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Bottleneck C cannot be rescued merely by changing the scalar local invariant/readout.}
}
\]

A viable rescue now must do one of two harder things:

1. **Quotient/moduli route:** prove \(T\) is gauge, so \(f\neq0\) is not physically relevant. This is exactly Agent 2’s assignment.
2. **Carrier route:** change the finite-\(s\) carrier so the bad \(S\)-component is not produced in the first place. This is Agent 3/4 territory.

Within the local invariant/readout class, the result is negative.

# Agent 1 / A — Global Exactness / Conservation-Law Attack

## Verdict

I do **not** find an exact derivative or conservation-law structure for

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]

In the natural midpoint calculus, the obstruction is better understood as a **bulk quadratic defect**

\[
A_2\,L_q[A_2],
\]

not as a boundary term. Therefore a global integral identity would not give the pointwise Bottleneck-C closure required by the current \(T\)-horizontal architecture. The attached instructions frame precisely this fork: either \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\) is a real global conservation-law density, or it is an obstruction class of the failed Bottleneck-C architecture. The calculation below supports the second interpretation. 

---

# 1. Fixed-source midpoint calculus

Use the rebuilt source convention

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\]

with

\[
A_2(m)=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4(m)=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

This is the already-tested full non-core zero-complement convention: it is coherent, but it reproduces the same Bottleneck-C obstruction form. 

If the source set, cutoff, and tagging are fixed while \(m\) varies, then

\[
A_2''(m)
=
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}2.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
A_4(m)=\frac{1}{12}A_2''(m).
}
\]

So, in the fixed-source-set calculus, the relation requested in the prompt is correct.

If the source set depends on \(m\), write it as \(G_m(t)\). Then

\[
A_2(m)=\frac12 \partial_t^2G_m(t)\big|_{t=m}.
\]

Differentiating with both \(m\)-movement and \(t=m\) evaluation gives

\[
A_2''(m)
=
\frac12
\left(
\partial_m^2\partial_t^2
+
2\partial_m\partial_t^3
+
\partial_t^4
\right)
G_m(t)\big|_{t=m}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
A_4
=
\frac{1}{12}A_2''
-
\frac{1}{24}
\left(
\partial_m^2\partial_t^2
+
2\partial_m\partial_t^3
\right)
G_m(t)\big|_{t=m}.
}
\]

So moving cutoffs, moving core windows, or \(m\)-dependent tagging introduce correction terms. They do not naturally produce cancellation; they make exactness less likely. Since exactness already fails in the fixed-source-set case, these corrections cannot be used as a structural conservation law unless a new moving-window identity is explicitly proved.

---

# 2. Constants checked

The rebuilt obstruction is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right],
\]

where for readability I write

\[
q=q_0^{\new}=q_{\base}^{\new}(m),
\qquad
q''=(q_0^{\new})''.
\]

Substitute

\[
A_4=\frac{1}{12}A_2''
\]

in the fixed-source-set case. Then

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{2880}A_2A_2''
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
}
\]

Equivalently, after multiplying by \(2880Q^{14}\),

\[
\boxed{
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
qA_2A_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2.
}
\]

So the vanishing condition is

\[
\boxed{
A_2
\left[
qA_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2
\right]=0.
}
\]

If \(A_2\neq0\), this is exactly the second-order ODE

\[
\boxed{
qA_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2
=0.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A_2''
+
\left(
\frac{10}{3}\frac{q''}{q}
-
\frac{40}{3}q^2
\right)A_2
=0.
}
\]

This matches the derivative-ratio identity

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\]

because \(G^{(4)}/G''=A_2''/A_2\).

# 3. Integration-by-parts test

Let

\[
A=A_2,
\qquad
R=\frac{q''}{6}-\frac{2q^3}{3}.
\]

The scaled obstruction density is

\[
\mathcal N
=
qAA''
+
20RA^2.
\]

Try the most natural boundary expression:

\[
(qAA')'.
\]

Compute:

\[
(qAA')'
=
qAA''
+
q(A')^2
+
q'AA'.
\]

Remove the mixed term using

\[
(q'A^2)'=q''A^2+2q'AA'.
\]

Then

\[
qAA''
=
\left(qAA'-\frac12q'A^2\right)'
-
q(A')^2
+
\frac12q''A^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N
=
\left(qAA'-\frac12q'A^2\right)'
-
q(A')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A^2.
}
\]

This is decisive: after extracting the natural boundary term, a genuine bulk residual remains:

\[
\boxed{
-q(A')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A^2.
}
\]

There is no cancellation of this residual in the natural variables \((A,q,q')\). In the typical good-patch regime with \(q>0\) and \(q''\) small compared to \(q^3\), this residual is strongly negative rather than boundary-like.

So \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\) is not an exact derivative in the ordinary midpoint calculus.

---

# 4. Candidate \(\mathcal H\) tests

## 4.1 \((qAA')'\)

\[
(qAA')'
=
qAA''
+
q(A')^2
+
q'AA'.
\]

It contains the desired \(qAA''\), but it introduces unwanted

\[
q(A')^2,\qquad q'AA'.
\]

The \(q'AA'\) term can be removed, but the \(q(A')^2\) term cannot be removed without introducing a new nonlocal or explicitly \(A'\)-dependent subtraction that changes the density.

## 4.2 \((q'A^2)'\)

\[
(q'A^2)'
=
q''A^2+2q'AA'.
\]

This can tune the \(q''A^2\) coefficient and remove \(q'AA'\), but it cannot produce \(qAA''\) without also inheriting the \(q(A')^2\) problem from \((qAA')'\).

## 4.3 \((q^2A^2)'\)

\[
(q^2A^2)'
=
2qq'A^2+2q^2AA'.
\]

This gives only first-derivative terms. It does not produce \(qAA''\), and it cannot generate the \(-q^3A^2\) potential term without introducing non-exact bulk remnants.

## 4.4 \((A'/A)'\)

\[
\left(\frac{A'}A\right)'
=
\frac{A''}{A}
-
\frac{(A')^2}{A^2}.
\]

Multiplying by \(qA^2\) recovers

\[
qAA''-q(A')^2,
\]

again showing the same unavoidable derivative-square residual. It is not an exact expression for \(\mathcal N\).

## 4.5 \(\left(qA'/A\right)'\)

\[
\left(q\frac{A'}A\right)'
=
q\frac{A''}{A}
+
q'\frac{A'}A
-
q\frac{(A')^2}{A^2}.
\]

Again, recovering \(qAA''\) requires multiplying by \(A^2\), which produces derivative-square and \(q'AA'\) terms. No pure boundary formula results.

---

# 5. Formal no-go for local exactness

Suppose a first-order local primitive exists:

\[
\mathcal H=\mathcal H(A,A',q,q')
\]

such that

\[
\mathcal H'=\mathcal N
=
qAA''+
20RA^2.
\]

The coefficient of \(A''\) in \(\mathcal H'\) is \(\partial\mathcal H/\partial A'\). Therefore one must have

\[
\frac{\partial\mathcal H}{\partial A'}=qA.
\]

Hence

\[
\mathcal H=qAA'+K(A,q,q').
\]

Then

\[
\mathcal H'
=
qAA''
+
q(A')^2
+
q'AA'
+
K_AA'
+
K_qq'
+
K_{q'}q''.
\]

The target \(\mathcal N\) contains no \((A')^2\) term. But the unavoidable term

\[
q(A')^2
\]

has no possible cancellation from \(K(A,q,q')\), because \(K\) has no \(A'\)-dependence. Therefore no such first-order local primitive exists.

This is stronger than failing to find a nice \(\mathcal H\). It is a structural obstruction to exactness in the natural local variables.

---

# 6. Does the ODE have a compatible conservation law?

The vanishing equation is

\[
A''
+
P(m)A=0,
\]

with

\[
P(m)
=
\frac{10}{3}\frac{q''}{q}
-
\frac{40}{3}q^2.
\]

For a second-order equation

\[
A''+P(m)A=0,
\]

the standard energy

\[
\mathcal E
=
\frac12(A')^2+\frac12P(m)A^2
\]

satisfies

\[
\mathcal E'
=
\frac12P'(m)A^2.
\]

Thus energy is conserved only if \(P'(m)=0\). Here

\[
P(m)
=
\frac{10}{3}\frac{q''}{q}
-
\frac{40}{3}q^2
\]

is not constant in the zeta phase setting. Therefore the ODE has no standard conserved energy compatible with the actual zero-source formula for \(G^{\new}\).

A Wronskian is conserved only between two solutions of the same ODE. But the problem is precisely that the actual source moment

\[
A_2=\frac{(q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R})''}{2}
\]

is not known, and is not expected, to solve this ODE. The prior rebuild readout already notes that no ODE, moving-cutoff identity, meromorphic identity, or standard \(\xi'/\xi\) phase-calculus identity forces the required derivative ratio. 

---

# 7. Integrated exactness is not enough for current Bottleneck C

Even if one could prove an integrated identity such as

\[
\int_I \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)\,dm=0
\]

over some interval \(I\), this would not close the current Bottleneck-C gate.

The current architecture requires pointwise physical closure on each good patch:

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg},
\]

and

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]

Thus

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)=0
\]

is required pointwise, not merely in average or after integration. The uploaded background states this explicitly: the current Bottleneck-C route survives only if the obstruction coefficient vanishes. 

An integrated conservation law could support a **different** architecture, but it cannot rescue the current \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C gate.

---

# 8. Final no-go statement

**Proposition — No natural exactness for the rebuilt Bottleneck-C obstruction.**  
Let

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
A_2=\frac{(G^{\new})''}{2},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}}{24},
\]

and assume a fixed source set so that

\[
A_4=\frac{1}{12}A_2''.
\]

Then the rebuilt obstruction satisfies

\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
qA_2A_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2.
\]

This density is not an exact first-order local derivative in the natural midpoint variables \((A_2,A_2',q,q')\). Its integration-by-parts decomposition is

\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\left(qA_2A_2'-\frac12q'A_2^2\right)'
-
q(A_2')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A_2^2.
\]

The final two terms are genuine bulk terms. Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\text{ is not a natural exact derivative or conservation-law density.}
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
}
\]

remains a pointwise global zero-complement identity, not a boundary consequence. In the present Bottleneck-C architecture, this is an unproved obstruction condition, not a conservation law already latent in the midpoint calculus.

# 1. Notation

Let

\[
Q(t)
\]

denote the full phase derivative, and write the rebuilt split as

\[
Q(t)=b(t)+G(t),
\]

where

\[
b(t):=q_{\base}^{\new}(t),
\qquad
G(t):=G^{\new}(t)=q_{\aux,R}(t)+T_{\far,R}(t).
\]

The rebuilt Bottleneck-C row uses the baseline values

\[
b_0=b(m),
\qquad
b_2=b''(m),
\]

and the source moments

\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
G''(m)=Q''(m)-b''(m),
\]

\[
G^{(4)}(m)=Q^{(4)}(m)-b^{(4)}(m).
\]

---

# 2. Required identity in \(Q,b\) variables

The rebuilt obstruction is

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q_{\scale}^{14}}
\left[
\frac{b_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{b_2}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

Substitute

\[
A_2=\frac{Q''-b''}{2},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}}{24}.
\]

Then pointwise flatness is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\frac{b_0}{11520}
(Q''-b'')
(Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)})
+
\frac{1}{576}
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
(Q''-b'')^2
=0.
}
\]

Multiplying by \(11520\),

\[
\boxed{
b_0
(Q''-b'')
(Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)})
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
(Q''-b'')^2
=0.
}
\]

Let

\[
D_2:=Q''-b''=G'',
\qquad
D_4:=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}=G^{(4)}.
\]

Then the condition is

\[
\boxed{
D_2
\left[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
\right]
=0.
}
\]

Thus either

\[
\boxed{
G''(m)=0,
}
\]

or, if \(G''(m)\neq0\),

\[
\boxed{
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b_0}.
}
\]

Equivalently, as an equation for the baseline,

\[
\boxed{
b^{(4)}(m)
=
Q^{(4)}(m)
-
\left(
\frac{40b_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b_0}
\right)
\left(
Q''(m)-b''(m)
\right).
}
\]

This is the key reduction: the desired flatness is not a consequence of \(Q=b+G\). It is a nonlinear fourth-order condition on \(b\).

---

# 3. Does the exact decomposition \(Q=b+G\) imply it?

No.

The identity

\[
Q=b+G
\]

only gives

\[
G''=Q''-b'',
\qquad
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]

It imposes no relation of the form

\[
G^{(4)}
=
\left(
\frac{40b^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''}{3b}
\right)G''.
\]

That relation would be a new differential constraint coupling the **non-core zero complement** to the **baseline phase derivative**. The fixed-core definition partitions the phase derivative into core, auxiliary-zero, far-zero, background, and estimate pieces; it does not itself impose a fourth-order ODE tying the complement to \(b,b''\). The shared background explicitly treats this obstruction as a surviving pointwise condition after the coherent source rebuild, not as an already derived identity. 

---

# 4. Can standard phase asymptotics make it plausible?

Only under a very special tuning that is not present in the draft.

Suppose \(b\) contains the dominant smooth phase/background component. Then typically

\[
b(t)\sim \frac12\log(t/2\pi)
\]

away from zeros, while

\[
b''(t)
\]

is lower order. The required ratio becomes approximately

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
\approx
\frac{40}{3}b^2
\sim
\frac{10}{3}\log^2(t/2\pi).
\]

But \(G\) is a non-core zero-complement sum. Its derivative ratio is governed by the distances from \(m\) to the non-core source poles. A single source pole at distance \(d\) gives a ratio on the order of

\[
\frac{1}{d^2}.
\]

Thus the identity would require the non-core source geometry to align its effective distance scale and constants with the baseline logarithmic phase scale at every good patch. That is not forced by the decomposition.

If the non-core cutoff is microscopic, say \(d\asymp1/\log t\), the scale \(\log^2 t\) is at least dimensionally possible. But the constant and sign would still need to match the specific expression

\[
\frac{40b^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''}{3b},
\]

pointwise. The previous one-pair and finite-tail tests already show that source geometry can produce different ratios; the full complement would need a new global zero-set theorem to enforce the exact value.

---

# 5. Can the identity define the “correct” baseline \(b\)?

Formally, yes. Legitimately, no.

The flatness equation can be solved for \(b^{(4)}\):

\[
b^{(4)}
=
Q^{(4)}
-
\left(
\frac{40b^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''}{3b}
\right)
(Q''-b'').
\]

So one could define \(b\) by requiring it to satisfy this fourth-order equation. But that is circular in this proof architecture: \(b\) would be chosen precisely to kill the Bottleneck-C obstruction.

For this to be legitimate, the draft would need an independent analytic principle selecting \(b\), such as:

\[
b=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}
\]

satisfying this ODE because of the functional equation, a scattering relation, a canonical connection, or a zero-counting conservation law. No such principle is currently present.

So the identity can be used as a **definition of a special baseline**, but not as a proof of Bottleneck-C flatness.

---

# 6. Can a special core/window choice force the identity?

Only by violating the architecture’s source-tagging intent.

There are three artificial ways to force flatness:

### 1. Force \(G''(m)=0\)

Then

\[
A_2=0
\]

and the obstruction vanishes. But this requires choosing the baseline so that

\[
b''(m)=Q''(m)
\]

at every good patch. That moves the relevant source curvature into the baseline and empties the source moment responsible for the row. This is not the fixed source calculus; it changes the gate by construction.

### 2. Force the derivative ratio

Choose the core/window so that

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{40b^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''}{3b}.
\]

This is again a Bottleneck-C-tuned source convention. Unless the window is selected by an independent geometric rule, this is circular.

### 3. Put all problematic zeros into the core

If \(G\) is made negligible or zero, the row disappears. But then the fixed-core/far-tail architecture degenerates: the “core” becomes an infinite or dynamically tuned object, and lower-gate finite-core bookkeeping is no longer the same proof.

Therefore a core/window choice can force the identity only by redefining the source split to absorb the obstruction, not by proving that the actual zero complement satisfies it.

---

# 7. The decisive obstruction

The decomposition

\[
Q=b+G
\]

does not couple \(G^{(4)}/G''\) to \(b,b''\). The required identity says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the fourth-to-second derivative ratio of the non-core zero complement is determined by the baseline phase jet.}
}
\]

That is a strong pointwise claim. It is not implied by:

\[
G=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\]

\[
b=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R},
\]

or the tautological sum

\[
Q=b+G.
\]

It would need to be proved as a new global zero-complement rigidity theorem.

---

# 8. Final dependency statement

The strongest correct statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Bottleneck C requires the full non-core zero complement }
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\text{ to satisfy}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}
{(G^{\new})''(m)}
=
\frac{40(q_{\base}^{\new}(m))^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_{\base}^{\new})''(m)}
{3q_{\base}^{\new}(m)}
}
\]

on every good patch with

\[
(G^{\new})''(m)\neq0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
}
\]

This remains **unproved**. It is not supplied by the source rebuild, the full decomposition \(q=b+G\), standard phase asymptotics, or a non-circular core/window convention.

## Impact on Bottleneck C

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
\quad\text{is still an unproved global dependency.}
}
\]

Thus the pointwise \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C route remains open-negative: either the paper must prove this new global non-core zero-complement identity, or pivot away from the current Bottleneck-C architecture.

_Thought for 59s_

# Agent 5 — Quotient RH-Detection / Lost-\(T\) Agent

## Verdict

The quotient-only architecture is **not yet proved RH-detecting**. It is internally coherent as a gauge-invariant replacement program, but the current draft’s existing scalar detection pipeline still uses representative-level \(\Phi_K\), \(H_m(s)\), and \(T=v_7/c\). Therefore the no-\(T\) architecture can proceed only after proving a new theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH violation}\Rightarrow \text{nonzero quotient anomaly}
}
\]

using only

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1})
\]

and not \(T,\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), or \(v_7\) as independent data. The attached prompt explicitly assigns this as the reused Global Identity Agent task. 

---

## 1. What quotient data forget

The quotient architecture keeps

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\]

only through

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]

and higher determinants

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

Under the line shift

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

we have

\[
u_7\mapsto u_7+\chi u_5,
\qquad
v_7\mapsto v_7+\chi v_5.
\]

Then

\[
\Delta_7
\mapsto
(u_7+\chi u_5)v_5-u_5(v_7+\chi v_5)
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7
=
\Delta_7.
\]

So quotient data are unchanged.

But

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]

changes by

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

Similarly, since

\[
\Phi_K(I)=0,
\qquad
\Phi_K(S)=2,
\]

one gets

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\mapsto
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})+2\chi v_5.
\]

Thus \(T\) and \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\) do **not** descend to the quotient. The attached quotient note states exactly this conditional no-go: if any downstream local-to-global step requires reconstruction of \(T\) or \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), then quotient-only architecture cannot replace Bottleneck C. 

---

## 2. Direct lost-\(T\) model

Assume a good \(v_5\neq0\) patch and \(c\neq0\). Fix quotient data

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7).
\]

Let

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]

For any \(\chi\in\mathbf C\), define

\[
A_{7,\chi}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then

\[
\Delta_{7,\chi}=\Delta_7,
\]

but

\[
T_\chi
=
T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

Since \(\chi\) is arbitrary, \(T_\chi\) can be made any desired value:

\[
\chi=\frac{c}{v_5}(\tau-T)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
T_\chi=\tau.
\]

Therefore quotient data contain an entire affine line of possible hidden \(T\)-states.

This is not a small ambiguity. It means that if a downstream RH-detection statement distinguishes states by \(T\), \(v_7\), or \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), quotient data cannot reproduce that distinction.

On a \(u_5\neq0\) patch with \(v_5=0\), the parallel quotient coordinate is

\[
-\frac{\Delta_7}{cu_5},
\]

but the same issue remains: quotient data determine only the class modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), not a representative.

---

## 3. Classification of current uses

### A. \(T=v_7/c\)

**Classification:** essential representative-level data in the current \(T\)-horizontal architecture.

The existing Bottleneck-C gate uses

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]

So the current architecture treats \(T\)-motion as physical. Since quotienting identifies states with different \(T\), the current Bottleneck-C proof cannot be quotiented directly.

This is precisely why the no-\(T\) route is a new architecture, not a repair of Bottleneck C. The prompt states that the quotient architecture may use \((c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,D_9,\ldots)\) but may not use \(T,\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), or \(v_7\) as independent representative-level data. 

### B. \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\)

**Classification:** essential for the current transform-scalar readout; quotient-invisible line shifts change it.

Because

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})+2\chi v_5,
\]

\(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\) is not a function of quotient data.

Any theorem that uses \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\) as an independent local scalar must be rewritten.

### C. \(H_m(s)=\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m))\)

**Classification:** essential in the current scalar analytic pipeline, not cosmetic.

The current \(H_m(s)\) scalarization is a \(\Phi_K\)-visible transform extraction. That is representative-level because \(\Phi_K\) sees the \(S\)-component. It cannot be replaced merely by saying “take the quotient” unless the entire scalar analytic pipeline is redefined.

A quotient replacement would need something like

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h\!\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right),
\]

or its finite-order determinant analogue. But this new scalar kills every line component

\[
\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Thus it cannot reproduce \(H_m(s)\). It can only replace \(H_m(s)\) if the proof shows that all RH-relevant anomalies have nonzero quotient projection.

### D. Mixed four-point scalar exits

**Classification:** replaceable by quotient determinant data.

The mixed four-point layer appears compatible with quotient determinants: its natural residual is

\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f,
\]

rather than \(f\) alone. The quotient architecture’s local gate is therefore

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0,
\]

not

\[
f=0.
\]

The attached notes explicitly distinguish this from the old \(T\)-horizontal gate. 

So the mixed four-point layer survives quotienting. The full \(\Phi_K\)-visible transform-state layer does not.

---

## 4. Can quotient data alone detect off-line zeros?

Not from the current draft.

The quotient data detect only transverse determinant failure:

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

If all quotient determinants vanish,

\[
D_7=D_9=\cdots=0,
\]

then the fixed-sector anomaly may still be nonzero, but line-gauge:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

That line-gauge anomaly is invisible to quotient data but can still change \(T\) and \(\Phi_K\). The attached coordinator readout already records this risk: quotient finite determinacy is weaker than full determinacy, since \(C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}=0\) says only that the finite-core anomaly lies in the line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), not that the representative anomaly vanishes. 

Thus quotient data alone can detect off-line zeros only if one proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{An off-line zero cannot produce only line-gauge fixed-sector anomalies.}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH violation}\Rightarrow
\exists r\le R:
D_{2r+1}\neq0
}
\]

outside controlled quotient-incidence sets.

That theorem is not currently present.

---

## 5. Candidate quotient scalar readout

A plausible replacement readout is:

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
:=
\omega_h
\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right).
\]

At finite order this gives coefficients

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

This is a valid quotient scalar. It is invariant under

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi_r A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But it loses the entire \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line component.

Therefore

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
\]

can replace

\[
H_m(s)=\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m))
\]

only if the old proof’s contradiction mechanism did not actually require the line component.

I do not find that established. The current scalar analytic machinery built around \(H_m\) must be rederived for \(H_m^{\quot}\).

---

## 6. The precise no-go for direct replacement

**Proposition — Direct \(H_m\)-to-\(H_m^{\quot}\) replacement fails.**  
Let

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S
\]

with \(v_5\neq0\). Let

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]

The quotient data

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7)
\]

are invariant under

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

but

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]

and

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\]

change by

\[
\chi\frac{v_5}{c}
\]

and

\[
2\chi v_5,
\]

respectively. Hence no function of quotient data can recover \(T\) or \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\). Any proof step depending on those quantities cannot be performed in quotient-only variables.

This matches the conditional no-go already inserted in the attached quotient architecture note. 

---

## 7. Exact theorem needed to save the no-\(T\) architecture

The no-\(T\) architecture needs a theorem of the following form.

**Quotient RH-detection theorem.**  
On every good patch associated to an off-critical zero configuration, the corrected fixed-sector odd germ has nonzero quotient determinant data at finite order. More precisely, there exists an order bound \(R=R_{\Theta_k}\) and a lower bound \(\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q)>0\) such that

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\]

implies

\[
\left\|
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))
\right\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1}).
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH violation cannot be hidden entirely in }
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This theorem must not use:

\[
T,\qquad
v_7/c,\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\qquad
H_m(s)=\Phi_K(\cdots).
\]

It may use:

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s),
\qquad
D_{2r+1},
\qquad
\Delta_7,
\qquad
\omega_h(\cdot,A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

plus mixed four-point scalar exits and quotient finite-core geometry.

---

## Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quotient data alone do not currently prove RH detection.}
}
\]

The no-\(T\) architecture is still viable only as a **new proof program**, not as a drop-in replacement for the existing \(H_m=\Phi_K(\cdots)\) pipeline.

The first indispensable \(T\)-dependent step in the current proof is the scalar transform extraction

\[
H_m(s)=\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)).
\]

To continue Branch C, this must be replaced by a quotient scalar

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

and the paper must prove that this quotient scalar still detects all RH-relevant off-line zero anomalies. At present, that theorem is missing.
