## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:40:19)

_Thought for 13s_

# Agent 5 — \(K_1\)-Transport Isolation Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The live order-7 channel belongs to the }K_1\text{-transport sector and cannot be cancelled by }K_3\text{ or pure same-point sectors.}
}
\]

The only possible cancellation would have to come from the \(K_5\)-line sector, because

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But if the \(K_1\)-channel is nonzero modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), then no \(K_5\)-line term can cancel it. Thus the decisive reduced statement is:

\[
\boxed{
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]\neq0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

For the centered one-whitening-slot channel, the fixed-sector contribution is an \(I\)-component

\[
-2yBr\,I.
\]

This is quotient-nonzero whenever \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is not parallel to \(I\), equivalently when \(v_5\neq0\). If \(v_5=0\), the rank-two vector is still nonzero, but quotient isolation no longer rules out \(K_5\)-line cancellation. That case should be treated as a separate incidence branch. The attached updates already sharpen the status to “visibility has a nonzero corrected-whitening channel; remaining issue is cross-channel cancellation.” 

---

# 1. Septic decomposition

Use the draft’s septic decomposition:

\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

The fixed-sector projection has the recorded structure:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

with

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

while the \(K_3\)-shadow vanishes after fixed-sector projection and the pure same-point septic sector vanishes in the odd two-point germ. The actual reduced-core derivation update states this as the canonical quotient-level septic structure: in

\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

one has

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}].
\]

This is the key isolation fact. 

---

# 2. The live channel is \(K_1\)

The live channel is

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}
+
X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\]

with

\[
Y=yJ,\qquad X_{-,1}=BS,\qquad X_0=pI+rD.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1},
\]

so

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_0-X_0YX_{-,1}.
\]

The fixed-sector projection is

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

This channel has exactly the structural shape of a \(K_1\)-transport term: it is not a pure same-point septic term, because it uses one ordered endpoint whitening slot; it is not a \(K_3\)-shadow, because it survives fixed-sector projection; and it is not a \(K_5\)-normalization shadow, because it is generated by the one-whitening-slot transport of a skew quadratic mixed block. The updates explicitly identify this as the live \(K_1\)/one-whitening-slot channel. turn19file2

So I classify

\[
\boxed{
T_7^{(1)}\subset A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

---

# 3. \(K_3\) and pure sectors cannot cancel it

The \(K_3\)-shadow is killed after fixed-sector projection:

\[
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

Therefore it contributes nothing to the fixed-sector vector and cannot cancel

\[
-2yBr\,I.
\]

The pure same-point septic sector vanishes in the odd two-point germ:

\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

This also cannot cancel the live channel.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
K_3\text{ and pure sectors are irrelevant for cancellation.}
}
\]

The only remaining cancellation source is \(K_5\).

---

# 4. \(K_5\)-line terms cannot cancel \(K_1\) in quotient

Because

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

its quotient class vanishes:

\[
[A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Therefore

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}].
\]

If

\[
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]\neq0,
\]

then

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\neq0,
\]

and hence

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\]

as a full rank-two vector.

So the \(K_5\)-line sector cannot cancel a quotient-nonzero \(K_1\) contribution. Any full-vector cancellation

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
=0
\]

would imply

\[
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]=0,
\]

because \(A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\) is zero in the quotient. Thus full cancellation is possible only if the \(K_1\) term is already quotient-zero.

---

# 5. Quotient test for the centered one-whitening-slot channel

The live centered channel is

\[
L_7
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

Let

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The quotient determinant is

\[
\omega_h(L_7,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
\omega_h(-2yBr\,I,\ u_5I+v_5S).
\]

Using

\[
\omega_h(uI+vS,\ u'I+v'S)=uv'-u'v,
\]

we have for \(L_7=(-2yBr)I+0S\),

\[
\omega_h(L_7,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
(-2yBr)v_5.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
[L_7]\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
yBrv_5\neq0.
}
\]

The channel computation already gives

\[
y\neq0,\qquad B\neq0,\qquad r\neq0
\]

outside the incidence conditions

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

Therefore the \(K_1\)-channel is quotient-nonzero provided

\[
v_5\neq0.
\]

So the clean quotient-isolation theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
yBrv_5\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

---

# 6. What if \(v_5=0\)?

If

\[
v_5=0,
\]

then

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I
\]

is parallel to the \(I\)-direction. In that case the live channel

\[
L_7=-2yBr\,I
\]

lies in

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then quotient isolation cannot rule out cancellation by \(K_5\), because both terms lie in the same line.

However, in the full rank-two architecture, \(L_7\) is still a nonzero vector if

\[
yBr\neq0.
\]

The problem is only that a \(K_5\)-line term could, in principle, cancel it.

Thus \(v_5=0\) should be treated as a separate incidence or line-degenerate case:

\[
\mathcal E_{v_5}^{\core}
=
\{v_5=0\}.
\]

This is not fatal to the rank-two architecture, but it is fatal to the quotient-isolation proof of non-cancellation.

So the theorem should be stated on the generic patch

\[
v_5\neq0.
\]

---

# 7. Non-centered \(q^{(7)}\) \(K_1\) channel

The non-centered route is cleaner. The draft’s septic \(K_1\)-transport slice gives a direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven fixed-sector contribution with

\[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
\qquad
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv0.
\]

Again, this is \(I\)-directional. Its quotient determinant is

\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}
=
u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5.
\]

Thus the same conclusion holds:

\[
q^{(7)}\neq0,\quad u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\neq0,\quad v_5\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]\neq0.
\]

Then \(K_5\)-line cancellation is impossible.

If \(v_5=0\), the full vector may still be nonzero, but quotient isolation does not protect it from \(K_5\)-line cancellation.

---

# 8. The \(K_1\)-isolation theorem

The theorem-ready statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.92\linewidth}
On a reduced good patch, suppose the septic decomposition satisfies
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
with \(K_3\)- and pure-sector terms vanishing after the relevant odd/fixed
projection. Then
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Consequently, if
\[
\omega_h(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})\neq0,
\]
then
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
\]
For the centered one-whitening-slot channel
\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\supset -2yBr\,I,
\]
this condition is
\[
-2yBrv_5\neq0.
\]
Therefore, outside the incidence walls
\[
y=0,\quad B=0,\quad r=0,\quad v_5=0,
\]
the live \(K_1\)-channel cannot be cancelled by \(K_5\), \(K_3\), or pure
same-point sectors.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

---

# 9. Exceptional set update

The visibility-positive reduced base should include the exclusion

\[
\mathcal E_{K_1\text{-quot}}^{\core}
=
\{yBrv_5=0\}.
\]

Since

\[
B=0\Longleftrightarrow q''=0
\]

in the centered one-slot route, and

\[
r=0\Longleftrightarrow g=h,
\]

this is

\[
\mathcal E_{K_1\text{-quot}}^{\core}
=
\{y=0\}
\cup
\{q''=0\}
\cup
\{g=h\}
\cup
\{v_5=0\}.
\]

For the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\) route, replace \(\{y=0,q''=0,g=h\}\) by

\[
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\cup
\{u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0\}.
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\]

should exclude these analytic incidence walls.

---

# 10. Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }K_1\text{-transport channel is isolated modulo }\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
K_5\text{-line terms cannot cancel it if the }K_1\text{ quotient determinant is nonzero.}
}
\]

For the centered one-whitening-slot witness, this nonzero quotient condition is

\[
\boxed{
yBrv_5\neq0.
}
\]

For the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\) witness, it is

\[
\boxed{
q^{(7)}u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}v_5\neq0.
}
\]

Therefore order-7 packet visibility is certified on the generic reduced patch excluding the explicit incidence walls above.

The only remaining gap is the \(v_5=0\) branch. For the full rank-two architecture it may still be visible, but quotient isolation no longer rules out \(K_5\)-line cancellation. That branch should be either added to the exceptional set or handled by a separate full-vector \(K_5\)-coefficient computation.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:45:12)

_Thought for 8s_

# Agent 5 — Affine Transport Meaning and Global-Control Agent

## Verdict

Assuming the local rank-two affine forcing equation is established,

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]

the architecture still does **not** yet prove RH. It converts the old scalar Bottleneck-C obstruction into a vector-valued affine transport problem. That is a real improvement: \(E_{\eta\eta}\) no longer has to vanish pointwise by definition. But the proof now needs a **global control theorem** for the accumulated affine displacement.

The next missing theorem is not local. It must be a boundary, holonomy, index, or non-concentration theorem controlling

\[
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt.
\]

The attached instruction correctly frames this as the next step after packet visibility: determine what global theorem would make the affine forcing equation proof-relevant. 

---

# 1. Local affine equation

The local equation is

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f} A = E,
\]

where in the Bottleneck-C order-7 case,

\[
A=A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\]

and

\[
E=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

The active forcing term is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in \Gamma(\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}).
\]

Under the rank-two architecture, this is no longer interpreted as a scalar defect. It is a vector-valued forcing section in the fixed-sector bundle

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]

That is the correct conceptual upgrade.

---

# 2. Transport solution formula

Along a path

\[
\Gamma:[a,b]\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

let

\[
U_{t\to b}
\]

be parallel transport for

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then the forced transport equation has the solution

\[
\boxed{
A(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A(a)
+
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt.
}
\]

For the present case,

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)
+
\int_a^b
U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt.
}
\]

Thus the local obstruction becomes the accumulated displacement

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
:=
\int_\Gamma
U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt.
}
\]

The proof now needs to say something global about this displacement.

---

# 3. Possible path parameters

There are several possible directions for \(\Gamma\).

## 3.1 \(\kappa\)-path

This is the most natural local continuation, because the original Bottleneck-C failure was expressed as a \(\kappa\)-slope:

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]

In the rank-two architecture, the analogue is

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

A \(\kappa\)-path is natural locally, but it needs endpoint values or a closed loop to become a global proof gate.

## 3.2 Midpoint path \(m\)

A midpoint path

\[
m\mapsto b(m)
\]

is natural because the reduced base already depends on the moving local midpoint. The issue is that no canonical interval endpoints are yet tied to RH.

Candidate endpoints might be adjacent reduced-good-patch boundaries, zero-midpoint intervals, or packet neighborhoods. But the proof must specify boundary values of \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\), not just the path.

## 3.3 Finite-core parameter path \(\theta\)

This connects naturally to finite-core non-concentration:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}+J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}.
\]

A path in \(\theta\)-space could make sense if the rank-two forcing controls how finite-core data evolves. This likely merges with the old sampled non-concentration problem.

## 3.4 Source/core deformation path

This is **not** currently safe. Arbitrary source/core changes were previously found non-functorial or affine/torsor-like. On

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

the core convention is fixed. Source/core deformation paths should remain excluded unless the affine torsor theorem is separately proved.

---

# 4. Is there a canonical path or cycle?

Not yet.

The best local candidate is a \(\kappa\)-path at fixed reduced core. The best global candidate is a midpoint path inside one connected component of

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]

But neither currently supplies a canonical closed cycle or boundary condition.

A useful global proof would need one of the following:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical path }\Gamma\text{ with known endpoints;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical loop }\Gamma\text{ with holonomy constraint;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{path-independent affine displacement;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{global zero-counting contour mapped into }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
}
\]

At present, none is established.

So the rank-two affine equation is not yet a proof gate. It is a local transport law awaiting global geometry.

---

# 5. Endpoint and boundary values

The forced transport formula becomes useful if one knows, for instance,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)=0,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)=0.
\]

Then

\[
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt=0
\]

would be forced, and any theorem showing the integral is nonzero would contradict the assumed off-line packet.

Alternatively, if one knows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)-U_{a\to b}A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)
\]

from global zeta symmetry, then the integral is constrained.

But no such boundary values are currently available. Packet visibility gives

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\]

on reduced good patches; it does not give endpoint vanishing.

Thus the next theorem must identify canonical endpoint constraints or convert the equation into an index/holonomy statement.

---

# 6. Does \(E_{\eta\eta}\) have sign, exactness, or monotonicity?

## 6.1 Sign

No useful sign is known. The coefficient

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
\]

contains competing terms such as

\[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
\]

and

\[
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2.
\]

Earlier attacks showed this is not sign-definite. Therefore the forcing is not naturally monotone.

## 6.2 Exactness

Earlier exactness attacks found bulk terms after integration by parts. Multiplying by transport and projecting into \(\mathcal F\) does not automatically make the forcing exact.

So the current status is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}\text{ is not known to be an exact covariant derivative.}
}
\]

## 6.3 Holonomy

The rank-two connection may have holonomy, but the forcing equation is affine. The relevant invariant would be affine holonomy/displacement, not ordinary homogeneous holonomy:

\[
\operatorname{AffHol}_\Gamma
=
\left(
U_\Gamma,
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt
\right).
\]

No global theorem constraining this affine holonomy is currently known.

## 6.4 Index

An index theorem would need a path/cycle and a crossing or winding interpretation of \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\). This may be possible, but it is not yet formulated.

---

# 7. What would make the affine equation proof-relevant?

There are four plausible proof gates.

## Gate 1 — Boundary contradiction

Prove:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)=A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)=0
\]

or otherwise known, while

\[
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}E_{\eta\eta}(t)\,dt\neq0.
\]

This would be the cleanest affine-transport contradiction.

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical endpoints with known }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ values.}
}
\]

## Gate 2 — Affine holonomy obstruction

Find a canonical loop \(\Gamma\) and prove global zeta structure requires

\[
\operatorname{AffHol}_\Gamma=0
\]

or prescribed, while an off-line packet forces nonzero affine displacement.

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical loop and affine holonomy law.}
}
\]

## Gate 3 — Index/spectral-flow theorem

Interpret

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\]

or its projectivization as a path in a rank-two bundle, and prove off-line zeros force a nonzero index while zeta symmetry forces zero index.

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective/affine index theorem tied to RH.}
}
\]

## Gate 4 — Finite-core non-concentration with transport

Use the affine equation to strengthen finite-core non-concentration:

\[
\theta(m)\notin \mathcal Z_k^{\vec f}\cup \mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Rightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}+J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\|_\infty
\ge \Lambda.
\]

Missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{transport-controlled finite-core non-concentration.}
}
\]

This is likely hard, but it may be the most compatible with the existing architecture.

---

# 8. What is the immediate next theorem?

The local affine forcing equation alone is not enough. After it is established, the next theorem should be one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical affine path/boundary theorem}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transported finite-core non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

Given the history of the proof attempt, I would prioritize:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Affine path/boundary theorem.}
}
\]

Reason: without a canonical path or boundary, the transport equation has no global content. Non-concentration can be attacked later, once we know what global transport object is being constrained.

---

# 9. Current proof-state ledger

If Agents 1–4 establish the local equation, the ledger becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet visibility: closed modulo explicit incidence walls.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rank-two connection: conditionally defined on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Bottleneck-C row: reinterpreted as tensorial affine forcing.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global proof gate: still missing.}
}
\]

The missing global gate is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{control of }
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}
(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower})(t)\,dt.
}
\]

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{The affine forcing equation is meaningful only if paired with a global affine transport theorem.}
}
\]

The equation

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

should be treated as a local structural theorem, not yet a contradiction.

The next mathematical target after proving the local equation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find a canonical path/cycle/boundary condition on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\text{ that constrains the affine displacement.}
}
\]

More concretely:

\[
\boxed{
A(b)
=
U_\Gamma A(a)
+
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt
}
\]

must be connected to RH by either endpoint values, holonomy, index, or finite-core non-concentration. Without that global theorem, the rank-two architecture remains locally coherent but proof-incomplete.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:48:59)

_Thought for 10s_

# Agent 5 — Background/Core Baseline and Line-Term Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}\text{ and }E_{\rm bg/core}\text{ are acceptable parts of }E_{\rm lower}
\text{ for the rank-two affine transport architecture.}
}
\]

The \(K_5\)-line / normalization-shadow terms are not scalar defects; they are legitimate vector-valued line components inside the rank-two bundle. The background/core baseline terms are fixed analytic forcing terms on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), not new Bottleneck-C obstructions, provided the reduced base keeps the source/core convention fixed. The attached instruction asks specifically whether these two classes are controlled inside \(E_{\rm lower}\), and the answer is yes, conditionally on the already stated fixed-core and functorial-projection hypotheses. 

---

# 1. \(K_5\)-line / normalization-shadow terms

The septic decomposition has the form

\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

The \(K_5\) sector is the normalization / reference-line shadow:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

So the corresponding contribution to the affine forcing equation is

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This term is invisible in the quotient

\[
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

but the present architecture is **not** quotient-only. It is rank-two. Therefore the line term is not discarded; it is transported as part of the full vector

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}\text{ is not a defect; it is a legitimate rank-two forcing component.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Can \(E_{\rm line}\) cancel \(E_{\eta\eta}\)?

The active forcing row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

A line term could cancel it in the full rank-two space only if

\[
E_{\eta\eta}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\omega_h(E_{\eta\eta},A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0.
\]

For

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\]

this condition is

\[
\omega_h(wI+uS,u_5I+v_5S)
=
wv_5-u_5u
=
0.
\]

Thus a full cancellation by a line term requires the incidence condition

\[
\boxed{
wv_5-u_5u=0.
}
\]

This is not a structural identity of the rank-two system. It is a proper line-alignment condition. Therefore, outside the incidence wall

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm line-align}^{\core}
=
\{wv_5-u_5u=0\},
\]

\(K_5\)-line terms cannot cancel the \(K_1\) / \(E_{\eta\eta}\) forcing.

Even on the incidence wall, the right interpretation is not “Bottleneck C closes”; it is “the forcing happens to lie in the reference line.” Since the rank-two architecture keeps line components, this remains transportable data, not a quotient-level zero.

---

# 3. Relation to the \(K_1\)-visibility channel

The live order-7 visibility channel was isolated as a \(K_1\)-transport contribution. In the centered one-whitening-slot calculation, it has the form

\[
L_7=-2yBr\,I.
\]

The \(K_5\)-line sector can cancel this only if

\[
L_7\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

For

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\]

this happens generically only when

\[
v_5=0,
\]

i.e. when \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is itself \(I\)-parallel.

Therefore the previous visibility analysis correctly excluded or separated the incidence wall

\[
\boxed{
v_5=0.
}
\]

Outside \(v_5=0\), \(K_5\)-line terms cannot cancel the \(K_1\) visibility channel. Inside \(v_5=0\), quotient isolation fails, but the rank-two vector may still be nonzero; this branch should be handled as a controlled incidence case or by direct full-vector computation.

---

# 4. Background/core analytic baseline terms

Now consider

\[
E_{\rm bg/core}.
\]

These are contributions coming from:

\[
q_{\core},
\qquad
B_{\bg},
\qquad
E_{\est,R},
\]

and from fixed analytic baseline pieces of the corrected local kernel.

On the reduced base

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

the source/core convention is fixed. Therefore these background/core terms are not transition artifacts. They are analytic functions or sections on the same rank-two bundle:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}\in \Gamma(\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}).
}
\]

They may be nonzero, but they are not uncontrolled Bottleneck-C rows. They are part of the total forcing

\[
E=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

Thus the affine forcing equation should be written as

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm line}
+
E_{\rm bg/core}
+
E_{\rm GateA/B}
+
E_{\rm shadow}
+
E_{\rm conn}.
}
\]

After Gate A/B closure, shadow projection, and covariantization, the meaningful remaining local forcing is

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm line}+E_{\rm bg/core}.
}
\]

That is acceptable for the affine transport architecture.

---

# 5. Are background/core terms lower order?

They are lower-risk rather than necessarily lower-order.

Some background/core terms may occur at the same order \(7\), but they are **known analytic baseline data** once the reduced core convention is fixed. They do not carry the same status as the previously fatal scalar Bottleneck-C row, because the new architecture is allowed to have inhomogeneous forcing.

The real question is no longer local vanishing. It is whether the global affine displacement

\[
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}
\left(
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm line}
+
E_{\rm bg/core}
\right)(t)\,dt
\]

is constrained by some path, boundary, holonomy, or index theorem.

So background/core terms are not locally fatal. They merely enter the forcing budget.

---

# 6. Do background/core terms depend on forbidden source/core transitions?

On

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

no. By construction, arbitrary source/core transitions are excluded. The canonical core is fixed and locally stable. Therefore:

\[
q_{\core},\quad B_{\bg},\quad E_{\est,R}
\]

are part of the local analytic data of the chosen reduced stratum.

If one attempted to compare different core conventions, background/core terms could acquire affine transfer corrections. But that is outside the reduced-base architecture. It was precisely the reason to restrict to

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]

So the line/background audit is valid only under the fixed-core convention.

---

# 7. Does \(E_{\rm lower}\) contain a new local obstruction?

From the line/background perspective:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No new scalar-type local obstruction appears.}
}
\]

The only remaining possible local obstruction would be if

\[
E_{\rm bg/core}
\]

contained an additional uncontrolled source-Hessian row of the same tensorial type as \(E_{\eta\eta}\), not listed under Gate A/B, \(K_5\), \(K_3\), pure, or connection terms.

That cannot be ruled out solely from the line/background audit; it belongs to Agent 1’s full row-table inventory and Agent 3’s septic sector decomposition. But, assuming their classification holds, line and baseline terms are controlled.

Thus my conditional closure statement is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}+E_{\rm bg/core}
\text{ is acceptable inside }E_{\rm lower}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Theorem-ready statement

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.92\linewidth}
On the reduced visibility-positive base \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the
\(K_5\)-normalization sector contributes only line terms
\[
E_{\rm line}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
These terms are legitimate rank-two forcing components and are not scalar
defects. They cannot cancel a quotient-nonzero \(K_1\) contribution outside
the line-alignment incidence
\[
\omega_h(E_{K_1},A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0.
\]
The background/core terms \(E_{\rm bg/core}\) are fixed analytic sections of
\(\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\) because the source/core convention is fixed on
the reduced base. They may enter the total affine forcing, but they do not
create a new local Bottleneck-C obstruction. Therefore, after Gate A/B,
shadow, pure, and connection terms are separately controlled, the remaining
lower forcing
\[
E_{\rm line}+E_{\rm bg/core}
\]
is acceptable for the next global affine transport theorem.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}\text{ is controlled as a transported line component.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}\text{ is controlled as fixed analytic baseline forcing.}
}
\]

Thus, from Agent 5’s assigned perspective,

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm lower}\text{ has no additional local obstruction from line or background/core terms.}
}
\]

The next global theorem must control the total affine forcing

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm line}+E_{\rm bg/core}
}
\]

through path, boundary, holonomy, index, or finite-core non-concentration.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:54:06)

_Thought for 15s_

# Agent 5 — Transported Finite-Core Non-Concentration Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transport data do not by themselves close finite-core non-concentration.}
}
\]

The affine equation

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

adds meaningful differential structure, but it does not prevent the old aligned branch

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
\]

unless paired with a global boundary, monotonicity, sign, or incidence theorem. A transported finite-core vector is coherent, but the non-concentration theorem remains essentially as hard as before. This is the Agent 5 task in the global affine transport wave. 

---

# 1. Candidate transported finite-core vectors

There are three natural candidates.

## Candidate A — value plus derivative

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots).
}
\]

This is the most direct transport-enhanced vector. It records both the fixed-sector coefficient and its covariant motion.

Using the affine equation,

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]

the second component is not independent. It is the forcing.

## Candidate B — value plus forcing

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{E}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
E_9,
\ldots).
}
\]

This makes the forcing explicit. It is cleaner if the goal is to measure whether the packet produces nonzero local displacement.

## Candidate C — residual form

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm res}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
R_7,
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
R_9,
\ldots),
}
\]

where

\[
R_7
:=
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
-
(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}).
\]

But if the affine forcing equation is correct, then

\[
R_7=0.
\]

So this residual vector is useful for checking the local equation, not for proving RH. It cannot be the finite-core non-concentration vector.

The only plausible candidate for proof is therefore Candidate A or B.

---

# 2. Does forcing prevent aligned cancellation?

No, not locally.

The old obstruction was:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f},
\]

with the bad aligned branch

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}.
\]

If we transport-enhance the vector, the analogous decomposition is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

There is still a formal aligned branch:

\[
\boxed{
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

Adding

\[
\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\]

only adds more coordinates. It does not by itself impose a sign, convexity, or positivity condition that forbids simultaneous cancellation in value and derivative.

A local countermodel is immediate. Let

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)=p(t),
\]

and choose

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(t)
=
-p(t)+\varepsilon w(t),
\]

with small nonzero \(\varepsilon\). Then

\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|
=
\varepsilon \|w(t)\|
\]

can be made smaller than any proposed lower bound unless an incidence theorem forbids the alignment.

So transport does not remove the aligned branch. It merely changes the vector in which alignment occurs.

---

# 3. Does \(E_{\eta\eta}\neq0\) give a lower bound?

Only for the derivative/forcing component, not for the value component.

Packet visibility gives

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\]

on

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]

The affine forcing equation gives

\[
\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

If

\[
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\neq0,
\]

then the transported vector

\[
(A_7,\nabla A_7)
\]

is nonzero. But finite-core non-concentration needs a quantitative lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)
}
\]

outside incidence.

Nonzero forcing is not enough. A function can have nonzero derivative at a point and arbitrarily small value there; conversely, derivative contributions can be cancelled by interaction terms unless a sign or cone theorem controls them.

Thus the local equation supplies detection, not non-concentration.

---

# 4. Role of \(E_{\rm line}\) and \(E_{\rm bg/core}\)

The lower forcing has the accepted form

\[
E_{\rm lower}
=
E_{\rm line}+E_{\rm bg/core}
+\text{closed/shadow/connection terms}.
\]

The line term satisfies

\[
E_{\rm line}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The background/core term is fixed analytic forcing on the reduced base.

Both are legitimate rank-two forcing components. But both can also contribute to cancellation in a normed finite-core vector:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm line}
+
E_{\rm bg/core}.
\]

Unless the paper proves that these components lie in a cone, have a sign, or are transverse to the interaction subspace, they do not improve non-concentration. They enlarge the forcing vector but also enlarge the possible aligned-cancellation space.

So:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm line}\text{ and }E_{\rm bg/core}\text{ are controlled locally, but not coercive globally.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Transported feature-balance problem survives

If one defines a transported feature curve

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)
=
(v_{\rm value}(u),v_{\nabla}(u)),
\]

then the \(dd\)-interaction kernel has the same schematic form:

\[
K_{ij}^{dd,\rm tr}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2
\langle v_{\rm tr}(u_i),v_{\rm tr}(u_j)\rangle.
\]

Feature balance still requires:

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)=0
\quad
\forall \sum_i a_i=0.
\]

As before, this is equivalent to sampled constancy:

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\rm tr}(u_k).
\]

The same countermodel survives:

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)
=
v_0+\varepsilon u^2w,
\]

with

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\qquad
a=(1,-2,1),
\]

giving

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)
=
2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

Thus transport does not automatically solve interaction rigidity.

---

# 6. Spectral/cone problem also survives

For a unit transported feature curve,

\[
\langle v_{\rm tr}(u),v_{\rm tr}(u)\rangle=1,
\]

the same expansion gives

\[
\kappa_4
=
-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle\le0,
\]

but

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

The sign of

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
\]

is not controlled by the affine transport equation.

A unit curve

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)
=
(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

still violates the desired sign when

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}.
\]

So the transported finite-core route inherits the old spectral-cone obstruction unless the rank-two forcing equation imposes additional curvature restrictions on \(v_{\rm tr}\). It currently does not.

---

# 7. What theorem would make transported non-concentration viable?

A viable transported finite-core theorem would need one of the following.

## Option A — Coercive forcing theorem

Prove that

\[
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

has a component outside the interaction cancellation cone, with lower bound

\[
\|E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\|
\ge
\Lambda_E(m,Q).
\]

Then include forcing in the finite-core vector.

No such cone theorem is currently available.

## Option B — Differential non-concentration theorem

Prove that a section and its covariant derivative cannot both be small outside incidence:

\[
\boxed{
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|
+
\|\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
}
\]

This is plausible only with a unique continuation / finite-order analytic inequality. It would need a Remez/Łojasiewicz-type theorem for vector-valued sections and their derivatives.

This is a possible future route, but it is not established.

## Option C — Boundary-to-interior transport theorem

If endpoint values are controlled, then nonzero forcing can imply nonzero value somewhere along the path. This merges with the global affine path/boundary theorem.

This is probably the more natural route.

---

# 8. Final assessment

Transported finite-core non-concentration is not easier than the old finite-core problem unless we add a new global theorem.

The current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Affine forcing improves the geometric language but does not by itself produce a finite-core lower bound.}
}
\]

The aligned branch remains:

\[
\boxed{
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
}
\]

The interaction and spectral countermodels remain.

Therefore the next theorem should **not** be “transported non-concentration” immediately. It should first be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical path/boundary or differential non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

Without one of those, the transported finite-core vector is just a larger vector with the same cancellation problem.

---

# Theorem dependency if this route continues

A possible theorem statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Transported finite-core non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

On

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm int}^{\rm tr},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|
+
\|\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|
+
\sum_{r\ge4}
\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
}
\]

But the missing part is exactly

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm int}^{\rm tr}
\text{ contains the aligned branch.}
}
\]

That is not proved.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transported finite-core non-concentration remains open-negative.}
}
\]

The affine forcing equation does not eliminate the aligned branch or the \(dd\)-interaction feature/spectral obstructions.

The most viable next global target remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical affine path/boundary theorem}
}
\]

or, secondarily,

\[
\boxed{
\text{vector-valued differential non-concentration theorem for }(A_7,\nabla A_7).
}
\]

Without such a theorem, transported finite-core non-concentration is not yet a proof gate.

## Edit 1 — Add a reduced-core base subsection

**Where:** Insert immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{Rank-two fixed-sector bundle as the remaining viable language}
\label{subsec:rank-two-fixed-sector-remaining-language}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Reduced fixed-core base and source/core non-functoriality}
\label{subsec:reduced-fixed-core-base-source-core-nonfunctoriality}

The rank-two fixed-sector language is only meaningful globally after fixing the
source/core convention.  The source/core functoriality audits show that moving
a zero atom into or out of the fixed core is not presently known to be a
\(GL_2\)-change of fixed-sector frame.  Rather, a source/core move can change
the corrected local object itself.  At the level of fixed-sector coefficients,
the natural transition has the affine form
\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij,2r+1},
\]
not the vector-bundle form
\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The affine cocycle identity
\[
B_{ik}=G_{jk}^{-1}B_{ij}+B_{jk}
\]
is not presently proved.  Thus arbitrary source/core transitions are excluded
from the rank-two vector-bundle route.

We therefore work on a reduced fixed-convention base.  The intended core rule
is the symmetry-packet version of the nearest same-scale core:
\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]
Here the ordering is by symmetry packets, not by individual zeros.  This avoids
treating functional-equation or conjugation ties internal to a required packet
as core-boundary failures.

Let
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm tie}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm patch}^{\core},
\]
where the additional terms denote, respectively, packet-score ties
\(d_k=d_{k+1}\), same-scale boundary failure, symmetry-closure ambiguity,
endpoint-gap failure, Gram/whitening singularity, and patch-boundary or label
instability.  Define
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
:=
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\) the selected core is locally constant as a labelled
symmetry-closed same-scale zero packet, and no zero moves into or out of
\(q_{\core}\).

The reduced-base theorem still has a global reach condition.  For every
RH-relevant off-line packet
\[
\mathcal P(\rho)=\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne\frac12,
\]
one must prove either that there exists a nearby point
\[
b=(m,s,\mathcal C_k(m))\in\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\]
or that the failure lies in a controlled incidence component of
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}\).  In particular, it is not enough to say
that \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}\) is exceptional; one must prove that it
does not swallow all RH-relevant off-line configurations.

\begin{hypothesis}[Reduced good-patch existence]
\label{hyp:reduced-good-patch-existence}
Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet admits a reduced good patch
\(b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}\), or lies in a controlled incidence component of
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}\).
\end{hypothesis}

This hypothesis is now a standing reach condition for the rank-two route.
It is independent of the local coefficient algebra: Gate~A and Gate~B remain
local fixed-convention lemmas on each reduced stratum, but they do not prove
source/core functoriality across different core choices.
```

## Edit 2 — Add the visibility-positive reduced base

**Where:** Insert after the new subsection from Edit 1 and before the existing rank-two subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Visibility-positive reduced base}
\label{subsec:visibility-positive-reduced-base}

The rank-two route also requires the off-line packet to be visible to the
fixed-sector odd germ.  Define
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\]
on the reduced stratum.  The fixed-sector invisibility locus is
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
:=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}.
\]
The packet-visibility audits reduce this condition to explicit order-seven
incidence walls.

At centered parity, the direct raw off-diagonal order-seven coefficient
\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
-1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
is not itself a fixed-sector witness.  If \(X_0=G_0^{-1/2}\) is the leading
same-point whitening, then
\[
X_0N_7^{\off}X_0
=
C_7(\det X_0)J,
\]
which is still skew, and hence
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]
Thus the raw lower-left \(s^7\)-coefficient is not the visibility witness.

The live centered channel is instead the one-whitening-slot term
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]
At centered parity
\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]
Write
\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS.
\]
Then
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_0-X_0YX_{-,1},
\]
and a direct multiplication gives
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]
Here
\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\qquad
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}),
\]
where
\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right).
\]
For the centered off-line packet, \(q''=2A_2\ne0\), and the quadratic
mixed-block coefficient has leading value
\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\ne0.
\]
Therefore the centered one-whitening-slot channel is fixed-sector visible
outside the incidence walls
\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

The septic decomposition also isolates this channel from the remaining
order-seven pieces.  We have
\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}+A_{7,K_5}+A_{7,K_3}+A_{7,\mathrm{pure}},
\]
with
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\qquad
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
after fixed-sector projection and odd two-point extraction.  Hence
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in }
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
For the centered one-whitening-slot witness
\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\supset -2yBr\,I,
\]
the quotient determinant is
\[
\omega_h(-2yBr\,I,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
-2yBr\,v_5.
\]
Thus \(K_5\)-line terms cannot cancel the live \(K_1\)-channel on the generic
patch
\[
yBrv_5\ne0.
\]

There is also a non-centered visibility route.  The draft's local construction
uses
\[
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2}
\]
and does not force \(m\) to equal the packet center.  For the paired packet
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]
one has, near \(x_m=0\),
\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m
+
O(x_m^3).
\]
Thus \(x_m=0\) is a simple zero of \(q^{(7)}(m)\), and every sufficiently small
nonzero perturbation of \(m\) activates the septic \(K_1\)-transport slice.
This gives order-seven visibility on the non-centered reduced patch outside
\[
q^{(7)}=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\Xi_{K_1}=0.
\]

Define the visibility-positive reduced base by
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
:=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7},
\]
where, for the centered one-whitening-slot route, one may take
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
\supset
\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\}\cup\{v_5=0\},
\]
and, for the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-route, one may take
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
\supset
\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\),
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\ne0.
\]
Thus packet visibility is closed modulo explicit analytic incidence walls.
```

This insertion captures the main recent positive result: the live order-7 \(K_1\) / one-whitening-slot channel is visible, while the raw \(N_7^{\off}\) channel is not. The attached notes explicitly flag this as the significant positive update.

## Edit 3 — Strengthen the rank-two connection subsection

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{Rank-two fixed-sector bundle as the remaining viable language}
\label{subsec:rank-two-fixed-sector-remaining-language}
```

Find the paragraph beginning:

```latex
The local candidate connection is the projected ambient derivative
```

Replace through the end of the proposition `\ref{prop:conditional-rank-two-connection}` with the following cleaner version, preserving the existing label if you already use it.

**Replacement:**

```latex
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the local candidate connection is the
projected ambient derivative
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\bigl(d_X^{\mathcal J}A\bigr),
\]
where \(\mathcal J\) is the ambient corrected finite-\(s\) jet/kernel-state
bundle, \(d^{\mathcal J}\) is its ambient derivative, and
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}:\mathcal J_b\to\mathfrak f_h(b)
\]
is the fixed-sector projection.  Since \(\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)\) is
treated as a subbundle of \(\mathcal J_b\), no arbitrary ambient lift is
involved: a section \(A\in\Gamma(\mathcal F)\) is differentiated as its
canonical ambient representative and then projected back to \(\mathcal F\).

The projected derivative satisfies the Leibniz rule.  Indeed,
\[
d_X^{\mathcal J}(fA)=X(f)A+f\,d_X^{\mathcal J}A,
\]
and \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}A=A\), hence
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}(fA)
=
X(f)A+f\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A.
\]

In a local frame
\[
E=(I,S),
\qquad
A=Ea,
\]
the connection has the form
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A
=
E(da+\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}a).
\]
If
\[
E=E^{\rm raw}W,
\]
then formally
\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W+W^{-1}dW.
\]
In particular, if the raw frame is flat in the chart, then
\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}=W^{-1}dW.
\]

On an overlap with
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\]
the connection matrices satisfy
\[
\Gamma_j
=
G_{ij}^{-1}\Gamma_iG_{ij}
+
G_{ij}^{-1}dG_{ij}.
\]
Thus the connection is canonical exactly to the extent that the reduced
fixed-sector atlas and the fixed-sector projection are functorial.

\begin{proposition}[Conditional rank-two connection theorem]
\label{prop:conditional-rank-two-connection}
Assume that on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\):
\begin{enumerate}
\item the core/source convention is fixed and locally stable;
\item no zero moves into or out of \(q_{\core}\);
\item the fixed-sector frames satisfy
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik};
\]
\item the ambient corrected jet bundle \(\mathcal J\) and the fixed-sector
projection \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\) are functorial under the same transitions.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\]
defines a rank-two connection on
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]
\end{proposition}
```

## Edit 4 — Replace/strengthen the \(E_{\eta\eta}\) affine forcing subsection

**Where:** In:

Keep the opening statement that \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is a section, then replace the current “expected decomposition” block with the following.

**Replacement:**

```latex
The natural local replacement for scalar Bottleneck-C flatness is an affine
transport equation
\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm lower}.
\]
Here \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is the tensorial symmetric source-Hessian forcing
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]
and \(E_{\rm lower}\) denotes every remaining order-seven contribution after
passing to the covariant derivative.

The expected local table is
\[
E_{\rm lower}
=
E_{\rm GateA}
+
E_{\rm GateB}
+
E_{\rm line}
+
E_{K_3}
+
E_{\rm pure}
+
E_{\rm conn}
+
E_{\rm bg/core}
+
E_{K_1}^{\rm comp}.
\]
The current local ledger classifies these pieces as follows:
\[
E_{\rm GateA}=0,
\qquad
E_{\rm GateB}=0
\]
under the accepted Gate~A/B fixed-convention hypotheses;
\[
E_{\rm conn}=0
\]
after replacing ordinary differentiation by
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}=\Pi_{\mathfrak f}d^{\mathcal J};
\]
\[
E_{K_3}=0
\]
after fixed-sector projection;
\[
E_{\rm pure}=0
\]
in the odd two-point germ; and
\[
E_{\rm line}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The \(K_5\)-line terms are not scalar defects in the rank-two architecture.
They are transported as part of the full vector.  They can cancel a \(K_1\)
forcing vector only on the line-alignment incidence
\[
\omega_h(E_{K_1},A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0.
\]
For the centered one-whitening-slot visibility channel
\[
E_{K_1}\supset -2yBr\,I,
\]
this quotient-noncancellation condition is
\[
yBrv_5\ne0.
\]

The background/core terms \(E_{\rm bg/core}\) are fixed analytic forcing data
on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), because the source/core convention is frozen
there.  They may contribute to the total forcing, but they do not constitute a
new local Bottleneck-C obstruction.  A fully written row table is still needed
to document that no additional same-grade \(K_1\) source-Hessian companion
survives outside the already identified \(E_{\eta\eta}\) row.

Thus the present local status is:
\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm lower}
}
\]
is conditionally closed on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), pending only the
written \(E_{\rm lower}\) row table.  No second uncontrolled fixed-sector
source-Hessian row has been found.
```

This matches the latest local closure status: \(E_{\rm lower}\) is controlled modulo a written table, and the next issue is global affine transport.

## Edit 6 — Add a transported finite-core no-go remark

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}
\label{subsec:finite-core-sampled-vector-nonconcentration}
```

Insert after `\begin{definition}[Interaction-aligned finite-core branch]...` or after the paragraph defining the aligned branch.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Transported finite-core data do not remove alignment]
\label{rem:transported-finite-core-data-do-not-remove-alignment}
One may try to strengthen the finite-core vector by adding covariant transport
data, for instance
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots),
\]
or by replacing the derivative coordinate using the affine equation
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]
This is coherent, but it does not by itself prove sampled
non-concentration.  The old aligned branch simply becomes
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]
Adding derivative or forcing coordinates enlarges the finite vector but does
not impose a sign, cone, monotonicity, or endpoint constraint that forbids
alignment.

Thus any transported finite-core theorem would need a genuinely new input,
such as
\[
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|
+
\|\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|
+
\sum_{r\ge4}\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)
\]
outside a controlled transported incidence set.  This is a new
non-concentration theorem, not a formal consequence of the local affine
forcing equation.
\end{remark}
```

This directly captures the transported finite-core no-go: the affine equation adds geometry but does not itself remove the aligned branch.

## Edit 7 — Add a stronger global affine transport dependency statement

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{Global affine transport dependency}
\label{subsec:global-affine-transport-dependency}
```

Replace the final remark if it already exists, or insert immediately after it.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Global proof gate after local affine forcing]
\label{rem:global-proof-gate-after-local-affine-forcing}
The local affine forcing equation is not a contradiction.  It gives the
transport identity
\[
A(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A(a)
+
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt,
\qquad
E=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]
To become proof-relevant, this identity needs one of the following additional
global inputs:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a canonical path \(\Gamma\) with known endpoint values for
\(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\);
\item a canonical loop with prescribed affine holonomy;
\item a path-independent affine displacement theorem;
\item a projective-plus-scale index theorem tied to the rank-two section;
\item a transported finite-core non-concentration theorem.
\end{enumerate}
At present, none is proved.  In particular, \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is not sign
definite, not known to be exact, and not currently tied to a boundary value or
holonomy law.  The rank-two formulation therefore changes the local
interpretation of Bottleneck~C but leaves the main global proof gate open.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
by a canonical boundary, holonomy, index, exactness, or transported
```

## Edit 9 — Optional but recommended: add a theorem-style visibility statement

**Where:** After Edit 2’s subsection, or at the end of the existing rank-two subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Order-seven packet visibility on the reduced base]
\label{prop:order-seven-packet-visibility-reduced-base}
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the fixed-sector finite vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots)
\]
is nonzero.  More precisely, in the centered route the one-whitening-slot
channel
\[
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\qquad
Y=yJ,
\]
has fixed-sector projection
\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]
which is nonzero outside
\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]
Its \(K_1\)-class cannot be cancelled by \(K_5\)-line, \(K_3\)-shadow, or pure
same-point septic sectors outside the additional line-incidence wall
\[
v_5=0.
\]
In the non-centered route, the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven septic \(K_1\)-slice
gives order-seven visibility outside
\[
q^{(7)}=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\Xi_{K_1}=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For the centered route, the direct raw off-diagonal term is skew and killed by
fixed-sector projection, but the one-whitening-slot term satisfies
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}
\right)
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]
The factors are nonzero on the visibility-positive base by definition.  The
septic decomposition gives
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in }
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
because \(K_5\) is line-valued, \(K_3\) is projected away, and pure same-point
septic terms vanish in the odd two-point germ.  Hence quotient-nonzero
\(K_1\) visibility implies \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0\).

For the non-centered route, the local construction treats \(m\) as the sample
midpoint
\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2,
\]
not as the zero-packet center.  The packet offset
\[
x_m=2m-\gamma
\]
is therefore a genuine local parameter, and
\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3)
\]
near \(x_m=0\).  Thus \(q^{(7)}\) is nonzero off a proper analytic wall, and
the direct septic \(K_1\)-transport slice gives \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0\) on
the corresponding visibility-positive patch.
\end{proof}
```

This is the most important positive structural insertion.

## Edit 1 — Add explicit reduced-good-patch reach hypothesis

This was a recurring dependency in the core/non-swallowing waves. turn27file14

```latex
labelled symmetry-closed packet.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Reduced good-patch reach]
\label{hyp:reduced-good-patch-reach}
Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line symmetry packet
\[
\mathcal P(\rho)=\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne\frac12,
\]
admits a nearby reduced good patch
\[
b=(m,s,\mathcal C_k(m))\in\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\]
or else the failure lies in a controlled component of
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}\).
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Status of the reach hypothesis]
\label{rem:status-reduced-good-patch-reach}
The strict-gap, same-scale, endpoint, symmetry-closure, and Gram/whitening
conditions are open conditions once they hold at one point.  Thus
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:reduced-good-patch-reach} is a non-swallowing assertion:
the enlarged exceptional set
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\]
must not contain all RH-relevant off-line packet configurations.  This is a
global reach condition for the rank-two route, not a consequence of Gate~A or
```

```latex
For the centered route, the direct skew \(N_7^{\off}\)-term projects to zero,
but the one-whitening-slot \(K_1\)-channel has fixed-sector projection
\[
-2yBr\,I.
\]
This vector is nonzero outside
\[
\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\}.

we also exclude
\[
v_5=0.

\[
\omega_h(-2yBr\,I,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=

so \(K_5\)-line terms cannot cancel the \(K_1\)-channel on the generic patch

The branch \(v_5=0\) is therefore either included in
```

```latex
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
```

```latex
The notation in this subsection originally arose in the scalar
\(\Phi_K\)-sampled formulation.  In the current rank-two architecture, the
corresponding fixed-sector vector is
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(\theta)
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,

\[

should be regarded as its \(\Phi_K\)-readout, not as the full fixed-sector

P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(\theta),
\]
or for a transported enhancement of this vector, rather than merely for the
scalar \(\Phi_K\)-projection.
```

This keeps the old material usable while demoting it to a projection of the new object.

---

## Edit 5 — Add one sentence to the global dependency section: transported non-concentration is not currently easier

**Why:** The draft includes a good remark near finite-core, but the global section should also state the same conclusion: transported finite-core is not automatically easier. This prevents the reader from thinking the transport vector immediately resolves the aligned branch. 

**Where:** In:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current global dependency]
\label{rem:current-global-affine-transport-dependency}
```

After the list ending with:

```latex
\item a transported finite-core non-concentration theorem for the full
fixed-sector vector.
```

**Insert before “None of these is presently proved.”:**

```latex
The last option is not automatic: adding
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]
to the finite-core vector merely produces a larger transported vector.  It
does not by itself exclude the aligned branch
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\]
without an additional coercivity, boundary, incidence, or cone theorem.
```

---

## Holistic status / promotion-demotion notes

### Promote

The following is now strong enough to be presented as a named local result:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Order-seven packet visibility on the reduced base]
...
\end{proposition}
```

This is already present. Keep it, but apply Edit 2 so the \(v_5\)-condition is visible.

### Keep conditional

The rank-two connection theorem and affine forcing theorem should stay conditional. The assumptions are not cosmetic: fixed core convention, functorial \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\), \(GL_2\)-atlas, and no source/core moves are still real dependencies.

### Demote / avoid overclaiming

Avoid saying:

```latex
Packet visibility is closed.
```

without qualification. Prefer:

```latex
Packet visibility is closed on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) modulo explicit incidence walls.
```

The draft mostly does this, but the proposition title and ledger should keep “on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\)” prominent.

### Keep the global gate open

The paper now correctly says the missing theorem is global affine transport / boundary / holonomy / index / transported non-concentration. That should remain the final status. No insertion needed beyond Edit 5.

---

## Bottom line

I would apply the five edits above. The latest draft has captured the core structural findings. The main remaining precision issue is to prevent two overreadings:

1. that packet visibility holds without the \(v_5\) / \(K_5\)-line incidence caveat;  
2. that transported finite-core non-concentration follows automatically from the affine forcing equation.

Everything else looks appropriately promoted/demoted.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 20:49:46)

_Thought for 17s_

# Agent 5 — Transported Finite-Core / Cone Lower-Bound Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transported finite-core data do not currently give a proof-closing lower bound.}
}
\]

The candidate transported vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
\left(
A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots
\right)
\]

is coherent and probably the right object if the rank-two route continues. But the old cancellation branch survives in transported coordinates:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

I do **not** find a cone, scale, or transport mechanism that forbids this alignment. The affine equation adds local differential structure, but without a global boundary/holonomy/coercivity theorem it only enlarges the finite-core vector; it does not produce the needed quantitative lower bound. This is exactly the global gate assigned to Agent 5 in the attached instruction. 

---

# 1. Candidate transported finite-core object

The natural transported vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)
=
\left(
A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots,
A_{2R+1}^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_{2R+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\right)(\theta).
\]

Using the affine forcing equation,

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]

one can also write the first transported block as

\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}).
\]

So the transported finite-core vector records both value and forced motion.

The desired theorem would be something like:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
}
\]

Equivalently, after the pair/interaction decomposition,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr},
\]

one wants

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)
}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

---

# 2. Formal alignment countermodel survives

The alignment obstruction survives immediately in the transported vector space.

Let \(V_{\rm tr}\) be the finite-dimensional vector space containing the transported finite-core data. Pick any nonzero vector

\[
p\in V_{\rm tr},
\]

and another nonzero vector

\[
w\in V_{\rm tr}.
\]

Define a one-parameter analytic family

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)=p,
\]

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)=-p+\varepsilon w.
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)
=
\varepsilon w.
\]

For every \(\varepsilon\ne0\),

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)\ne0,
\]

so the point is not in the exact vanishing locus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}.
\]

But

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\varepsilon)\|
=
|\varepsilon|\,\|w\|
\]

can be made arbitrarily small.

Thus no purely local analytic nonvanishing theorem can imply a uniform lower bound. One needs an additional theorem excluding near-alignment:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

This is the same obstruction as before, just in a larger vector space.

---

# 3. Does the affine forcing equation forbid alignment?

No, not locally.

The equation

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

relates the derivative component of \(C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\) to local forcing. But the interaction side can still align both value and derivative components.

Formally, write

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=P_7+J_7.
\]

Then

\[
\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\nabla P_7+\nabla J_7.
\]

The aligned branch may satisfy

\[
J_7=-P_7+\varepsilon w_0,
\]

and simultaneously

\[
\nabla J_7=-\nabla P_7+\varepsilon w_1.
\]

Then

\[
(A_7,\nabla A_7)
=
\varepsilon(w_0,w_1).
\]

The forcing equation only says

\[
\nabla A_7=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

It does not prohibit

\[
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

from being small after pair/interaction cancellation unless one proves that the forcing lies in a cone or transverse subspace unavailable to the interaction term.

No such cone or transversality theorem is currently available.

---

# 4. Cone separation attempt

A possible route would be:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in \mathcal C_P,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in \mathcal C_J,
\]

with cones satisfying

\[
\mathcal C_P\cap (-\mathcal C_J)=\{0\}.
\]

Then alignment would be impossible.

But the present architecture gives no such cones. In particular:

1. \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is sign-indefinite through

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2
\right].
\]

2. \(E_{\rm line}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) can point along the reference line.

3. \(E_{\rm bg/core}\) is fixed analytic forcing, but not sign-controlled.

4. The rank-two fibre is complex two-dimensional; without a positivity or reality cone, “opposite direction” is always locally available in the vector model.

Therefore cone separation does not follow from the rank-two formalism.

A cone theorem would have to be an additional arithmetic/geometric input, not a formal consequence of affine transport.

---

# 5. Incidence-containment attempt

Another route would be to prove:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}.
\]

But near-cancellation is not the same as exact incidence. Exact cancellation gives analytic equations:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=0.
\]

Near-cancellation gives inequalities:

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\|<\Lambda.
\]

Analytic incidence controls zero sets; it does not automatically control how close an actual zeta path may approach them. To turn incidence into a lower bound, one needs a quantitative separation theorem, e.g. a Łojasiewicz/Remez-type inequality with constants compatible with height \(Q\).

The local analytic fact would be:

\[
\mathrm{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr})^\mu
\lesssim
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)\|.
\]

But this gives a lower bound only if one already has a lower bound for

\[
\mathrm{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}).
\]

That is an arithmetic or dynamical separation input. The current framework does not provide it.

Thus incidence containment alone is insufficient.

---

# 6. Scale incompatibility attempt

One could hope that the pair part and interaction part live at incompatible \(Q\)-scales. For example:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\asymp Q^{-\alpha},
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\asymp Q^{-\beta},
\qquad
\alpha\ne\beta.
\]

Then cancellation would be impossible at leading scale.

But the Bottleneck-C analysis repeatedly shows matched same-scale terms. The active row itself is a same-grade source-Hessian effect. The interaction machinery was built precisely because pair and interaction contributions can appear at the same finite-core scale.

Transport does not change this scale matching. It differentiates or transports the same finite-core data; it does not separate pair and interaction orders by default.

So scale incompatibility is not currently available.

A viable theorem would need to show that after transport, one component has a leading \(Q\)-order absent from the other side. I see no such component in the present ledger.

---

# 7. Łojasiewicz / analytic lower-bound route

The most plausible rigorous route is a quantitative analytic inequality.

Let

\[
F(\theta)=C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)
\]

on a compact reduced stratum. Since \(F\) is analytic and not identically zero, one has a local Łojasiewicz inequality near the zero set:

\[
\|F(\theta)\|
\ge
C\,\mathrm{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z(F))^\mu.
\]

But the constants \(C,\mu\), and more importantly the distance of the actual zeta point \(\theta(m)\) from \(\mathcal Z(F)\), are not controlled.

Thus the theorem one would actually need is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{dist}\bigl(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}\bigr)
\ge
Q^{-A}
}
\]

for some controlled exponent \(A\). Then one could obtain

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|
\ge
Q^{-A\mu}C.
\]

This is the correct analytic shape of a transported non-concentration theorem. But it is a major new arithmetic/geometric input.

Without such a separation theorem, transported non-concentration remains open.

---

# 8. Interaction feature obstruction persists

The transported feature curve would be

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)
=
(v_{\rm value}(u),v_{\nabla}(u),\ldots).
\]

Balanced amplitudes satisfy only

\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]

To annihilate the \(dd\)-interaction term, one would need

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)=0.
\]

For all balanced \(a\), this is equivalent to

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\rm tr}(u_k).
\]

A generic transported feature curve is not constant. The countermodel survives:

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w,
\]

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\qquad
a=(1,-2,1),
\]

giving

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)=2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

So transported data do not supply feature balance.

---

# 9. Spectral cone obstruction persists

For a unit transported feature curve,

\[
\langle v_{\rm tr}(u),v_{\rm tr}(u)\rangle=1,
\]

the \(dd\)-kernel expansion still has

\[
\kappa_4
=
-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\]

and

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

The sign of

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
\]

is uncontrolled.

The unit curve

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)
=
(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

still violates the desired sign for

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}.
\]

Thus transported finite-core data do not automatically produce spectral positivity.

---

# 10. No-go statement

**Proposition — Transported finite-core data do not imply non-concentration.**  
Let \(V_{\rm tr}\) be the finite-dimensional transported fixed-sector data space. Suppose the only local information is that

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\]

is analytic and not identically zero outside incidence. Then no positive lower bound

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)\|
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q)
\]

follows. For any nonzero \(p,w\in V_{\rm tr}\), the analytic family

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=p,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=-p+\varepsilon w
\]

has

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=\varepsilon w,
\]

which is nonzero for \(\varepsilon\ne0\) but arbitrarily small. Therefore a transported finite-core lower bound requires an additional theorem excluding near-alignment, such as cone separation, incidence-distance lower bounds, arithmetic separation, boundary control, or holonomy/index constraints.

---

# 11. What theorem should be attacked next?

The most precise next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Transported incidence-distance theorem.}
}
\]

A viable statement would be:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{dist}\bigl(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on the reduced visibility-positive base. Together with analytic Łojasiewicz/Remez bounds, this would imply

\[
\boxed{
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|
\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

for some \(B\).

Alternatively, one can attack a stronger cone theorem:

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\notin -\mathcal C_J
}
\]

for an interaction cone \(\mathcal C_J\), but no such cone is currently visible.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transported finite-core non-concentration remains open-negative.}
}
\]

The affine forcing equation is valuable because it gives a canonical transported vector, but it does not itself prevent

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

A proof-closing theorem must supply one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative distance from transported incidence,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{cone separation between pair and interaction contributions,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical boundary/holonomy constraints,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{an arithmetic lower bound preventing near-cancellation.}
}
\]

Absent one of these, the rank-two affine transport route is locally coherent but globally non-closing.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 20:54:20)
