_Thought for 38s_

# Agent 5 — Cone / Positivity Agent with Actual Geometry

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No usable cone theorem follows from the current actual packet geometry.}
}
\]

The rank-two local theory gives real structure, visibility, and affine forcing, but it does **not** produce a sign cone or positivity cone strong enough to rule out

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

The decisive obstruction is not merely abstract complex linear algebra. It already appears in the actual off-line packet geometry: the non-centered order-seven \(K_1\) visibility channel changes sign when the sampling midpoint crosses the packet center. Thus the pair contribution itself occupies both orientations of the same rank-two direction on nearby reduced good patches. A pointed cone containing all actual packet contributions would have to contain both \(v\) and \(-v\), so it is not a separating cone.

This matches the current handover’s strategic diagnosis: the local rank-two theory survives, but the global proof gate is still quantitative non-concentration / incidence separation, not a formal cone argument. 

---

## 1. Candidate cone theorem

The desired theorem would be something like:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in \mathcal C_P,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\in \mathcal C_J,
\qquad
\mathcal C_P\cap(-\mathcal C_J)=\{0\}.
\]

Then

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\]

could not be arbitrarily small unless both terms were small or the point entered a controlled incidence set.

But the available rank-two geometry does not give such cones. The transported finite-core vector lives in a complex rank-two fixed-sector bundle, and the actual visible packet channel is sign-reversible under legitimate midpoint motion.

---

## 2. Actual packet sign reversal kills a naive cone

For the paired off-line packet

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

with

\[
a=\frac12-\delta,\qquad b=\frac12+\delta,\qquad \delta\ne0,
\]

the non-centered order-seven channel satisfies near the packet center

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3),
\qquad x_m=2m-\gamma.
\]

Since

\[
a^{-9}+b^{-9}>0,
\]

the sign of the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel flips with the sign of \(x_m\). The draft now treats \(m\) as a sampling midpoint, not as a forced packet center, so \(x_m\) is a legitimate local parameter on the reduced base.

Thus, for the same off-line packet and the same canonical core stratum, nearby reduced good patches can produce

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim +cI
\]

and

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim -cI
\]

up to the same nonzero \(K_1\)-transport factor.

Therefore any cone \(\mathcal C_P\) meant to contain all actual packet pair contributions must contain both \(I\) and \(-I\), at least locally. Such a cone cannot separate pair contributions from negative interaction contributions.

This is a genuine actual-geometry obstruction to cone positivity.

---

## 3. Centered one-whitening-slot channel also lacks fixed sign

The centered visibility channel is

\[
L_7
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

Here

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\]

\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\]

and

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

For a centered off-line packet,

\[
q''=2A_2\ne0,
\]

so \(y\) and \(B\) are nonzero outside incidence. But the sign and phase of \(L_7\) still depend on

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}),
\]

i.e. on the leading Gram anisotropy

\[
g-h.
\]

The condition

\[
g=h
\]

is an incidence wall, but crossing it reverses the \(I\)-component orientation. Since \(g\) and \(h\) include the background/core phase data, no fixed sign is available without imposing an additional one-sided Gram-anisotropy convention. The current proof does not have such a convention.

So the centered route also fails to produce a natural positivity cone.

---

## 4. Stieltjes / positivity structure does not survive the fixed-sector construction

One might hope that the zero-source terms

\[
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
\]

give a positive kernel or moment cone. At the raw scalar level, there are useful sign patterns. For example, at \(x=0\),

\[
A_2<0,\qquad A_4>0,\qquad A_6<0.
\]

But the fixed-sector coefficient is not a raw moment. It is obtained after:

\[
\text{finite-}s\text{ two-point expansion},
\]

\[
\text{mixed-block algebra},
\]

\[
\text{whitening},
\]

\[
\text{fixed-sector projection},
\]

and, in the rank-two route,

\[
\text{covariant transport}.
\]

These operations combine moments with Gram anisotropy, endpoint orientation, and mixed-block skew carriers. The visible channel

\[
-2yBr\,I
\]

already contains products of source curvature, Gram inverse-square-root derivatives, and a skew mixed block. It does not preserve a simple Stieltjes positivity sign.

Thus raw positivity of source kernels is insufficient for a cone theorem.

---

## 5. Interaction side remains too flexible

Even if one imposed an oriented cone on the pair part by choosing, for instance,

\[
x_m>0,
\]

the interaction side still has no corresponding cone restriction.

The aligned branch is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr},
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

The interaction feature obstruction remains:

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)=0
\]

for all balanced amplitudes would require

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\rm tr}(u_k).
\]

A generic transported feature curve does not satisfy this. The local model

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w,
\]

with

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\qquad
a=(1,-2,1),
\]

gives

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\rm tr}(u_i)=2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

So the interaction contribution can still create directions not controlled by ordinary amplitude balance. No actual-zeta symmetry currently forces the transported feature curve to be constant or one-sided.

---

## 6. Spectral-cone positivity still fails

For a unit transported feature curve,

\[
\langle v_{\rm tr}(u),v_{\rm tr}(u)\rangle=1,
\]

the local interaction kernel expansion has

\[
\kappa_4
=
-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle,
\]

but

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac1{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

The sign of

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
\]

is not controlled by rank-two transport.

The unit curve

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)
=
(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

has

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle=a(6b-a^3).
\]

So for

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6},
\]

the sign goes the wrong way. This is not excluded by the current rank-two construction.

Thus spectral positivity is still absent.

---

## 7. Actual-geometry no-go model

A cone theorem would have to survive the following actual local behavior.

Take a nondegenerate off-line packet and a reduced good patch centered near it. Since \(m\) is a free sampling midpoint, choose two nearby midpoints

\[
m_\pm=m_0\pm\epsilon,
\qquad
x_{m_\pm}=\pm 2\epsilon.
\]

For sufficiently small \(\epsilon\), the same core remains selected and all reduced-good-patch inequalities persist. But

\[
q^{(7)}(m_+)\sim +C\epsilon,
\qquad
q^{(7)}(m_-)\sim -C\epsilon.
\]

Therefore the order-seven \(K_1\) contribution satisfies

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}(m_+)\sim +V,
\qquad
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}(m_-)\sim -V,
\]

for a nonzero fixed-sector vector \(V\), up to nonzero analytic transport factors.

Any cone containing the actual local pair contributions at both \(m_+\) and \(m_-\) contains \(V\) and \(-V\). It is therefore not pointed and cannot prevent cancellation with interaction terms.

This is the core no-go.

---

## 8. What a viable cone theorem would need

A cone theorem remains possible only if it introduces a new, non-formal zeta-specific restriction. For example:

### Option A — Oriented half-patch theorem

Restrict to a canonical orientation such as

\[
x_m>0
\]

and prove the proof never needs the opposite side. Then try to build a cone only on the oriented half-patch.

This would require a canonical choice of side tied to zeta geometry. None is currently present.

### Option B — Interaction transversality theorem

Prove that the interaction contribution cannot point opposite the pair contribution:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\notin -\mathcal C_P
\]

outside incidence.

This is essentially the transported finite-core non-concentration theorem in cone form. It is not currently known.

### Option C — Arithmetic sign theorem

Use an explicit formula, zero-density constraint, or packet symmetry to force a sign/phase condition on the transported interaction features.

No such theorem is currently in the draft.

### Option D — Quantitative incidence-distance theorem

Abandon cones and prove that the actual zeta path stays at distance at least

\[
Q^{-A}
\]

from the transported cancellation set. This remains the most plausible route.

---

## 9. Final no-go statement

**Proposition — No formal actual-geometry cone from order-seven packet visibility.**  
On a reduced good patch around an off-line packet, the order-seven \(K_1\) visibility channel is nonzero outside explicit incidence. However, because the sampling midpoint \(m\) is free and

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3),
\]

the same actual packet family realizes both signs of the visible \(K_1\)-direction on nearby reduced patches. Hence no pointed cone containing all actual packet pair contributions can be extracted from the current rank-two geometry. Therefore cone separation cannot be used to rule out

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
\]

without an additional orientation, arithmetic sign, interaction transversality, or incidence-distance theorem.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual-geometry cone route fails formally.}
}
\]

The order-seven visibility theorem supplies nonzero local directions, but those directions are sign-reversible under legitimate midpoint motion. Therefore they do not define a positivity cone.

The best remaining proof-closing target is not cone positivity. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative transported incidence separation}
}
\]

of the form

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

combined with a Łojasiewicz/Remez lower bound for

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

Absent that kind of theorem, the rank-two architecture remains locally coherent but globally non-closing.

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 20:59:31)

_Thought for 17s_

# Agent 5 — Replacement Invariant Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No replacement invariant currently avoids the aligned branch.}
}
\]

I tested the natural candidates:

\[
\|C\|^2,\quad
\|P\|^2-\|J\|^2,\quad
\omega(P,J),\quad
\omega(C,\nabla C),\quad
\text{projective curvature},\quad
\text{multi-scale determinants},\quad
\text{renormalized energies}.
\]

All remain vulnerable to the same adversarial family

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr},
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=-P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+\varepsilon W,
\]

with \(\varepsilon\) arbitrarily small. Some invariants detect *exact* cancellation or near-antiparallel alignment, but none converts that detection into a lower bound or contradiction without an additional zeta-specific theorem. This matches the current strategic state: local rank-two infrastructure is coherent, but the missing proof gate is quantitative incidence separation / arithmetic non-concentration. 

---

## 1. Setup

Let

\[
C:=C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
P+J
\]

be the transported finite-core vector, where \(P\) is the pair/local packet contribution and \(J\) is the interaction contribution.

The bad branch is

\[
J\approx -P.
\]

A replacement invariant must satisfy two conditions:

1. it must remain detectably nonzero when \(C=P+J\) is small because of near-cancellation;
2. it must be tied to RH strongly enough to yield a contradiction or a quantitative lower bound.

The adversarial model is

\[
P=p,
\qquad
J=-p+\varepsilon w,
\]

with \(p,w\neq0\), so

\[
C=\varepsilon w.
\]

This model preserves local nonzero visibility for \(P\), allows \(C\neq0\), and makes the total transported finite-core vector arbitrarily small.

---

# 2. Norm energy \(\|C\|^2\)

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal E_C=\|C\|^2.
\]

Under the adversarial branch,

\[
\mathcal E_C
=
\|\varepsilon w\|^2
=
|\varepsilon|^2\|w\|^2.
\]

This is positive for \(\varepsilon\neq0\), but arbitrarily small. It gives qualitative nonvanishing only, not a lower bound.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\|C\|^2\text{ detects exact zero but does not prevent near-cancellation.}
}
\]

This is not a proof gate.

---

# 3. Difference of energies \(\|P\|^2-\|J\|^2\)

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal E_{\Delta}
=
\|P\|^2-\|J\|^2.
\]

Under

\[
P=p,\qquad J=-p+\varepsilon w,
\]

we get

\[
\|J\|^2
=
\|-p+\varepsilon w\|^2
=
\|p\|^2
-2\operatorname{Re}\bigl(\varepsilon\langle w,p\rangle\bigr)
+
|\varepsilon|^2\|w\|^2.
\]

Hence

\[
\mathcal E_{\Delta}
=
2\operatorname{Re}\bigl(\varepsilon\langle w,p\rangle\bigr)
-
|\varepsilon|^2\|w\|^2.
\]

This is \(O(\varepsilon)\) and can vanish to first order by choosing

\[
\operatorname{Re}\langle w,p\rangle=0.
\]

It can also be made arbitrarily small.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\|P\|^2-\|J\|^2\text{ is not coercive.}
}
\]

It detects imbalance only if pair and interaction magnitudes are separated, which is exactly what remains unproved.

---

# 4. Wedge / determinant invariant \(\omega(P,J)\)

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal W(P,J)=\omega(P,J).
\]

Under the aligned branch,

\[
\omega(P,J)
=
\omega(p,-p+\varepsilon w)
=
\varepsilon\omega(p,w).
\]

Again this is \(O(\varepsilon)\). It vanishes for exact antiparallel cancellation and can be arbitrarily small for near-cancellation.

A normalized angle invariant,

\[
\frac{|\omega(P,J)|}{\|P\|\|J\|},
\]

detects the angle between \(P\) and \(J\), but near-cancellation is precisely the regime where the angle tends to \(\pi\), i.e. wedge tends to zero. So the determinant invariant confirms the bad branch rather than excluding it.

\[
\boxed{
\omega(P,J)\text{ is an alignment detector, not an alignment obstruction.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Projective invariant of \(C\)

Candidate:

\[
[C]\in \mathbf P(\mathcal F),
\]

or a projective winding relative to \([A_5]\),

\[
d\log \omega(C,A_5).
\]

Problem: if

\[
C=\varepsilon w,
\]

then

\[
[C]=[w]
\]

is independent of \(\varepsilon\). Projectivization discards the smallness that matters for non-concentration. It can detect direction, but the proof needs a quantitative lower bound for

\[
\|C\|.
\]

Also, projective invariants are undefined at exact cancellation \(C=0\), and near that point they become unstable rather than contradictory.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective invariants lose scale and cannot supply the needed lower bound.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Mixed projective-scale package

Candidate:

\[
([C],\|C\|).
\]

This is complete, but tautological. It is equivalent to keeping \(C\) itself. The scale component is still

\[
\|C\|=|\varepsilon|\|w\|,
\]

so the same near-cancellation problem remains.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective + scale is no stronger than the transported vector itself.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Curvature / Wronskian invariant \(\omega(C,\nabla C)\)

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal K
=
\omega(C,\nabla C).
\]

This is tempting because even if \(C\) is small, \(\nabla C\) might be nonzero.

But the adversarial branch can make value and derivative small simultaneously. Let

\[
C(t)=\varepsilon w(t).
\]

Then

\[
\nabla C(t)
=
\varepsilon \nabla w(t),
\]

and

\[
\omega(C,\nabla C)
=
\varepsilon^2\omega(w,\nabla w).
\]

So \(\mathcal K=O(\varepsilon^2)\).

A normalized curvature,

\[
\frac{\omega(C,\nabla C)}{\|C\|^2},
\]

may remain \(O(1)\), but it loses scale and becomes singular near \(C=0\). It does not imply

\[
\|C\|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\omega(C,\nabla C)\text{ does not prevent simultaneous value-derivative near-cancellation.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Multi-scale determinant

Candidate: sample transported data at several scales or midpoints,

\[
\det(C(m_1),C(m_2),\ldots),
\]

or in rank two,

\[
\omega(C(m_i),C(m_j)).
\]

Adversarial model:

\[
C(m)=\varepsilon w(m).
\]

Then

\[
\omega(C(m_i),C(m_j))
=
\varepsilon^2\omega(w(m_i),w(m_j)).
\]

Again the invariant is arbitrarily small.

A multi-scale determinant can detect rank variation of the residual, but not its magnitude. Without a lower bound on the residual scale, it does not solve the non-concentration problem.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{multi-scale determinants inherit the same small parameter.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Signed spectral invariant

Candidate: use the transported \(dd\)-kernel

\[
K_{dd}^{\rm tr}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v_{\rm tr}\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v_{\rm tr}\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle
\]

and extract a sign or negative-type invariant.

But the previous spectral obstruction survives:

\[
\kappa_4
=
-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\]

under unit normalization, while

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac1{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

The sign of

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
\]

is uncontrolled. The unit curve

\[
v_{\rm tr}(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

has

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle=a(6b-a^3),
\]

which changes sign depending on \(b\). The actual packet geometry does not presently impose the needed sign condition.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the spectral invariant still lacks a sign theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Renormalized residual ratio

Candidate:

\[
R=\frac{\|C\|}{\|P\|+\|J\|}.
\]

Under

\[
P=p,\qquad J=-p+\varepsilon w,
\]

we get

\[
R
\sim
\frac{|\varepsilon|\|w\|}{2\|p\|}.
\]

This precisely measures the near-cancellation. It is useful diagnostically, but the desired theorem is exactly a lower bound

\[
R\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So the invariant does not avoid the missing theorem; it names it.

---

# 11. Strongest possible replacement: pair-interaction angle plus scale

The most informative package is

\[
\left(
\|P\|,
\|J\|,
\frac{\omega(P,J)}{\|P\|\|J\|},
\|P+J\|
\right).
\]

But this still allows

\[
\|P\|\asymp\|J\|,
\qquad
\frac{\omega(P,J)}{\|P\|\|J\|}\approx0,
\qquad
P+J\approx0.
\]

To exclude this, one needs either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{angle cannot approach }\pi
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{magnitudes cannot match}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{near-antiparallel matching implies incidence.}
}
\]

None follows from the current local formalism.

---

# 12. Conclusion: no invariant replacement, only reformulation

Every candidate falls into one of three classes:

1. **Invariant of the total residual \(C\):**  
   vulnerable because \(C=\varepsilon w\) can be arbitrarily small.

2. **Invariant of the pair \((P,J)\):**  
   detects near-antiparallel alignment but does not forbid it.

3. **Projective/normalized invariant:**  
   loses scale and cannot yield the lower bound required for RH.

Therefore the replacement-invariant search does not bypass the main obstruction.

\[
\boxed{
\text{The missing theorem remains quantitative non-concentration.}
}
\]

---

# 13. The theorem that would actually help

The useful theorem should be stated directly:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Together with a Łojasiewicz/Remez inequality,

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)\|
\ge
c\,\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta,
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)^\mu,
\]

this would give

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|
\ge
Q^{-B}.
\]

Alternatively, one could prove directly:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
Q^{-B}.
}
\]

But no replacement invariant avoids the need for such a theorem.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Replacement invariant route: failed as a formal bypass.}
}
\]

The best diagnostics are:

\[
\omega(P,J),
\qquad
\frac{\|P+J\|}{\|P\|+\|J\|},
\qquad
\omega(C,\nabla C),
\qquad
\text{multi-scale determinants}.
\]

But none supplies a lower bound without an additional zeta-specific quantitative theorem.

So the next mathematical attack should not search for another invariant. It should attack:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative incidence-distance / arithmetic non-concentration}
}
\]

for the actual zeta transported finite-core path.

# Agent 5 — New Invariant Under Midpoint Sign Reversal

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{I do not find a replacement invariant that survives midpoint sign reversal and also closes the global gate.}
}
\]

The sign reversal

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3)
\]

means the visible local packet contribution changes orientation when \(x_m\mapsto -x_m\). Any invariant robust under

\[
V\mapsto -V
\]

must be even/projective/energy-like. Such invariants can detect that a local packet exists, but they either lose the scale needed for non-concentration, are not observables of the total transported finite-core vector, or remain vulnerable to the same near-cancellation branch. This matches the attached strategic update: the remaining gate is quantitative zeta-specific separation from transported cancellation incidence, not another formal invariant. 

---

## 1. The sign-reversal obstruction

Near a nondegenerate off-line packet center,

\[
V(x_m):=A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
c\,x_m\,e+O(x_m^2),
\qquad c\ne0,
\]

for some local fixed-sector direction \(e\). Hence

\[
V(-x_m)=-V(x_m)+O(x_m^2).
\]

So any pointed cone argument fails: the same packet family realizes both \(e\) and \(-e\) on nearby legitimate reduced patches.

A replacement invariant must therefore be even under sign:

\[
\mathcal I(V)=\mathcal I(-V).
\]

The problem is that even invariants tend to measure magnitude but not prevent cancellation in the **total** transported vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}=P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

---

## 2. Squared norm / energy

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_1(V)=\|V\|^2.
\]

This is robust under \(V\mapsto -V\). For the packet channel,

\[
\|V(x_m)\|^2
=
|c|^2x_m^2\|e\|^2+O(x_m^3),
\]

so it detects a non-centered packet.

But the proof does not observe the pair contribution alone. It observes

\[
C=P+J.
\]

Under the adversarial aligned branch,

\[
P=V,\qquad
J=-V+\varepsilon W,
\]

we get

\[
C=\varepsilon W,
\qquad
\|C\|^2=|\varepsilon|^2\|W\|^2.
\]

Thus energy of the total residual remains arbitrarily small. Energy of \(P\) alone is positive, but that is not a contradiction unless one proves that interaction cannot cancel it.

\[
\boxed{\|V\|^2\text{ is sign-robust but not cancellation-robust.}}
\]

---

## 3. Projective invariant \([V]\)

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_2(V)=[V]\in \mathbf P(\mathcal F).
\]

This identifies

\[
V\sim \lambda V,
\]

so \(V\) and \(-V\) have the same projective class.

But projectivization discards scale. If

\[
C=\varepsilon W,
\]

then

\[
[C]=[W]
\]

is well-defined for \(\varepsilon\ne0\), independent of how small \(\varepsilon\) is. The RH gate needs a lower bound like

\[
\|C\|\ge Q^{-B},
\]

not merely a direction.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective invariants solve sign reversal by throwing away the quantity that must be bounded.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Symmetric two-sided midpoint invariant

Since \(V(-x)=-V(x)+O(x^2)\), try the two-sided energy

\[
\mathcal I_3(x)
=
\|C(x)\|^2+\|C(-x)\|^2.
\]

If only the packet contribution existed,

\[
C(x)=V(x),\qquad C(-x)=V(-x),
\]

then

\[
\mathcal I_3(x)
=
2|c|^2x^2\|e\|^2+O(x^3),
\]

which is positive.

But the interaction contribution can cancel on both sides:

\[
J(x)=-V(x)+\varepsilon W(x),
\]

\[
J(-x)=-V(-x)+\varepsilon W(-x).
\]

Then

\[
C(x)=\varepsilon W(x),
\qquad
C(-x)=\varepsilon W(-x),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal I_3(x)=O(\varepsilon^2).
\]

So two-sided symmetrization does not defeat aligned cancellation.

---

## 5. Odd-difference invariant

Try to exploit the oddness:

\[
\mathcal I_4(x)
=
C(x)-C(-x).
\]

For the packet alone,

\[
V(x)-V(-x)=2cx\,e+O(x^2),
\]

so this restores a signed signal.

But with aligned interactions,

\[
C(x)=\varepsilon W(x),
\qquad
C(-x)=\varepsilon W(-x),
\]

so

\[
\mathcal I_4(x)
=
\varepsilon(W(x)-W(-x)).
\]

Again it can be arbitrarily small.

If one instead applies \(\mathcal I_4\) to the pair contribution \(P\) alone, it is nonzero, but the global proof sees \(P+J\), not \(P\) in isolation.

---

## 6. Wedge between two midpoints

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_5(x)
=
\omega(C(x),C(-x)).
\]

For the packet alone,

\[
V(-x)\approx -V(x),
\]

so

\[
\omega(V(x),V(-x))\approx \omega(V,-V)=0.
\]

Thus the wedge between the two symmetric pair signals is actually a poor invariant: the leading terms are collinear.

If one perturbs to nonsymmetric midpoints \(x_1,x_2\), then

\[
V(x_1)\approx c x_1 e,\qquad V(x_2)\approx c x_2 e,
\]

still collinear to leading order. The wedge sees curvature or higher-order changes, not the main packet signal.

And if using the total residual,

\[
C=\varepsilon W,
\]

then all such wedges scale like \(\varepsilon^2\).

So:

\[
\boxed{\omega(C(x_1),C(x_2))\text{ is not a robust packet detector at leading order.}}
\]

---

## 7. Pair-interaction angle invariant

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_6(P,J)
=
\frac{|\omega(P,J)|}{\|P\|\|J\|}.
\]

This is sign-insensitive and detects non-parallelism. But near-cancellation is precisely near-antiparallel alignment:

\[
J=-P+\varepsilon W.
\]

Then

\[
\omega(P,J)=\varepsilon\omega(P,W),
\]

so

\[
\mathcal I_6(P,J)=O(\varepsilon).
\]

It diagnoses the bad branch by becoming small, but it does not forbid it.

A theorem saying

\[
\mathcal I_6(P,J)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

would be useful, but that is exactly a quantitative transversality theorem. It is not supplied by the invariant itself.

---

## 8. Difference of energies

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_7(P,J)=\|P\|^2-\|J\|^2.
\]

Under

\[
J=-P+\varepsilon W,
\]

we get

\[
\|J\|^2
=
\|P\|^2
-
2\operatorname{Re}\varepsilon\langle W,P\rangle
+
O(\varepsilon^2),
\]

so

\[
\mathcal I_7
=
2\operatorname{Re}\varepsilon\langle W,P\rangle+O(\varepsilon^2).
\]

This can be made arbitrarily small, and even vanish to first order by taking

\[
\operatorname{Re}\langle W,P\rangle=0.
\]

So energy difference is not coercive.

---

## 9. Determinant of pair and derivative

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_8(P)=\omega(P,\nabla P).
\]

This is robust under \(P\mapsto -P\), because

\[
\omega(-P,-\nabla P)=\omega(P,\nabla P).
\]

But for the leading packet branch

\[
P(x)=cx\,e+O(x^2),
\]

we have

\[
\nabla_xP=ce+O(x),
\]

so

\[
\omega(P,\nabla P)
=
\omega(cx e,ce)+O(x^2)=O(x^2).
\]

The leading one-dimensional packet direction gives zero wedge. This invariant detects curvature of the packet direction, not the primary visible signal.

For total residual \(C=\varepsilon W\),

\[
\omega(C,\nabla C)=O(\varepsilon^2).
\]

Again not proof-closing.

---

## 10. Multiscale norm packet

Candidate:

\[
\mathcal I_9
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^L
\|C(x_\ell)\|^2
\]

for a fixed set of nearby midpoints \(x_\ell\).

If the interaction can align at one point only, multiscale sampling might help. But the current formalism does not restrict \(J(x)\) enough to prevent

\[
J(x_\ell)=-P(x_\ell)+\varepsilon W_\ell
\]

for finitely many sample points. That is exactly the finite-core aligned branch in multiscale form.

A multiscale invariant becomes useful only with a rigidity theorem saying the interaction term cannot interpolate the negative pair signal at all sampled points. That theorem is not currently available.

---

# 11. What kind of invariant could work?

A replacement invariant would need to be one of the following.

## Option A — Observes \(P\) separately and proves \(P\) cannot be cancelled

But observing \(P\) separately does not prove RH unless one proves interaction cancellation impossible. This reduces to the same non-concentration problem.

## Option B — Uses a nonlinear functional where \(F(P+J)\) is not small even if \(P+J\) is small

That is impossible for continuous \(F\) with \(F(0)=0\). If the RH-compatible state corresponds to zero residual, any continuous invariant of the total residual must be small near cancellation.

## Option C — Singular/projective invariant near \(C=0\)

Projective invariants may blow up or oscillate near \(C=0\), but they lose the scale needed for a quantitative contradiction. They also become undefined at exact cancellation.

## Option D — Arithmetic invariant of actual zeta zeros

This remains possible, but it is not a formal rank-two invariant. It would be a genuinely zeta-specific non-concentration theorem.

---

# 12. Conclusion

The sign reversal

\[
V(x)\mapsto -V(x)
\]

forces any robust local invariant to become even/projective/energy-like. Those invariants detect local packet presence, but they do not prevent the total transported finite-core vector from being arbitrarily small through

\[
P+J\approx0.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{replacement-invariant route fails as a formal bypass.}
}
\]

The only viable next theorem is still quantitative:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge Q^{-B},
}
\]

or equivalently a transported incidence-distance estimate

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Any invariant that helps must be in service of proving that estimate; it cannot replace it.

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:06:45)

_Thought for 15s_

# Agent 5 — Quantitative Separation Attempt

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{I cannot prove }|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ from the current local/rank-two framework.}
}
\]

Even if \(\Phi_{\rm align}\) is made explicit, the local theory gives only analytic non-identity. It does **not** give a quantitative lower bound along the actual zeta zero path. The minimal missing input is a zeta-specific arithmetic separation theorem saying that the actual transported finite-core configuration cannot approach the alignment incidence set faster than a fixed power of \(Q\). This matches the attached strategic diagnosis: the next phase must attack one explicit transported alignment coordinate quantitatively, not search for another invariant or local Bottleneck-C repair. 

---

# 1. The target coordinate

Take an explicit transported alignment coordinate of the form

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta)
=
\ell\!\left(
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)
\right)
=
\ell\!\left(
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta)
\right),
\]

where \(\ell\) is a fixed coordinate functional in a chosen local rank-two frame.

Typical candidates are:

\[
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

\[
\omega_h(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

or one component of

\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots).
\]

The desired estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|
\ge
Q^{-A}
}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

---

# 2. What analyticity gives

On a fixed reduced stratum, after excluding pole collisions, Gram singularities, visibility walls, and core-boundary walls, the coordinate

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta)
\]

is analytic, or meromorphic with denominators bounded away from zero.

If

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}\not\equiv0,
\]

then its zero set

\[
Z_\Phi=\{\Phi_{\rm align}=0\}
\]

is a proper analytic incidence set.

A Łojasiewicz inequality gives a local bound

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta)|
\ge
c\,\operatorname{dist}(\theta,Z_\Phi)^\mu.
\]

On a compact reduced chart, this can be patched into a finite inequality.

But this only reduces the problem to:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),Z_\Phi)\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for the actual zeta configuration \(\theta(m)\).

The current framework does not supply that distance estimate.

---

# 3. Why qualitative nonzero is insufficient

A qualitative theorem

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))\neq0
\]

does not imply a useful lower bound.

An actual trajectory can satisfy

\[
0<|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(Q))|<e^{-Q}
\]

while never entering the incidence set. This would defeat any polynomial estimate

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Therefore, proving

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\neq0
\]

or

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}\not\equiv0
\]

is not enough. The RH-scale proof needs quantitative separation from the transported cancellation locus.

---

# 4. The aligned-branch obstruction

Write

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}
=
\Phi_P+\Phi_J,
\]

where \(\Phi_P\) is the pair/local packet contribution and \(\Phi_J\) is the interaction contribution.

The bad branch is

\[
\Phi_J\approx-\Phi_P.
\]

Even if \(\Phi_P\) is visibly nonzero, for example from the order-seven \(K_1\)-channel, an interaction contribution can formally satisfy

\[
\Phi_J=-\Phi_P+\varepsilon.
\]

Then

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}=\varepsilon.
\]

The local rank-two framework does not prevent \(\varepsilon\) from being exponentially small in \(Q\).

So the desired theorem is not merely nonvanishing of \(\Phi_P\). It is anti-alignment:

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_P+\Phi_J|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Pilot coordinate: \(q^{(7)}\) is easier but not enough

For the isolated off-line packet,

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3).
\]

If one can choose

\[
|x_m|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then the isolated packet contribution is polynomially large.

But the actual core quantity is not just the isolated packet contribution:

\[
q_{\core}^{(7)}(m)
=
f_{\beta,\gamma}^{(7)}(m)
+
R_{\core}^{(7)}(m).
\]

The rest of the core/background can in principle satisfy

\[
R_{\core}^{(7)}(m)
=
-f_{\beta,\gamma}^{(7)}(m)+\varepsilon.
\]

Then the total \(q_{\core}^{(7)}\) can be arbitrarily small.

Thus \(q^{(7)}\) is a useful pilot incidence function, but it does not solve the transported alignment problem unless one proves a lower bound for the full sum.

---

# 6. What an explicit formula could and could not do

If \(\Phi_{\rm align}\) were a **linear zero statistic**, then one could try to construct a test function \(\varphi\) so that

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}
\approx
\sum_\rho \varphi(\rho).
\]

Then an explicit formula might convert it to a prime-side expression.

But the transported finite-core coordinate involves nonlinear operations:

\[
\text{core selection},
\quad
\text{finite jet products},
\quad
G_\pm^{-1/2},
\quad
\pi_{\mathfrak f},
\quad
\text{transport},
\quad
\text{pair/interaction decomposition}.
\]

These operations make \(\Phi_{\rm align}\) a nonlinear analytic function of the zero packet, not a simple linear statistic.

A multi-level expansion could in principle express products of zero statistics, but it would still need a sign, positivity, or non-cancellation principle on the prime side. No such principle is currently visible.

Thus the explicit formula may help compute \(\Phi_{\rm align}\), but it does not automatically give the lower bound.

---

# 7. Minimal missing theorem

The clean missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Transported incidence-distance theorem.}
}
\]

For the actual zeta finite-core path \(\theta(m)\), there exist constants \(A>0\) and \(Q_0\) such that for all \(Q\ge Q_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge
Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, for a finite list of transported incidence functions

\[
\Phi_1,\ldots,\Phi_M,
\]

one needs

\[
\boxed{
\max_j|\Phi_j(\theta(m))|
\ge
Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Then analytic Łojasiewicz/Remez inequalities could convert this into

\[
\boxed{
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Without this theorem, transported non-concentration remains open.

---

# 8. Why standard zero facts do not give it

Standard zero information gives:

\[
N(T+H)-N(T)
\]

on average, zero-density estimates, functional equation symmetry, and broad log-derivative control.

It does not give polynomial separation of a finite-dimensional analytic zero-configuration coordinate from an arbitrary transported incidence variety.

Even zero simplicity, if assumed, would only say zeros do not collide. It would not imply

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Likewise, pair symmetries give relations, but they can also make cancellations more plausible. They do not prevent near-alignment.

So the missing theorem is not a standard consequence of known zeta zero distribution facts. It is closer to a Diophantine/non-concentration statement for local zeta zero configurations.

---

# 9. Possible sharper target

Rather than attack the full transported vector first, pick a single coordinate:

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}
=
\omega_h(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]

or

\[
\Phi_{\rm align}
=
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Then try to prove:

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

under the reduced-base exclusions.

If this fails, determine whether the failure is due to:

1. cancellation by another packet;
2. interaction terms;
3. Gram/whitening nonlinearities;
4. core selection instability;
5. lack of arithmetic separation among zeros.

This would make the global obstruction concrete.

---

# 10. Conditional theorem if a distance bound is assumed

If one assumes the transported incidence-distance theorem, then the route works at the level of finite-core non-concentration.

Precisely, suppose:

1. \(C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\) is analytic on a compact reduced stratum;
2. \(C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\not\equiv0\);
3. the actual zeta path satisfies

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\theta(m),
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\right)
\ge
Q^{-A};
\]

4. the relevant Łojasiewicz exponent is \(\mu\).

Then

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|
\ge
cQ^{-A\mu}.
\]

This would give the desired polynomial lower bound with

\[
B=A\mu+O(1).
\]

So the architecture is conditionally viable if and only if the quantitative separation theorem is supplied.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The quantitative separation theorem is the minimal missing arithmetic input.}
}
\]

I cannot prove

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}(\theta(m))|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

from the current local architecture, nor from qualitative analytic nonvanishing, nor from standard zero-distribution facts.

The next useful attack should choose one explicit \(\Phi_{\rm align}\), expand it fully in zero-packet variables, and test whether any zeta-specific arithmetic input can prove

\[
|\Phi_{\rm align}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Until such a theorem is found, the rank-two framework remains locally coherent but globally non-closing.

_Thought for 8s_

# Agent 5 — Quantitative lower-bound attempt for \(\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}\)

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ reduces to three missing polynomial-separation bounds: }
|y|,\ |q''|,\ |g-h|.
}
\]

The algebra is clean. The scalar admits an explicit lower-bound reduction:

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\,\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
\]

Thus, if

\[
|y|\ge Q^{-a},\qquad |q''|\ge Q^{-b},\qquad |g-h|\ge Q^{-c},
\]

and

\[
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|\ge C Q^{-(a+b+c+4d)}.
}
\]

But the key point is negative: the current framework proves none of the three lower bounds

\[
|y|\ge Q^{-a},\qquad |q''|\ge Q^{-b},\qquad |g-h|\ge Q^{-c}
\]

for actual zeta data outside exact incidence. These are precisely quantitative incidence-distance assumptions. The weakest visible link is still the Gram anisotropy factor \(g-h\). The attached instruction explicitly identifies this scalar as the locked coordinate and asks Agent 5 to reduce the lower bound to exact missing arithmetic conditions. 

---

## 1. Algebraic reduction

Start with

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\,
\frac{q''(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2})}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}.
\]

Use

\[
g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}
=
\frac{\sqrt h-\sqrt g}{\sqrt{gh}}
=
\frac{h-g}{\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt h+\sqrt g)}.
\]

Then

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\,
\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\,
\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
=
\frac{|y|\,|q''|\,|g-h|}
{4\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

This is the exact lower-bound factorization.

---

## 2. Denominator control

Assume good-patch positive Gram bounds

\[
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d.
\]

Then

\[
gh\le Q^{2d},
\]

and

\[
(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2
\le
(2Q^{d/2})^2
=
4Q^d.
\]

Hence

\[
4\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2
\le
16\pi Q^{3d}.
\]

This gives the sharper bound

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
\ge
\frac{1}{16\pi}
|y|\,|q''|\,|g-h|\,Q^{-3d}.
}
\]

If one uses a coarser symmetric denominator bound, one may write

\[
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
\gg
|y|\,|q''|\,|g-h|\,Q^{-4d},
\]

but \(3d\) is enough under the displayed assumptions.

Thus if

\[
|y|\ge Q^{-a},
\qquad
|q''|\ge Q^{-b},
\qquad
|g-h|\ge Q^{-c},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
\gg
Q^{-(a+b+c+3d)}.
}
\]

A safe statement is

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
\ge C Q^{-(a+b+c+4d)}.
}
\]

---

## 3. What the factors mean

Recall

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right).
\]

Therefore

\[
g-h
=
\frac1\pi\left(
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right).
\]

The Gram-isotropy wall is

\[
g=h
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

The scalar is therefore controlled by the product

\[
\boxed{
y\cdot q''\cdot
\left(q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''\right).
}
\]

The denominator is harmless on a good positive Gram patch. The numerator is the real issue.

---

## 4. Leading packet substitution

At the leading centered packet level,

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

Thus

\[
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2})}
{288\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}.
\]

Using the same identity,

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^2q''(h-g)}
{288\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

For a centered distinguished packet,

\[
q''=2A_2,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^3(h-g)}
{144\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

Therefore, for the isolated packet contribution, a sufficient lower bound is

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-a_0},
\qquad
|A_2|\ge Q^{-a_2},
\qquad
|g-h|\ge Q^{-c},
\qquad
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1,\lead}^{(7,I)}|
\gg
Q^{-(a_0+3a_2+c+3d)}.
}
\]

But for actual zeta data, \(A_2,q'',g,h,y\) are full-core quantities, not just the distinguished packet’s isolated contribution.

---

## 5. Status of each needed assumption

### Assumption 1: \(Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d\)

This is the least problematic. It is a good-patch/Gram-control assumption. Since

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right),
\]

positive Gram nondegeneracy already requires

\[
g>0,\qquad h>0.
\]

Polynomial upper/lower control is plausible if the local phase jets are bounded at the working \(Q\)-scale. But it should be recorded as an analytic good-patch bound, not assumed silently.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{locally plausible / should be part of good-patch quantitative hypotheses.}
}
\]

---

### Assumption 2: \(|q''|\ge Q^{-b}\)

This is not proved globally.

For the isolated centered off-line packet,

\[
q''_P=2A_{2,P},
\]

and

\[
A_{2,P}=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3})\ne0.
\]

So the distinguished packet contribution is nonzero.

But actual core data contain rest/background contributions:

\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R.
\]

A cancellation

\[
q''_R\approx -q''_P
\]

is not forbidden by the local rank-two framework.

Thus the needed statement is:

\[
\boxed{
|q''_P+q''_R|\ge Q^{-b}
}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

That is an arithmetic/non-concentration input.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{globally missing.}
}
\]

---

### Assumption 3: \(|y|\ge Q^{-a}\)

At leading packet level,

\[
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

So if

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-a_0},
\qquad
|A_2|\ge Q^{-a_2},
\]

then

\[
|y_{\rm lead}|\ge Q^{-(a_0+2a_2)}.
\]

But again, \(y\) in the full coordinate is not merely the isolated packet leading term. It may receive rest/core/mixed contributions:

\[
y=y_P+y_R+y_{\rm mix}.
\]

The local framework does not prevent

\[
y_R+y_{\rm mix}\approx -y_P.
\]

So the actual missing statement is

\[
\boxed{
|y_P+y_R+y_{\rm mix}|\ge Q^{-a}
}
\]

outside incidence.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{globally missing.}
}
\]

---

### Assumption 4: \(|g-h|\ge Q^{-c}\)

This is the most vulnerable factor.

Since

\[
g-h
=
\frac1\pi\left(
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right),
\]

the wall is

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Nothing in the current architecture gives a sign or lower bound for

\[
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''.
\]

Moreover, unlike \(A_2\) or \(q''\), this factor mixes slope and curvature of the full phase. It is easy to imagine rest/background contributions tuning it close to zero while preserving

\[
g>0,\qquad h>0.
\]

The needed statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right|
\ge Q^{-c}.
}
\]

This is a quantitative Gram-anisotropy separation theorem.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{globally missing and likely the weakest link.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Minimal sufficient theorem

A sufficient theorem for this coordinate is:

**Pilot \(K_1\)-coordinate lower-bound theorem.**  
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), suppose there exist constants

\[
a,b,c,d>0
\]

such that

\[
|y|\ge Q^{-a},
\qquad
|q''|\ge Q^{-b},
\]

\[
\left|
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right|
\ge Q^{-c},
\]

and

\[
Q^{-d}\le
\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\quad
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
\le Q^d
\]

with both Gram factors positive. Then

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
\ge C Q^{-(a+b+c+3d)}
}
\]

for an absolute constant \(C>0\), after adjusting constants for \(\pi\).

This theorem is algebraically immediate. The missing work is proving the hypotheses for actual zeta data.

---

## 7. Minimal missing arithmetic condition

The weakest single compressed condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|y\,q''\,(g-h)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on the actual reduced zeta configuration.

In expanded phase-jet form:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
y\,q''
\left(
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If one substitutes leading packet data,

\[
y\sim -\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\]

then the condition becomes approximately

\[
\boxed{
\left|
q_0A_2^2q''
\left(
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

For a centered isolated packet with \(q''=2A_2\),

\[
\boxed{
\left|
q_0A_2^3
\left(
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac13A_2
\right)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But the actual theorem must be for the full-core quantities, not the isolated packet.

---

## 8. Can this be proved from current exclusions?

The current exclusions are exact incidence walls:

\[
y\ne0,
\qquad
q''\ne0,
\qquad
g\ne h.
\]

They imply only

\[
yq''(g-h)\ne0.
\]

They do **not** imply

\[
|yq''(g-h)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A point can avoid all three walls while satisfying

\[
0<|yq''(g-h)|<e^{-Q}.
\]

So the current visibility-positive base is qualitative. To support an RH proof, it must be upgraded to a quantitative visibility-positive base, e.g.

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,{\rm quant}}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\{|yq''(g-h)|<Q^{-A}\}.
\]

But then one must prove actual zeta data land in this quantitative base. That is the hard arithmetic problem.

---

# Final answer

The lower-bound problem for the locked scalar reduces exactly to:

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
=
\frac{|y|\,|q''|\,|g-h|}
{4\pi\,g h(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}.
}
\]

With polynomial Gram bounds

\[
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d,
\]

one gets

\[
\boxed{
|\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}|
\gg
|y|\,|q''|\,|g-h|\,Q^{-3d}.
}
\]

Therefore the minimal sufficient assumptions are:

\[
\boxed{
|y|\ge Q^{-a},\quad
|q''|\ge Q^{-b},\quad
|g-h|\ge Q^{-c},\quad
Q^{-d}\le g,h\le Q^d.
}
\]

The minimal missing arithmetic condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|yq''(g-h)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\left|
y\,q''
\left(
q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''
\right)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This condition is not proved by the current local rank-two framework. It is the exact quantitative non-concentration theorem needed for the pilot coordinate.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:14:44)

_Thought for 13s_

# Agent 5 — Quantitative Good-Patch Geometry Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The upgrade }
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ is conditionally reachable, but not justified by the current framework.}
}
\]

Qualitative avoidance of the wall

\[
g-h=0
\]

is easy once \(m\) is a free sampling midpoint. Quantitative avoidance is different. To prove that every RH-relevant off-line packet reaches

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,\mathrm{quant}}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\cap\{|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\},
\]

one needs a Remez/Cartan-type lower-bound theorem for the analytic function

\[
G(m):=g(m)-h(m)
=
\frac1\pi\left(q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''\right)
\]

on the admissible sampling interval, with polynomial control of interval length, analytic complexity, and at least one non-tiny coefficient/derivative. None of that is currently proved. The attached instruction correctly identifies \(g-h\) as the current weak factor in the locked scalar \(\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}\). 

---

# 1. Qualitative reach is not the issue

On the reduced base, the exact wall is

\[
g=h
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

If \(G(m)=g(m)-h(m)\) is not identically zero on an admissible midpoint interval \(I\), then the set

\[
\{m\in I:G(m)=0\}
\]

is discrete or lower-dimensional. So one can choose \(m\) with

\[
G(m)\ne0.
\]

This gives qualitative visibility. It does not give

\[
|G(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The latter is the actual RH-scale requirement.

---

# 2. What midpoint freedom gives

Let \(I_\rho\) be the admissible midpoint interval for a fixed off-line packet \(\mathcal P(\rho)\), after imposing:

\[
d_k<d_{k+1},
\]

same-scale bounds,

endpoint separation,

Gram positivity,

and packet visibility walls other than \(g=h\).

If \(I_\rho\) contains an interval of length

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

and \(G\) has a simple zero in \(I_\rho\) with derivative

\[
|G'(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M},
\]

then choosing

\[
|m-m_0|\asymp Q^{-(A+M)}
\]

gives

\[
|G(m)|\gtrsim Q^{-A},
\]

provided the chosen \(m\) remains inside \(I_\rho\). So midpoint freedom can produce quantitative separation **if** the admissible interval is polynomially wide and \(G\) is not too flat.

But neither condition is currently established.

---

# 3. Simple-zero avoidance is insufficient

Suppose \(G(m_0)=0\) and \(G'(m_0)\ne0\). Locally,

\[
G(m)=G'(m_0)(m-m_0)+O((m-m_0)^2).
\]

If

\[
|G'(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M},
\]

then polynomial escape is available. But if

\[
|G'(m_0)|\le e^{-Q},
\]

then even a polynomial offset may leave

\[
|G(m)|\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus simple zero is not enough. We need a quantitative transversality condition:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le j\le J}|G^{(j)}(m_*)|\ge Q^{-M}
}
\]

for some controlled point \(m_*\) in the admissible region and bounded \(J\).

This is a new analytic/arithmetic input.

---

# 4. Whole-interval smallness is possible without a lower-bound theorem

Even if \(G\not\equiv0\), it may satisfy

\[
0<\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|G(m)|<e^{-Q}.
\]

That would avoid the exact wall but miss every polynomial lower bound.

The local rank-two framework does not exclude this. It only excludes exact incidence:

\[
G=0.
\]

So the quantitative good-patch upgrade requires more than analytic nonvanishing.

---

# 5. Remez/Cartan route

A plausible theorem would be:

**Quantitative Gram-anisotropy reach theorem.**  
Let \(G(m)=g(m)-h(m)\) be analytic on a complex neighborhood \(U\) of an admissible real interval \(I_\rho\). Suppose:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

\[
\sup_U |G|\le Q^M,
\]

and

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|G(m)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
\]

Then there exists \(m\in I_\rho\) such that

\[
|G(m)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
\]

This is tautological at the last step, but the real use of Remez/Cartan is stronger: if \(G\) is bounded above and has finite analytic complexity, then the set where

\[
|G(m)|<Q^{-A}
\]

cannot occupy all of \(I_\rho\) unless \(G\) is itself tiny on a larger complex neighborhood. One then needs a non-tiny coefficient, derivative, or value to rule that out.

A useful version would be:

\[
\boxed{
\exists j\le J,\quad |G^{(j)}(m_*)|\ge Q^{-M}
}
\]

plus complex-neighborhood control. Then polynomial separation follows on some subinterval.

The missing piece is exactly the derivative/coefficient lower bound.

---

# 6. Can the good-patch definition simply require \(|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\)?

One can define

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,\mathrm{quant}}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\cap
\{|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\}.
\]

This is mathematically clean. But reach becomes a new hypothesis:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every RH-relevant off-line packet admits a reduced patch in }
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,\mathrm{quant}}.
}
\]

Without proving this, the definition may exclude exactly the packets one needs to detect.

So the quantitative upgrade is acceptable as a bookkeeping device, but not as a proof step.

---

# 7. Same-scale/core-gap restrictions can obstruct quantitative escape

Even if \(G\) has polynomially good points nearby, the admissible interval may be very small. The available midpoint window is limited by:

\[
d_k<d_{k+1},
\]

same-scale inequalities,

endpoint separation,

Gram positivity,

and visibility walls.

If the admissible interval length satisfies only

\[
|I_\rho|\ll e^{-Q},
\]

then one may not have room to move polynomially far from a \(g=h\) wall. The current framework does not provide a lower bound

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}.
\]

Thus quantitative Gram-anisotropy reach also depends on quantitative reduced-base reach.

The needed combined hypothesis is:

\[
\boxed{
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}
\quad\text{and}\quad
G\text{ is not }e^{-Q}\text{-flat on }I_\rho.
}
\]

---

# 8. Could \(G\) be freely tuned?

At the level of local jet variables,

\[
G
=
\frac1\pi\left(q_0-\frac13q_0^3-\frac16q''\right).
\]

The wall is

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

There is no local obstruction to tuning \(q''\) close to this value while keeping

\[
g>0,\qquad h>0.
\]

For example, one can set

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon
\]

with

\[
\varepsilon=e^{-Q},
\]

and then

\[
g-h=-\frac{\varepsilon}{6\pi}.
\]

As long as \(q_0>0\) and the resulting \(h>0\), the Gram block remains positive. This shows that any lower bound must use actual zeta constraints, not local jet geometry alone.

---

# 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quantitative upgrade: conditionally reachable / not justified.}
}
\]

It is conditionally reachable under these hypotheses:

\[
\boxed{
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I_\rho}|G|\ge Q^{-M}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\max_{j\le J}|G^{(j)}(m_*)|\ge Q^{-M},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
G\text{ has controlled analytic complexity on a polynomial-size complex neighborhood.}
}
\]

It is not justified because none of these is currently proved for actual zeta data.

---

# 10. Exact missing theorem

The needed theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quantitative Gram-anisotropy reach theorem.}
}
\]

For every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet that reaches \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), there exists an admissible sampling midpoint \(m\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\left|
q_0(m)-\frac13q_0(m)^3-\frac16q''(m)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|g(m)-h(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

A stronger but more usable sufficient theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho}
\left|
q_0(m)-\frac13q_0(m)^3-\frac16q''(m)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for a polynomial-size admissible interval \(I_\rho\).

---

# Final answer

The reduced good-patch definition **can** be upgraded to include

\[
|g-h|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but only as a conditional quantitative base:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,\mathrm{quant}}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\cap\{|g-h|\ge Q^{-A}\}.
\]

The current proof does not show that every RH-relevant off-line packet reaches this base.

The exact missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remez/Cartan-type lower bound for }g-h
\text{ on the admissible sampling interval, with zeta-controlled coefficients.}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m\in I_\rho:
\left|
q''(m)-6q_0(m)+2q_0(m)^3
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Until that theorem is proved, the locked scalar

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
\]

remains diagnostically useful but not proof-closing.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:20:51)

# Agent 5 — Ambient \(D\)-Sector Feasibility Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The ambient \(D\)-sector route is locally viable, but it is a major architecture rebuild and not proof-closing by itself.}
}
\]

At the Gram-isotropy wall \(g=h\), the centered order-7 fixed-sector \(I\)-component dies because \(r=0\), but the ambient anti-fixed component survives:

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yB p\,D,
\qquad
p=g^{-1/2}.
\]

So the signal has not vanished; it has moved out of

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S
\]

and into the anti-fixed sector. This means the centered order-7 failure is not a total loss of local packet information. But using it requires replacing the rank-two fixed-sector bundle with at least a rank-four ambient block bundle

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\oplus\mathbf C D\oplus\mathbf C J.
\]

A rank-three bundle \(\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\oplus\mathbf C D\) is not safely closed. The \(J\)-sector appears naturally in the mixed-block carrier and under multiplication, so excluding \(J\) would create artificial projection problems. The attached instruction frames this as Branch C: use the surviving anti-fixed \(D\)-component if order 9 does not rescue the rank-two fixed-sector route. 

---

# 1. The surviving \(D\)-component

The centered one-whitening-slot term is

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

Write

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

Then

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_0-X_0YX_{-,1}.
\]

Using

\[
SJ=-D,
\qquad
JS=D,
\]

one gets

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yB(pD+rI).
\]

The rank-two fixed-sector projection keeps only

\[
-2yBr\,I.
\]

On the Gram-isotropy wall

\[
g=h,
\]

we have

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2})=0,
\qquad
p=g^{-1/2}\neq0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
T_7^{(1)}\big|_{g=h}
=
-2yBg^{-1/2}D.
}
\]

If

\[
y\neq0,
\qquad
B\neq0,
\qquad
g>0,
\]

then this is nonzero.

Thus the local order-7 packet signal survives at \(g=h\), but outside the fixed sector.

---

# 2. Minimal enlargement

The natural matrix basis is

\[
I=
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
S=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]

\[
D=
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
-1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The rank-two fixed-sector bundle uses

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

The killed complement is

\[
\mathfrak a_h=\mathbf C D\oplus\mathbf C J.
\]

The \(D\)-sector signal arises from

\[
S\cdot J
\quad\text{and}\quad
J\cdot S.
\]

So any enlargement that keeps \(D\) but discards \(J\) is unstable: \(J\) is the carrier that produces \(D\). Therefore the clean ambient object is the full local \(2\times2\) block algebra

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_b
=
\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b\oplus\mathbf C D_b\oplus\mathbf C J_b.
}
\]

A rank-three bundle

\[
\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\oplus\mathbf C D
\]

may work for a single projected coefficient after calculation, but it is not a natural invariant bundle for the algebra.

---

# 3. Transition/functoriality status

The full ambient corrected block bundle is more natural than the fixed-sector subbundle. If the local corrected kernel block transforms functorially, then the full \(2\times2\) coefficient space transforms by conjugation or by the induced raw-frame/whitening transition.

So, locally, the ambient bundle is plausible:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
}
\]

with fibre

\[
\mathcal A_b=\mathrm{Mat}_{2}(\mathbf C)
\]

or its corrected local block representation.

However, the same old caveat remains: source/core transitions are still excluded. The ambient enlargement does not solve source/core non-functoriality. It only avoids the fixed-sector projection losing the \(D\)-component.

Thus the ambient route is coherent only under the same fixed reduced-core convention:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed core, fixed whitening branch, no source/core transitions.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Does whitening preserve the larger sector?

Yes, the full matrix algebra is stable under whitening:

\[
N\mapsto X_-NX_+.
\]

If

\[
X_\pm
\]

are arbitrary \(2\times2\) matrices in the same local block algebra, then

\[
X_-NX_+\in \mathrm{Mat}_2(\mathbf C).
\]

So the full rank-four ambient bundle is closed.

The rank-two fixed-sector subbundle is not closed under multiplication by arbitrary whitening variations; that is precisely why the \(J\)-carrier plus \(S\)-whitening variation can create \(D\) and \(I\) components. Enlarging to the full matrix bundle removes this projection artifact.

---

# 5. Packet visibility in the ambient sector

Packet visibility becomes easier locally.

At \(g=h\), the ambient coordinate

\[
\ell_D(T_7^{(1)})
\]

is

\[
\boxed{
\ell_D(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBg^{-1/2}.
}
\]

Using

\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\]

and setting \(g=h\), we get

\[
\sqrt{gh}=g,
\qquad
\sqrt g+\sqrt h=2\sqrt g,
\]

so

\[
B\big|_{g=h}
=
\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\ell_D(T_7^{(1)})\big|_{g=h}
=
-\frac{yq''}{4\pi g^2}.
}
\]

With

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\qquad
q''=2A_2
\]

for the centered packet, the leading ambient \(D\)-signal is

\[
\boxed{
\ell_D(T_7^{(1)})_{\rm lead}
=
\frac{q_0A_2^3}{144\pi g^2}.
}
\]

This avoids the multiplicative weak factor \(g-h\). Thus the ambient \(D\)-coordinate is locally stronger than the rank-two fixed-sector \(I\)-coordinate at Gram isotropy.

---

# 6. Does the affine forcing equation extend?

Formally, yes.

The rank-two connection was

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
\]

For the full ambient block bundle, the natural connection is simply

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_X^{\mathcal A}A
=
\Pi_{\mathcal A}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A),
}
\]

where \(\Pi_{\mathcal A}\) is projection to the full local \(2\times2\) block coefficient space. If \(\mathcal A\) is the full block fibre, \(\Pi_{\mathcal A}\) may be the identity on the relevant coefficient block.

Then one expects an affine forcing equation

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathcal A}A_7^{\mathcal A}
=
E_{\eta\eta}^{\mathcal A}
+
E_{\rm lower}^{\mathcal A}.
\]

This is formally easier than the fixed-sector equation because no \(I/S\) projection is throwing away \(D/J\) data.

But it is a new architecture. All prior \(E_{\rm lower}\), Gate A/B, visibility, and finite-core definitions would need to be lifted from

\[
\mathfrak f_h
\]

to

\[
\mathcal A_b.
\]

---

# 7. Does the global cancellation problem reappear?

Yes.

The ambient route rescues local visibility at \(g=h\), but it does not solve the global problem:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}+J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx0.
\]

Now the finite-core vector is larger:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathcal A}
=
(A_7^{\mathcal A},\nabla A_7^{\mathcal A},A_9^{\mathcal A},\ldots).
\]

The bad branch becomes

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathcal A}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\mathcal A}.
\]

There is no automatic cone or positivity theorem in the full matrix algebra. In fact, the full ambient space is even more flexible than the fixed-sector subspace.

So the ambient route avoids the specific \(g-h\) weak factor, but it does not avoid the need for quantitative anti-cancellation.

---

# 8. Compatibility with symmetry and RH contradiction

This is the major conceptual risk.

The fixed-sector \(\mathfrak f_h\) was selected because it corresponded to the intended symmetric/two-point fixed channel. The \(D\)-sector is anti-fixed under the projection

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
\begin{pmatrix}
a&b\\
c&d
\end{pmatrix}
\right)
=
\frac{a+d}{2}I+\frac{b+c}{2}S.
\]

The \(D\)-component records endpoint imbalance between the two diagonal directions. It may be meaningful local data, but the proof must establish that it is RH-relevant globally.

In particular, one must prove that a nonzero \(D\)-sector anomaly cannot be pure gauge, endpoint-orientation artifact, or cancelled by considering the swapped endpoint chart.

Endpoint swap may send

\[
D\mapsto -D
\]

depending on conventions. If so, the \(D\)-signal is orientation-odd. To use it globally, one needs either:

1. an oriented endpoint bundle; or
2. an orientation-invariant scalar such as \(\|D\|^2\); or
3. a signed transport law respecting swaps.

This is a significant additional burden.

---

# 9. Feasibility table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Requirement} & \text{Status} & \text{Obstruction} \\
\hline
\text{Local ambient fibre } \mathrm{Mat}_2(\mathbf C) & \text{viable} & \text{none locally} \\
\text{Closure under whitening} & \text{viable} & \text{full matrix algebra is closed} \\
\text{Fixed reduced-core atlas} & \text{conditional} & \text{same source/core caveat as rank two} \\
\text{Packet visibility at }g=h & \text{positive} & \ell_D=-yq''/(4\pi g^2)\ne0 \\
\text{Affine forcing extension} & \text{formally viable} & \text{requires full row-table lift} \\
\text{Endpoint-swap covariance} & \text{unclear} & D\text{ may be orientation-odd} \\
\text{RH relevance of }D & \text{unproved} & D\text{ may be gauge/artifact} \\
\text{Global non-concentration} & \text{not solved} & P+J\approx0\text{ survives} \\
\end{array}
\]

---

# 10. Comparison with the order-9 fixed-sector branch

Branch B asks whether

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{g=h}\neq0.
\]

If yes, the proof remains inside the rank-two fixed-sector architecture and avoids a major rebuild.

Branch C uses

\[
D
\]

at order 7. It is locally available now, but requires an ambient-sector architecture.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order 9 should be tested before committing to the ambient }D\text{-sector rebuild.}
}
\]

The \(D\)-sector is a fallback if order 9 also fails.

---

# 11. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ambient \(D\)-sector route: viable but major rebuild.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local signal: yes.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rank-two fixed-sector compatibility: no.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full ambient bundle feasibility: yes, conditionally.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global proof closure: still missing.}
}
\]

If pursued, the new local object should be

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\qquad
\mathcal A_b=\mathrm{Mat}_2(\mathbf C)
=
\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b\oplus\mathbf C D_b\oplus\mathbf C J_b.
}
\]

The next theorem would be an ambient analogue of the rank-two theorem:

\[
\nabla^{\mathcal A}A_7^{\mathcal A}
=
E^{\mathcal A}_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}^{\mathcal A}.
\]

But before rebuilding the architecture, one should compute

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{g=h}.
\]

If order-9 fixed-sector visibility survives, that route is strictly preferable.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:25:00)

I’ll treat this as the second-anisotropy incidence audit. The key question is whether the new order-9 wall \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) is genuinely independent of the old Gram-isotropy wall, or just the same obstruction one derivative later.

_Thought for 45s_

# Agent 5 — Second Anisotropy Incidence Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\text{ is a proper new incidence wall, but it is not easier to control quantitatively than }g-h=0.
}
\]

The order-9 route is a **local improvement** over the centered order-7 scalar because

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\not\Rightarrow\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

So order 9 can plausibly recover fixed-sector visibility on the first Gram-isotropy wall. However, as a global proof route it merely replaces the missing estimate

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

with the new missing estimate

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

At the level of local phase jets and finite \(\xi\)-like models, one can tune

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
0<|\Gamma_{G,2}|<e^{-Q}
\]

while preserving \(q_0>0\), \(g,h>0\), and \(g=h\) only approximately or exactly as desired. Thus \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is locally useful but not a proof-closing quantitative invariant by itself. The attached prompt identifies \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) as the new order-9 wall to audit. 

---

# 1. Definitions

The first Gram-isotropy functional is

\[
\Gamma_G
:=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

Since

\[
g-h
=
-\frac{1}{6\pi}\Gamma_G,
\]

the order-7 centered fixed-sector channel dies on

\[
\Gamma_G=0.
\]

The proposed order-9 survivor is controlled by the second anisotropy

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
:=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16 q^{(4)}.
}
\]

The candidate order-9 fixed-sector term is, schematically,

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yB(X_2)_D I,
\]

with

\[
(X_2)_D
\propto
\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

---

# 2. Does \(\Gamma_G=0\) imply \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\)?

No.

On the first Gram-isotropy wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\]

means

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Substitute this into \(\Gamma_{G,2}\):

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2)-\frac16q^{(4)}
\qquad
\text{on }\Gamma_G=0.
}
\]

Thus \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) imposes an additional condition:

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2).
}
\]

This is not implied by the first Gram-isotropy equation. It is a new fourth-jet incidence condition.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=0
\not\Rightarrow
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
}
\]

This is the core local reason order 9 is promising.

---

# 3. Centered packet check

For a centered packet

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

the center values are

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1},
\]

\[
q''=-8(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=384(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

For the clean packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\]

we get

\[
q_0=\frac{16}{3},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{14336}{27},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=\frac{31981568}{81}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
-\frac{2336}{9}
\neq0,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-\frac{12449792}{243}
\neq0.
\]

So the clean centered packet is not accidentally second-isotropic. Its second anisotropy is strongly nonzero.

This confirms that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is a genuine packet-visible fourth-jet channel.

---

# 4. Can \(\Gamma_G=0\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) be made tiny?

Yes, at the local jet level.

Take

\[
q_0=2.
\]

Then the first Gram-isotropy condition is

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3=12-16=-4.
\]

Let

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1.
\]

Now compute

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-3q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

With

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

this becomes

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
12-3\varepsilon_1-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Choose

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Therefore, for any desired small numbers \(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2\), including

\[
\varepsilon_1=0,
\qquad
0<|\varepsilon_2|<e^{-Q},
\]

one has

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
0<|\Gamma_{G,2}|<e^{-Q}.
\]

The Gram values are

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}=\frac2\pi>0,
\]

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac83-\frac23+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(2+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)>0
\]

for small \(\varepsilon_1\).

Thus Gram positivity survives.

This shows that neither

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\]

nor good-patch positivity prevents

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

from being exponentially small.

---

# 5. Is this compatible with finite \(\xi\)-like models?

At the level of finite even Hadamard-type models, there are enough continuous parameters to tune the local jets

\[
q_0,\qquad q'',\qquad q^{(4)}
\]

independently to first order, unless an additional zeta-specific constraint is imposed.

The model class has parameters such as:

\[
\mu,\qquad \delta_j,\qquad \gamma_j,\qquad \text{packet weights or multiplicities}.
\]

The local jets are analytic functions of these parameters. With at least three independent local parameters, the map

\[
(\mu,\delta_j,\gamma_j,\ldots)
\mapsto
(q_0,q'',q^{(4)})
\]

is generically full rank. Then the implicit function theorem allows tuning

\[
\Gamma_G
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

simultaneously, while preserving open inequalities such as

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g>0,\qquad h>0.
\]

Therefore, absent a new arithmetic constraint, finite \(\xi\)-like models can realize

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
0<|\Gamma_{G,2}|<e^{-Q}.
\]

This makes \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) a proper incidence wall, but not a quantitatively protected one.

---

# 6. Is \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) generically nonzero?

Yes.

Because

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\]

involves the fourth phase jet \(q^{(4)}\), it is independent of the first wall

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

The first wall constrains \(q''\) relative to \(q_0\). The second wall constrains \(q^{(4)}\) relative to \(q_0\) and \(q''\). There is no structural reason in the current framework forcing both.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\text{ is codimension one relative to }\Gamma_G=0,
}
\]

at least in the local jet model.

This is why order 9 is a meaningful local escape.

---

# 7. Is a polynomial lower bound easier for \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) than for \(\Gamma_G\)?

No.

The same problem recurs one jet higher. The desired theorem would be:

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But the current framework only proves

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\]

outside an exact incidence wall. It gives no lower bound.

A trajectory can avoid the wall while satisfying

\[
0<|\Gamma_{G,2}|<e^{-Q}.
\]

Thus the order-9 route improves **qualitative local visibility** but does not solve the global quantitative non-concentration problem.

In short:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ is locally better than }\Gamma_G,
\text{ but globally the same type of obstruction.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Consequence for order 9

The order-9 fixed-sector route gives the following conditional local theorem:

\[
\boxed{
g=h,\quad yq''\ne0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
}
\]

provided the degree bookkeeping and row-cancellation audit confirm that

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
\subset A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

and that no other order-9 row cancels it identically.

This is a useful local theorem.

But the corresponding proof-scale theorem would require:

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or a combined layered lower bound such as

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The current framework proves neither.

---

# 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Second anisotropy condition: proper and useful locally, same quantitative difficulty globally.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=0\not\Rightarrow\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ is generically nonzero and supplies a plausible order-9 fixed-sector survivor.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A}\text{ is not easier than }|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ without new zeta-specific input.}
}
\]

---

# Final answer

The second anisotropy wall

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\]

is a genuine new wall, not a disguised copy of

\[
g-h=0.
\]

It makes order 9 locally promising because

\[
g=h
\]

does not force

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

However, it does not by itself solve the global lower-bound problem. Finite \(\xi\)-like models and local jet tuning can make

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
0<|\Gamma_{G,2}|<e^{-Q}
\]

while preserving

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g,h>0.
\]

Therefore the order-9 route should be pursued as a **local fixed-sector recovery mechanism**, but it does not eliminate the need for a quantitative non-concentration theorem. The next decisive local question is whether the candidate term

\[
-2yB(X_2)_D I
\]

really appears in

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

with no forced cancellation. If yes, the local rank-two route gains a layered visibility statement:

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}>0
\Longrightarrow
\text{order }7\text{ or order }9\text{ fixed-sector visibility.}
}
\]

But a proof of RH would still require the quantitative version

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or an equivalent zeta-specific incidence separation theorem.
