## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:35:39)

_Thought for a couple of seconds_

# Agent 5 — Layered Visibility and Quantitative Incidence

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order 9 gives a genuine local layered-visibility improvement, but not a global quantitative close.}
}
\]

The order-9 survivor changes the local picture materially:

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\not\Rightarrow\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

So the first Gram-isotropy wall that kills the centered order-7 fixed-sector scalar does **not** automatically kill the next fixed-sector channel. The local theorem should now be layered:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad \Gamma_G\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

and, conditionally on the order-9 row audit,

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad \Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

However, this is still a **local nonvanishing theorem**, not an RH-scale lower bound. The new global gate becomes

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

That quantitative theorem is not currently available. The attached instruction correctly frames Agent 5’s job as deciding whether order 9 gives only local visibility or also quantitative progress; the answer is: local visibility yes, quantitative progress not yet. 

---

## 1. First and second anisotropy

Define the first Gram-anisotropy functional

\[
\Gamma_G
:=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

Since

\[
g-h
=
-\frac{1}{6\pi}\Gamma_G,
\]

the centered order-7 fixed-sector channel

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-2yBr
\]

dies when

\[
\Gamma_G=0.
\]

The order-9 candidate introduces the second anisotropy

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
:=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The candidate term is

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1},
\]

and on \(g=h\) the previous round gave

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
}
\]

Thus the fixed-sector signal can reappear at order 9 if

\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0.
\]

---

## 2. Layered local visibility statement

The centered order-7 statement is:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad \Gamma_G\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

Indeed,

\[
\Phi_{K_1}^{(7,I)}
=
-y\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2},
\]

and

\[
h-g=\frac{\Gamma_G}{6\pi}.
\]

So the order-7 channel is nonzero when

\[
yq''\Gamma_G\neq0.
\]

On the wall

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\]

the order-7 fixed-sector component dies. The order-9 candidate gives:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad \Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

provided the term

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
\]

is indeed in the \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) row and not structurally cancelled by other order-9 rows.

So the layered local theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad
\left(\Gamma_G\neq0\ \text{or}\ \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0\right)
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\ \text{or}\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}>0
\Longrightarrow
\text{fixed-sector visibility by order }9.
}
\]

This is a real local improvement over relying on \(\Gamma_G\) alone.

---

## 3. Independence of the second wall

The first wall is

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Substitute this into \(\Gamma_{G,2}\):

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)(6q_0-2q_0^3)-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

So on \(\Gamma_G=0\),

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2)-\frac16q^{(4)}.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

requires the additional fourth-jet condition

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2).
}
\]

This is not implied by

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=0\not\Rightarrow\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
}
\]

At the level of local jet geometry, \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) is a new codimension-one condition inside the first wall, not a tautological consequence of it.

---

## 4. Centered packet test

For a centered packet

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad x=2t-\gamma,
\]

the relevant derivatives are

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1},
\]

\[
q''=-8(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=384(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

For the clean packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\]

one obtains

\[
q_0=\frac{16}{3},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{14336}{27},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=\frac{31981568}{81}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-\frac{12449792}{243}\neq0.
\]

So the second anisotropy is not only formally independent; it is concretely nonzero for the clean off-line packet model.

This supports the local order-9 escape.

---

## 5. Can finite \(\xi\)-like models make both small?

Yes, locally.

Take a local jet model with

\[
q_0=2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
q''+4.
\]

Set

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1.
\]

Now

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-3q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Substitute \(q''=-4+\varepsilon_1\):

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
12-3\varepsilon_1-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Choose

\[
q^{(4)}
=
72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Thus one can arrange

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\]

with

\[
0<|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|<e^{-Q}.
\]

The Gram values remain positive for small \(\varepsilon_1\):

\[
g=\frac{2}{\pi}>0,
\]

\[
h=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac83+\frac16(-4+\varepsilon_1)\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(2+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)>0.
\]

So, at the local finite-jet level, both anisotropies can be made exponentially small while preserving good-patch positivity.

This means order 9 does not solve the quantitative problem by itself.

---

## 6. Does order 9 give quantitative progress?

It gives **layered qualitative progress**, not a quantitative lower bound.

Previously, order 7 required

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

to protect the scalar.

Now one can hope for the weaker-looking layered bound

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is better locally because the failure set has higher codimension:

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

But for an actual zeta path, higher codimension does not automatically imply polynomial separation. The path may approach the intersection faster than any power of \(Q\). Analytic nonvanishing or codimension alone is insufficient.

Thus the quantitative theorem is still missing.

---

## 7. The right local theorem

The order-9 route should be formulated as the following local theorem.

**Layered fixed-sector visibility theorem, local form.**  
Assume the reduced good-patch conditions, centered parity, and

\[
yq''\neq0.
\]

Assume also that the order-9 row audit confirms

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}\subset A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

with no structural cross-channel cancellation. Then

\[
\Gamma_G\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
\]

while

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\quad
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}>0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\text{ or }
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

This is the correct local win.

---

## 8. The quantitative theorem still needed

For RH-scale use, one needs:

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

More fully, since the actual scalar includes factors

\[
y,\qquad q'',
\]

one needs something like

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\cdot
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Or separately:

\[
|y|\ge Q^{-a},
\qquad
|q''|\ge Q^{-b},
\]

\[
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-c}.
\]

The local framework supplies none of these polynomial lower bounds for actual zeta data.

So the global obstruction remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative layered anisotropy separation.}
}
\]

---

## 9. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order 9 gives local layered visibility.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order 9 does not yet give quantitative global non-concentration.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The new wall is proper and useful, but has the same arithmetic-separation difficulty.}
}
\]

The next local priority is to finish the order-9 row audit:

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
\subset A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\]

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I,
\]

and no structural cancellation.

If that audit closes, the next global theorem is no longer

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but the layered version

\[
\boxed{
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Potentially, this can then be extended to a finite anisotropy tower:

\[
\max_{j\le J}|\Gamma_{G,j}|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but that is the next conceptual layer, not yet proved.

# Agent 5 — Layered Visibility Theorem Finalizer

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local fixed-sector visibility theorem now has a clean layered form through order }9.
}
\]

The order-7 channel detects off the first Gram-isotropy wall

\[
\Gamma_G\neq0,
\]

and the order-9 channel detects on that wall provided the second anisotropy

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0.
\]

The theorem is local and conditional: it still depends on the order-9 row-table audit, specifically that the remaining \(I\)-sector rows do not structurally cancel the candidate

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

The current instruction identifies this as the next theorem to lock: a layered local theorem through order 9, with cross-channel incidence separated from source incidence. 

---

# Layered fixed-sector visibility through order 9

Define the first Gram anisotropy

\[
\Gamma_G
:=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

Since

\[
g-h=-\frac{\Gamma_G}{6\pi},
\]

the centered order-7 fixed-sector channel is controlled by \(\Gamma_G\). The order-7 live row is

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yBr\,I,
\]

with

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_7^{(1)}
=
-y\frac{q''(h-g)}
{4\pi gh(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^2}I.
\]

Thus, away from the basic source walls,

\[
yq''\neq0,
\]

the order-7 row is nonzero whenever

\[
\Gamma_G\neq0.
\]

Now define the second anisotropy

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
:=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

On the wall \(g=h\), the order-9 candidate row is

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1},
\]

and the previous audit gives

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

So the local order-9 escape is nonzero whenever

\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0.
\]

---

# Theorem-ready statement

**Theorem — Layered fixed-sector visibility through order 9.**  
Work on a centered reduced good patch in the current fixed-core convention. Assume the rank-two fixed-sector projection and whitening conventions are fixed, and assume

\[
g>0,
\qquad
h>0,
\qquad
yq''\neq0.
\]

Let

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Let \(\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}\) denote the order-7 cross-channel cancellation locus, and let \(\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}\) denote the order-9 cross-channel cancellation locus, defined by cancellation of the nonzero \(I\)-sector row in the full \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) coefficient.

Then, outside the corresponding cross-channel incidence walls,

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
}
\]

On the first Gram-isotropy wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

provided the order-9 row

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}
\right)
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I
\]

is not cancelled by the remaining order-9 \(I\)-sector rows.

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,\qquad
\theta\notin
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)},
\qquad
\left(\Gamma_G\neq0\ \text{or}\ \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0\right)
}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\neq0.
}
\]

---

# Exceptional sets

Separate the source-vanishing walls from the cross-channel walls.

The source/anistropy incidence through order 9 is

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm source}^{(7,9)}
:=
\{yq''=0\}
\cup
\{\Gamma_G=0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}=0\}.
\]

The order-7 cross-channel wall is

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}
:=
\left\{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})_{\rm total}=0
\ \text{despite}\ 
yq''\Gamma_G\neq0
\right\}.
\]

The order-9 cross-channel wall should be defined as follows. Let

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_9^I,
\]

where \(R_9^I\) is the sum of all other order-9 \(I\)-sector rows at \(g=h\). Then

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
:=
\left\{
R_9^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\quad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\right\}.
\]

The full layered visibility exceptional set is therefore

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm vis}^{(7,9)}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm source}^{(7,9)}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(7)}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}.
\]

Outside this set,

\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\neq0.
\]

---

# Why this is a real local improvement

The order-7 theorem alone fails on

\[
\Gamma_G=0.
\]

The order-9 theorem replaces that single wall by the smaller layered wall

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

And

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\]

does not imply

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

Indeed, substituting

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3
\]

into \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) gives

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2)-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

So \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) imposes the additional fourth-jet condition

\[
q^{(4)}
=
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2).
\]

That is a genuinely new local incidence condition.

---

# What remains unproved

There are four remaining dependencies.

## 1. Full \(R_9^I\) row computation

The theorem assumes the candidate row is not structurally cancelled. To remove the conditional phrasing, one must compute

\[
R_9^I
\]

explicitly and prove

\[
R_9^I
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\not\equiv0.
\]

Until this is done,

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
\]

is a defined cross-channel incidence wall, not a fully audited proper wall.

## 2. Properness of \(\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}\)

One must prove that \(\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}\) is proper, i.e. the cancellation equation is not an identity on the relevant reduced stratum.

## 3. Quantitative lower bound

For RH-scale use, qualitative visibility is insufficient. The needed quantitative form is something like

\[
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

outside cross-channel incidence. Equivalently,

\[
\|(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

This is not proved by the local theorem.

## 4. Reduced-base reach into layered visibility

One still needs to know that every RH-relevant off-line packet reaches a reduced patch outside

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm vis}^{(7,9)}.
\]

This is the layered version of the earlier non-swallowing problem.

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order 9 gives local layered visibility.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order 9 does not yet give quantitative global non-concentration.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The next local task is the full }R_9^I\text{ row computation and properness of }\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}.
}
\]

If that audit closes, the rank-two local visibility stack improves to:

\[
\boxed{
yq''\neq0,
\qquad
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}>0
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})\neq0
}
\]

outside explicit cross-channel walls.

The global theorem remains the quantitative layered anisotropy/non-concentration estimate

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

# Agent 5 — Properness Witness Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{A formal channel-level witness exists, but an actual reduced-core witness still needs the raw }N_7,N_5\text{ tables.}
}
\]

At the level of the universal order-9 channel algebra, the candidate row

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I
\]

is plainly not identically zero: choose formal data with

\[
g=h>0,\qquad y\neq0,\qquad q''\neq0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\neq0,
\]

and set the companion raw \(I\)-sector carriers \(N_7^{I,D},N_5^{I,D},\ldots\) to zero. Then

\[
F_9^I
=
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\neq0.
\]

This proves there is no **sector/parity/degree identity** forcing cancellation of the \(Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}\) row. However, it does **not** yet prove properness for the actual reduced-core zeta row, because \(N_7^{I,D}\), \(N_5^{I,D}\), and lower raw carriers may be algebraically linked to the same phase jets. The attached prompt specifically asks for this properness witness for \(F_9^I\), and the current answer is therefore: formal properness yes; actual reduced-core properness still conditional on computing the companion carrier coefficients. 

---

## 1. The candidate row

We are auditing

\[
F_9^I
:=
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The candidate contribution comes from

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,2}+X_{-,2}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1,
\]

with

\[
X_1=BS,\qquad Y=yJ,\qquad X_2=aI+dD.
\]

Then

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yBd\,I,
\]

and the previous constant computation gives

\[
-2yBd
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

---

## 2. Formal properness witness

Take formal channel data satisfying:

\[
g=h=1,
\qquad
y=1,
\qquad
q''=1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=1.
\]

Set all companion \(I\)-sector raw carriers to zero:

\[
N_7^I=N_7^D=N_5^I=N_5^D=0,
\]

and similarly set any lower-carrier \(I\)-sector companion families to zero.

Then

\[
R_9^I=0,
\]

while

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{1}{128\pi^2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
F_9^I
=
\frac{1}{128\pi^2}
\neq0.
\]

So the equation

\[
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\equiv0
\]

is **not** forced by matrix sector algebra alone.

This is enough to rule out the strongest possible cancellation claim:

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is no universal sector/parity identity cancelling the candidate row.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Why this is not yet an actual zeta witness

The formal witness treats the channels

\[
Y,\quad X_1,\quad X_2,\quad N_7,\quad N_5,\ldots
\]

as independently tunable.

In the actual reduced-core coefficient, they are not independent. They are all generated by the same underlying phase jets, Gram matrix, whitening expansion, and finite-\(s\) numerator. Thus it remains possible, in principle, that the actual formulas satisfy an identity of the form

\[
R_9^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\]

on the actual reduced-core image, even though this identity is not forced by abstract sector algebra.

That is why the missing computation is still real:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }N_7^{I,D},\quad N_5^{I,D},\quad \text{and lower \(I\)-sector companion rows.}
}
\]

Without those coefficients, we cannot certify actual properness of

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}.
\]

---

## 4. Can the clean centered packet serve as witness?

The clean centered packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34
\]

has

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\]

and nonzero source jets. That makes it a strong candidate for an actual witness.

But it does not by itself prove

\[
F_9^I\neq0,
\]

because \(R_9^I\) has not yet been evaluated for that packet.

To use the clean packet as a properness witness, we need one of the following:

### Option A

Show by parity/source structure that

\[
N_7^I=N_7^D=N_5^I=N_5^D=0
\]

for the clean centered packet. Then

\[
R_9^I=0
\]

for the dangerous companion families, and the candidate row proves

\[
F_9^I\neq0.
\]

### Option B

Compute the actual values of

\[
N_7^{I,D},\qquad N_5^{I,D},\qquad X_3,\qquad X_4,
\]

and verify numerically/symbolically that

\[
R_9^I
\neq
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

### Option C

Find a specialization of the actual local phase jets where the companion rows vanish but the candidate survives. This would be a true reduced-core witness.

At present, none of these has been completed.

---

## 5. Strongest current conclusion

The order-9 candidate is structurally independent in the following precise sense:

\[
\boxed{
Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}
}
\]

is a distinct channel label from the raw carrier companions

\[
N_9,\qquad N_7,\qquad N_5,\qquad \ldots
\]

The previous audits already found

\[
N_9^I=0,
\]

so \(N_9\) cannot cancel the candidate. The remaining danger is

\[
N_7^{I,D}
\]

and

\[
N_5^{I,D}
\]

through the formulas

\[
R_7^I
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D,
\]

and

\[
R_5^I
=
N_5^I(2pe-2bc+a^2+d^2)
+
N_5^D(2pf+2ad).
\]

These are cross-channel companion rows, not sector-forced cancellations.

Thus the right local theorem can already be stated modulo the incidence wall

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
R_9^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\quad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\right\}.
\]

But to prove this wall is proper on actual reduced-core data, we still need an actual witness.

---

## 6. Required next computation

The properness witness is blocked by exactly these missing pieces:

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I,\quad N_7^D,\quad N_5^I,\quad N_5^D,
}
\]

and, if the \(N_5\)-family is nonzero,

\[
\boxed{
(X_3)_S,\quad (X_4)_I,\quad (X_4)_D.
}
\]

The immediate next best target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }N_7^I\text{ and }N_7^D.
}
\]

Reason: \(N_7\) is the closest same-order companion to the candidate, and its row

\[
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D
\]

can directly contribute to the same \(I\)-coordinate.

If

\[
N_7^I=N_7^D=0
\]

by centered parity, the candidate becomes substantially more protected. If not, we need their exact source scalars.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Formal witness found: }F_9^I\not\equiv0\text{ in the universal channel algebra.}
}
\]

But:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual reduced-core witness not yet certified.}
}
\]

The order-9 cross-channel wall

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
\]

is not a sector/parity identity, but its properness on the actual zeta/reduced-core image requires computing the companion rows.

The exact missing coefficients are:

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I,\quad N_7^D,\quad N_5^I,\quad N_5^D
}
\]

with priority on

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I,\quad N_7^D.
}
\]

So the next agent push should compute the raw \(N_7\) \(I,D\)-components first.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 21:53:01)

# Agent 5 — \(N_7\)-Cancellation Consequence Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }N_7=F_7J,\text{ then the }N_7\text{-family is harmless for the order-9 }I\text{-row.}
}
\]

The current order-9 theorem is blocked only if the raw \(N_7\) carrier has a diagonal component:

\[
N_7^I\neq0
\quad\text{or}\quad
N_7^D\neq0.
\]

If Agents 1–4 prove the expected centered-parity result

\[
N_7=F_7J,
\]

then

\[
N_7^I=N_7^D=0,
\]

and the dangerous companion

\[
R_7^I[N_7]
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D
\]

vanishes identically. Then the order-9 local theorem moves past \(N_7\), and the next remaining terms are \(N_5^D\) and \(R_{\le4}^I\). This matches the attached instruction’s current diagnosis that \(N_7^{I,D}\) is the immediate blocker for the order-9 row theorem. 

---

# 1. Setup

The order-9 \(I\)-coordinate is

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
C_9^{\rm cand}
+
R_9^I,
\]

where

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The \(N_7\)-family contribution is

\[
R_7^I[N_7]
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
\]

Here

\[
X_0=pI,\qquad X_1=BS,\qquad X_2=aI+dD,
\]

and on the order-9 wall

\[
d=(X_2)_D\propto \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

So \(N_7^I\) and \(N_7^D\) have very different implications.

---

# 2. Case A: \(N_7^I=N_7^D=0\)

Then

\[
R_7^I[N_7]=0.
\]

This is the clean case. It occurs if the raw centered order-7 carrier is purely skew:

\[
N_7=F_7J.
\]

Then

\[
N_7^I=N_7^S=N_7^D=0,
\qquad
N_7^J=F_7.
\]

Since the \(J\)-component does not contribute to the \(I\)-coordinate through the \(N_7\)-family row under the displayed formula, the dangerous companion disappears.

The order-9 \(I\)-row reduces to

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
C_9^{\rm cand}
+
R_5^I[N_5]
+
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

Using the prior reduction \(N_5^I=0\), this becomes

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
N_5^D(2pf+2ad)
+
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

So if Agents 1–4 prove \(N_7=F_7J\), the next target is:

\[
\boxed{
N_5^D
\quad\text{and}\quad
R_{\le4}^I.
}
\]

---

# 3. Case B: \(N_7^I=0,\ N_7^D\neq0\)

Then

\[
R_7^I[N_7]
=
2pd\,N_7^D.
\]

Since

\[
d\propto\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

this term shares the same second-anisotropy factor as the candidate:

\[
R_7^I[N_7]
\propto
\Gamma_{G,2}N_7^D.
\]

The full candidate plus \(D\)-companion has the form

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}+R_7^I[N_7]
=
\Gamma_{G,2}
\left(
\frac{yq''}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
\kappa_7 N_7^D
\right),
\]

for the coefficient \(\kappa_7\) determined by \(2pd/d\).

This is cancellation-prone only if

\[
N_7^D
\]

is algebraically tied to

\[
yq''
\]

with exactly the opposite coefficient. That would be a real cross-channel identity, not a sector-forced cancellation.

So in Case B the order-9 theorem can still proceed, but the order-9 incidence wall must include

\[
\boxed{
\frac{yq''}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
\kappa_7 N_7^D
=0.
}
\]

This is less clean than Case A, but not fatal.

---

# 4. Case C: \(N_7^I\neq0\)

Then

\[
R_7^I[N_7]
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
\]

This is more dangerous because the \(N_7^I\)-term does **not** necessarily contain the factor

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Therefore it can contribute to the order-9 \(I\)-coordinate even when

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

This has two possible interpretations.

First, it may be helpful: if

\[
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I\neq0,
\]

then \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) may already be visible without needing \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). That would strengthen the order-9 theorem.

Second, it may be dangerous: if \(N_7^I\) is tied to other order-9 rows, it could participate in a more complicated cancellation not controlled by the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-layer.

So if \(N_7^I\neq0\), the theorem must be reformulated around the full order-9 \(I\)-row

\[
F_9^I
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I
+
2pd\,N_7^D
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_5^I+R_{\le4}^I.
\]

At that point, \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is no longer the sole order-9 anisotropy. The next task would be to compute \(N_7^I\) explicitly and determine whether it defines a new visibility channel or a cancellation channel.

---

# 5. Case table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{case} & \text{effect on }R_9^I & \text{theorem status} \\
\hline
N_7^I=N_7^D=0
&
R_7^I[N_7]=0
&
\text{best case; proceed to }N_5^D,R_{\le4}^I
\\
N_7^I=0,\ N_7^D\ne0
&
R_7^I=2pdN_7^D\propto \Gamma_{G,2}N_7^D
&
\text{cross-channel incidence; compute }N_7^D
\\
N_7^I\ne0
&
R_7^I\text{ has a term not necessarily proportional to }\Gamma_{G,2}
&
\text{major branch; compute }N_7^I\text{ explicitly}
\end{array}
\]

---

# 6. Consequence if \(N_7=F_7J\)

If Agents 1–4 prove

\[
N_7=F_7J,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I=N_7^D=0.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
R_7^I[N_7]=0.
}
\]

The order-9 row becomes

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_5^I[N_5]
+
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

If we also accept the prior result

\[
N_5^I=0,
\]

then

\[
R_5^I[N_5]
=
N_5^D(2pf+2ad).
\]

Thus the next exact target would be

\[
\boxed{
N_5^D.
}
\]

The layered theorem would then be close to lockable modulo

\[
N_5^D
\quad\text{and}\quad
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

---

# 7. Final recommendation

The \(N_7\)-audit has a simple decision tree.

If

\[
N_7=F_7J,
\]

then stop worrying about \(N_7\) and move to

\[
\boxed{
N_5^D.
}
\]

If

\[
N_7^D\neq0
\]

but

\[
N_7^I=0,
\]

then compute \(N_7^D\) and fold it into the order-9 cross-channel incidence wall.

If

\[
N_7^I\neq0,
\]

then \(N_7^I\) becomes the main object; it may either strengthen visibility or introduce a new cancellation identity.

So the exact next step depends on Agents 1–4, but the preferred outcome is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove }N_7=F_7J.
}
\]

That would clear the main current blocker and move the order-9 theorem to the \(N_5^D/R_{\le4}^I\) stage.

# Agent 5 — \(N_5^D\)-Cancellation Consequence Agent

## Verdict

\[

The current order-9 \(I\)-row is

where

=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

Thus \(N_5^D\) is now the only named medium-order companion between the candidate row and the lower-carrier remainder. If Agents 1–4 prove

\[
N_5=F_5J
\quad\text{or at least}\quad

\]

then the \(N_5\)-family vanishes from the order-9 \(I\)-coordinate, and the next target becomes only

\[
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

If \(N_5^D\neq0\), it is not automatically fatal. It becomes a cross-channel term unless it shares the exact source monomial of \(C_9^{\rm cand}\). The attached prompt identifies \(N_5^D\) as the current blocker after \(N_7\) was cleared.

# 1. Current row

After the \(N_7\)-audit, we have

\[

\qquad

The candidate row comes from the channel

# 2. Case A: \(N_5^D=0\)

Then

\[
R_5^I[N_5]=0.
\]

The row simplifies to

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
C_9^{\rm cand}
+
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

This is the best case.

If \(R_{\le4}^I\) is also zero or lower-incidence/cross-channel only, then the order-9 local theorem becomes lockable:

\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad

\]

outside the remaining lower-carrier cross-channel wall.

Thus, if Agents 1–4 prove

\[

the next exact target is

\[

# 3. Case B: \(N_5^D\neq0\), but independent of the candidate monomial

\[

\]

but its source content is independent of

\[

\[

=

\mathcal E_{\rm cc,5}^{(9)}

---

# 4. Case C: \(N_5^D(2pf+2ad)\) shares the same source monomial

The dangerous case is that

\[
N_5^D(2pf+2ad)
\]

contains exactly the same scalar

\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

with a fixed opposite coefficient.

Then the candidate plus \(N_5\)-row could structurally combine as

\[
\left(
\frac{1}{128\pi^2g^3}
+\kappa_5
\right)
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If

\[
\kappa_5=-\frac{1}{128\pi^2g^3},
\]

then the candidate cancels structurally.

This would be serious. But it requires an exact coefficient identity. It is not implied by sector algebra or parity.

The exact identity to test is:

\[
\boxed{
N_5^D(2pf+2ad)
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
}
\]

If this identity does not hold, then the \(N_5\)-row is either harmless or just part of the cross-channel incidence wall.

---

\[

&

&

\end{array}
\]

---

# 6. Consequence if \(N_5=F_5J\)

If Agents 1–4 prove

\[
N_5=F_5J,
\]

then

\[
N_5^D=0.
\]

Since the \(J\)-sector does not directly produce the \(I\)-coordinate through the already reduced \(N_5^D\)-formula, the \(N_5\)-family becomes harmless for this row.

Then

\[

=

+

}

The local theorem is then blocked only by \(R_{\le4}^I\), or by proving that \(R_{\le4}^I\) is a proper cross-channel incidence term rather than a structural cancellation.

---

# 7. Final recommendation

The \(N_5^D\)-audit has the same decision structure as the \(N_7\)-audit, but it is slightly more delicate because \(N_5\) is lower order and can interact with higher whitening coefficients.

The preferred result is:

\[
\boxed{
N_5=F_5J
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
N_5^D=0.
}
\]

If that holds, proceed immediately to

\[
\boxed{
R_{\le4}^I.
}
\]

If instead

\]

then compute \(N_5^D\) explicitly and test the identity

\[
\boxed{

+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
=0.
}
\]

Until \(N_5^D\) is known, the order-9 theorem remains locally promising but not fully locked.

# Agent 5 — Properness Witness for \(F_9^I\)

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Formal channel-level witness found; actual reduced-core witness still blocked by }R_{\le4}^I.
}
\]

After clearing \(N_9,N_7,N_5\), the order-9 \(I\)-row is

\[
F_9^I
:=
R_{\le4}^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

At the level of universal channel algebra, this is not identically zero: set the lower carriers and correction rows to zero while keeping \(yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\). But that does **not** certify actual reduced-core properness, because \(R_{\le4}^I\) may be forced by the same finite-\(s\) numerator/normalization data and could still satisfy an identity cancelling the candidate row. The attached instruction identifies \(R_{\le4}^I\) as the remaining blocker after \(N_9,N_7,N_5\) were cleared. 

---

## 1. Current row

The row is now

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
C_9^{\rm cand}
+
R_{\le4}^I,
\]

where

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The cleared rows are

\[
R_9^I[N_9]=0,
\qquad
R_7^I[N_7]=0,
\qquad
R_5^I[N_5]=0.
\]

Thus all remaining possible cancellation is in

\[
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

---

## 2. Formal witness

Take formal channel data

\[
g=h=1,
\qquad
y=1,
\qquad
q''=1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=1.
\]

Set all lower-carrier and correction-row contributions to zero:

\[
N_4=N_3=N_2=N_1=N_0=0,
\qquad
R_{\rm corr}^I=0.
\]

Then

\[
R_{\le4}^I=0,
\]

and therefore

\[
F_9^I
=
\frac{1}{128\pi^2}
\neq0.
\]

So the identity

\[
R_{\le4}^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\equiv0
\]

is not forced by the matrix channel

\[
Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}.
\]

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is no universal sector/parity identity cancelling the candidate row.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Why this does not yet prove actual properness

The formal witness treats

\[
N_4,N_3,N_2,N_1,N_0
\]

and the correction rows as freely nullable. In the actual reduced-core expansion, they are not independent; they are determined by the same phase jets, numerator convention, whitening expansion, and core/background subtraction.

So an actual identity could still exist:

\[
R_{\le4}^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\]

on the image of the true reduced-core construction, even though it is not a universal matrix-sector identity.

Thus the properness of

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
R_{\le4}^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\right\}
\]

is not yet certified for actual zeta/reduced-core data.

---

## 4. Clean packet witness attempt

The clean centered packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34
\]

is a good candidate because prior computations give

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\neq0.
\]

It also gives nonzero source quantities needed for the candidate row:

\[
y\neq0,
\qquad
q''\neq0.
\]

So

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}\neq0.
\]

However, without evaluating

\[
R_{\le4}^I
\]

for this same packet, we cannot conclude

\[
F_9^I\neq0.
\]

The clean packet becomes a true witness only after one of the following is shown:

\[
R_{\le4}^I=0,
\]

or

\[
R_{\le4}^I
\neq
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\]

for that packet.

At present, that check is blocked by the uncomputed lower-carrier/correction rows.

---

## 5. Exact blocker

The blocker is

\[
R_{\le4}^I
=
\sum_{b=0}^4
\pi_I
\sum_{a+c=9-b}
(-1)^cX_aN_bX_c
+
R_{\rm corr}^I.
\]

The immediate unknowns are the \(I\)-sector parts produced by

\[
N_4,\quad N_3,\quad N_2,\quad N_1,\quad N_0,
\]

plus any correction/normalization rows that were not included in the raw \(N_b\).

The dangerous possibility is a lower-carrier identity of the form

\[
R_{\le4}^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

No evidence currently suggests this identity, but it has not been excluded.

---

## 6. Properness status

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
F_9^I\not\equiv0
\text{ in the formal channel algebra.}
}
\]

But:

\[
\boxed{
F_9^I\not\equiv0
\text{ on the actual reduced-core image is still unproved.}
}
\]

The latter requires either:

1. an explicit computation of \(R_{\le4}^I\);
2. a clean centered-packet evaluation showing \(F_9^I\neq0\);
3. a structural proof that lower-carrier/correction rows cannot share the candidate scalar
\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

---

# Final recommendation

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proceed to the lower-carrier inventory for }R_{\le4}^I.
}

The next exact target should be:

\[

N_4,N_3,N_2,N_1,N_0
}

and the correction-row ledger.

The theorem is not lockable yet as an actual reduced-core statement. It is lockable only modulo the named incidence wall

=

R_{\le4}^I
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\right\}.

To prove that this wall is proper, we need either the full lower-carrier row table or a genuine clean-packet witness.

# Agent 5 — Background/Core and Normalization/Subtraction Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}+E_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
\text{ should be treated as cross-channel correction data, not as a structural cancellation of }
C_9^{\rm cand}.
}
\]

I do **not** see a sector/parity reason forcing these correction rows to equal

\[
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

However, unless the correction convention is explicitly separated from the raw \(N_b\)-table, these rows cannot be declared zero. The right local theorem should therefore be locked **modulo a correction incidence wall**

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\right\},
\]

unless Agents 1–4 prove all correction classes are absorbed/projected/closed. The attached instruction identifies this correction-row audit as the final remaining local caveat after the raw row table was cleared. 

---

# 1. Current reduced row

The raw carrier audit has cleared

\[
R_9^I[N_9]=0,\qquad
R_7^I[N_7]=0,\qquad
R_5^I[N_5]=0,\qquad
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{raw}}=0.
\]

So the order-9 \(I\)-coordinate is now

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
C_9^{\rm cand}
+
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}},
\]

where

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The only remaining issue is whether the non-raw correction remainder

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
\]

is zero/absorbed/projected, or whether it remains as a cross-channel analytic term.

---

# 2. Background/core rows

Background/core rows are generated by fixed baseline pieces such as

\[
q_{\core},\qquad B_{\bg},\qquad E_{\est,R},
\]

and by the reduced-core convention itself.

On the reduced base, the core/source convention is frozen. Therefore background/core rows are **fixed analytic data** on the reduced stratum. They are not source/core transition artifacts.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}
\text{ is either zero by parity/projection, or a fixed analytic cross-channel row.}
}
\]

It is not structurally tied to the \(Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}\) channel unless its explicit formula contains the same product

\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

No such identity is currently known.

So the safe classification is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}
\in R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
\quad
\text{as cross-channel analytic baseline data, if nonzero.}
}
\]

It is locally harmless only in the sense that it does not force cancellation. It still belongs in the correction incidence wall if it contributes to the \(I\)-coordinate.

---

# 3. Normalization/subtraction rows

Normalization/subtraction rows include:

\[
\text{finite-}s\text{ subtractions},
\]

\[
\text{diagonal renormalizations},
\]

\[
\text{affine source subtraction},
\]

and any correction used to define the corrected numerator before whitening.

These rows are more delicate than background/core rows because they may be constructed from the same jets that enter

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}.
\]

However, structurally they do not have the same channel label as the candidate unless they contain the exact mechanism

\[
Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}.
\]

The candidate comes from a skew mixed carrier \(Y=yJ\), one odd whitening slot \(X_1=BS\), and the \(D\)-component of the second whitening slot \(X_2\). A diagonal subtraction or normalization row would usually enter as a raw lower carrier or baseline correction, not as the same three-factor whitening-transport channel.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
\text{ is not structurally cancelling unless an explicit correction formula reproduces }
-yq''\Gamma_{G,2}/(128\pi^2g^3).
}
\]

Absent that explicit identity, it should be treated as a cross-channel correction term.

---

# 4. Table of correction classes

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{correction} & I\text{-sector possible?} & \text{absorbed?} & \text{danger} \\
\hline
E_{\rm bg/core} & \text{yes, if baseline row has fixed component} & \text{no, unless included in baseline convention} & \text{cross-channel only} \\
E_{\rm norm/sub} & \text{yes, depending on correction formula} & \text{partly, if defined before raw }N_b\text{ table} & \text{cross-channel unless same channel appears} \\
\text{finite-}s\text{ diagonal subtraction} & \text{possible} & \text{convention-dependent} & \text{needs parity check} \\
\text{affine source subtraction} & \text{possible} & \text{if already included in corrected }N_b & \text{avoid double-counting} \\
\text{diagonal renormalization} & \text{possible} & \text{if absorbed into }G/X\text{ normalization} & \text{cross-channel if residual} \\
\end{array}
\]

The main audit point is bookkeeping: if these correction rows are already included in the corrected raw carriers \(N_b\), then the raw row-table clearance may already cover them. If they are **not** included in \(N_b\), then they remain in

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}.
\]

---

# 5. Can these rows structurally cancel \(C_9^{\rm cand}\)?

A structural cancellation would require

\[
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}
+
E_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\]

as an identity on the reduced stratum.

I see no reason this should follow from:

\[
\text{centered parity},
\]

\[
\text{fixed-sector projection},
\]

\[
\text{Gate A/B closure},
\]

or

\[
\text{normalization conventions}.
\]

Such an identity would be a new row-level theorem. It is not a matrix-sector consequence.

Thus the appropriate classification is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}+E_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
=
\text{cross-channel correction, unless explicit formula proves otherwise.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Proper incidence formulation

Define

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
:=
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}
+
E_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
+
\text{any remaining non-raw correction rows}.
\]

Then define the correction incidence wall:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
:=
\left\{
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3},
\quad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\right\}.
}
\]

If Agents 1–4 prove

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}=0,
\]

then this wall disappears and the theorem locks outright.

If not, the theorem locks modulo \(\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}\), provided one proves the cancellation equation is not identically true.

---

# 7. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
E_{\rm bg/core}^{I,(9)}+E_{\rm norm/sub}^{I,(9)}
\text{ is cross-channel only.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero/absorbed if already included in the corrected raw row table;}
}
\]

otherwise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{part of }R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}\text{ and handled by }\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}.
}
\]

I do **not** classify it as structurally dangerous unless an explicit correction formula shows the identity

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
\equiv
-\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

No such identity is presently established.

---

# Final answer

The order-9 local theorem should be considered lockable in one of two forms.

## Strong form

If correction rows are absorbed/projected/closed:

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}=0,
\]

then

\[
g=h,\qquad yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\Longrightarrow
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I\ne0.
\]

## Conditional incidence form

If correction rows remain:

\[
g=h,\qquad
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0,
\qquad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
\Longrightarrow
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I\ne0.
\]

The current evidence supports the second form unless the other agents fully absorb all correction rows.

# Agent 5 — Anisotropy Tower / Order-11 Forecast

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The order-7/order-9 mechanism strongly suggests an anisotropy tower, but this is likely an infinite local visibility ladder rather than a proof-closing theorem.}
}
\]

The pattern is now clear:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{uses}\quad
X_{0,D}\sim \Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{uses}\quad
X_{2,D}\sim \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If both vanish,

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

then the next plausible fixed-sector escape is controlled by

\[
X_{4,D},
\]

and should occur at order \(11\) or \(13\), depending on the degree bookkeeping of the carrier. This defines a third anisotropy \(\Gamma_{G,3}\) involving \(q^{(6)}\) and lower-jet combinations. The order-11/tower route is locally promising, but globally it likely recreates the same quantitative problem:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{j\le J}|\Gamma_{G,j}|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Finite \(\xi\)-like jet models appear flexible enough to make any finite collection of \(\Gamma_{G,j}\)’s super-polynomially small unless a genuinely zeta-specific separation theorem is added. The attached instruction explicitly asks whether the order-9 layering suggests such a tower and whether order 11 should be attacked next. 

---

## 1. The observed pattern

At centered parity, the order-7 term had the form

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_1YX_0-X_0YX_1.
\]

With

\[
X_1=BS,\qquad Y=yJ,\qquad X_0=pI+rD,
\]

we obtained

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
-2yB(pD+rI).
\]

The fixed-sector projection keeps

\[
-2yBr\,I.
\]

Thus order 7 is controlled by

\[
r=(X_0)_D
=
\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2})
\sim g-h
\sim \Gamma_G.
\]

On the wall \(g=h\), one has \(r=0\), and the order-7 fixed-sector signal dies.

At order 9, the survivor is

\[
T_9^{(1,2)}
=
X_1YX_2-X_2YX_1.
\]

With

\[
X_2=aI+dD,
\]

one gets

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
-2yBd\,I.
\]

The audit computed

\[
d=(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi}g^{-3/2}\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

So order 9 is controlled by

\[
X_{2,D}\sim\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This strongly suggests:

\[
\boxed{
\text{next fixed-sector leakage uses }X_{4,D}.
}
\]

---

## 2. Candidate order-11 / order-13 mechanism

The natural next matrix channel is

\[
T^{(1,4)}
=
X_1YX_4-X_4YX_1,
\]

or possibly

\[
T^{(3,2)}
=
X_3YX_2-X_2YX_3,
\]

depending on the internal degree bookkeeping.

For the same algebra, if

\[
X_4=eI+fD,
\]

then

\[
X_1YX_4-X_4YX_1
=
-2yB(eD+fI),
\]

and hence

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_1YX_4-X_4YX_1
\right)
=
-2yBf\,I.
\]

Thus the next leakage is controlled by

\[
f=(X_4)_D.
\]

So the next local target should be:

\[
\boxed{
(X_4)_D\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{fixed-sector visibility at the next odd order.}
}
\]

The exact order is likely \(11\) if the carrier bookkeeping adds \(1+6+4=11\), using the same \(Y=yJ\) raw degree-6 carrier. If the draft’s indexing shifts this family, the same mechanism may land at order \(13\), but the structural target remains \(X_{4,D}\).

---

## 3. Formula for \(X_{4,D}\)

At \(g=h\), write

\[
G_0=gI.
\]

Use the expansion

\[
G(s)=G_0+sG_1+s^2G_2+s^3G_3+s^4G_4+\cdots,
\]

with centered parity sectors

\[
G_1\in \mathbf C S,
\qquad
G_2=\alpha_2I+\delta_2D,
\]

\[
G_3\in \mathbf C S,
\qquad
G_4=\alpha_4I+\delta_4D.
\]

For

\[
X(s)=G(s)^{-1/2},
\]

the binomial expansion gives

\[
X
=
g^{-1/2}I
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\Delta
+\frac38g^{-5/2}\Delta^2
-\frac{5}{16}g^{-7/2}\Delta^3
+\frac{35}{128}g^{-9/2}\Delta^4+\cdots,
\]

where

\[
\Delta=G(s)-gI.
\]

The \(s^4\) \(D\)-component receives contributions from:

\[
-\frac12g^{-3/2}G_4,
\]

\[
\frac38g^{-5/2}(G_2^2+G_1G_3+G_3G_1),
\]

\[
-\frac{5}{16}g^{-7/2}(G_1^2G_2+G_1G_2G_1+G_2G_1^2),
\]

and

\[
\frac{35}{128}g^{-9/2}G_1^4.
\]

But

\[
G_1^2\in\mathbf C I,
\qquad
G_1^4\in\mathbf C I,
\]

so \(G_1^4\) has no \(D\)-component.

Also, if

\[
G_1=\sigma_1S,
\qquad
G_3=\sigma_3S,
\]

then

\[
G_1G_3+G_3G_1
=
2\sigma_1\sigma_3I,
\]

so that term has no \(D\)-component.

For

\[
G_2=\alpha_2I+\delta_2D,
\]

we have

\[
G_2^2
=
(\alpha_2^2+\delta_2^2)I+2\alpha_2\delta_2D.
\]

Similarly,

\[
G_1^2G_2+G_1G_2G_1+G_2G_1^2
\]

has a \(D\)-component proportional to \(\sigma_1^2\delta_2\), with a sign depending on the multiplication convention for \(SDS\). Since

\[
SDS=-D,
\]

we get

\[
G_1G_2G_1
=
\sigma_1^2 S(\alpha_2I+\delta_2D)S
=
\sigma_1^2(\alpha_2I-\delta_2D).
\]

Meanwhile,

\[
G_1^2G_2+G_2G_1^2
=
2\sigma_1^2(\alpha_2I+\delta_2D).
\]

Thus the sum has \(D\)-component

\[
(2\sigma_1^2\delta_2-\sigma_1^2\delta_2)
=
\sigma_1^2\delta_2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
(X_4)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\delta_4
+
\frac34g^{-5/2}\alpha_2\delta_2
-
\frac{5}{16}g^{-7/2}\sigma_1^2\delta_2.
}
\]

This matches the tower form described in the instruction.

---

## 4. Candidate \(\Gamma_{G,3}\)

Since

\[
(X_2)_D
\sim
\delta_2
\sim
\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

the next anisotropy should be the numerator of

\[
(X_4)_D.
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,3}
:=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\delta_4
+
\frac34g^{-5/2}\alpha_2\delta_2
-
\frac{5}{16}g^{-7/2}\sigma_1^2\delta_2,
}
\]

up to a harmless nonzero scalar normalization.

Equivalently, one could clear powers of \(g\) and define

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Gamma_{G,3}
:=
-8g^2\delta_4
+
12g\alpha_2\delta_2
-
5\sigma_1^2\delta_2.
}
\]

Here:

\[
\delta_2=(G_2)_D,
\qquad
\delta_4=(G_4)_D,
\qquad
\alpha_2=(G_2)_I,
\qquad
\sigma_1=(G_1)_S.
\]

In phase-jet terms, \(\delta_4\) will involve

\[
q^{(6)}
\]

plus lower-jet polynomial terms. Thus \(\Gamma_{G,3}\) is a new sixth-jet anisotropy condition.

On the layered incidence

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

we have

\[
\delta_0=0,
\qquad
\delta_2=0.
\]

Then the formula collapses to

\[
(X_4)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\delta_4.
\]

So on the first two anisotropy walls, order 11/13 should be controlled simply by

\[
\boxed{
\delta_4=(G_4)_D.
}
\]

This is the clean tower pattern.

---

## 5. Does \(\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) force \((X_4)_D=0\)?

No structural reason.

The first wall kills

\[
X_{0,D}.
\]

The second wall kills

\[
X_{2,D}.
\]

The next term \(X_{4,D}\) depends on a new even Gram derivative \(G_4\), hence on \(q^{(6)}\) and lower-jet terms. There is no current identity forcing it to vanish once the previous two anisotropies vanish.

So locally:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\not\Rightarrow
(X_4)_D=0.
}
\]

This suggests that a higher-order fixed-sector signal should reappear unless a new incidence wall is imposed.

---

## 6. Is the tower promising or an infinite regress?

Locally, it is promising.

It suggests a finite-order statement of the form:

\[
\max_{0\le j\le J}|\Gamma_{G,j}|>0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{fixed-sector visibility by some finite odd order.}
\]

But globally, it is likely an infinite regress unless one proves a finite nonflatness theorem.

Finite \(\xi\)-like local models with enough parameters can likely tune any finite jet list

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots,\Gamma_{G,J}
\]

to be arbitrarily small, while preserving positivity and symmetry, unless a zeta-specific constraint intervenes.

So the tower improves local detection but does not by itself close RH.

The global theorem would have to be:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{j\le J}|\Gamma_{G,j}|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for some finite \(J\) determined by the finite-core setup.

This is the same quantitative incidence-separation problem in tower form.

---

## 7. Order-11 target

The next local target, if order 9 fails on

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

is:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_1YX_4-X_4YX_1
\right)
=
-2yB(X_4)_D I.
}
\]

On the first two anisotropy walls,

\[
(X_4)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}(G_4)_D.
\]

Thus a candidate order-11/13 theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=0,\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0,\quad
(G_4)_D\neq0
\Longrightarrow
A_{11}^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\quad
\text{or}
\quad
A_{13}^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
}
\]

depending on degree bookkeeping.

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order-11 tower: locally promising.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{But the tower likely becomes an infinite quantitative incidence problem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Requires explicit }X_4/A_{11}\text{ or }A_{13}\text{ computation before promotion.}
}
\]

The next anisotropy candidate is

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,3}\sim (X_4)_D,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
(X_4)_D
=
-\frac12g^{-3/2}\delta_4
+
\frac34g^{-5/2}\alpha_2\delta_2
-
\frac{5}{16}g^{-7/2}\sigma_1^2\delta_2.
}
\]

On the prior layered wall

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

this reduces to

\[
\boxed{
(X_4)_D=-\frac12g^{-3/2}(G_4)_D.
}
\]

So if the order-9 theorem is blocked by \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\), the next local attack should compute the fixed-sector row using \(X_{4,D}\).

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:17:11)

_Thought for 15s_

# Agent 5 — Source Factor Non-Concentration Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ is not proved by the current local framework.}
}
\]

The leading centered formula gives

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36},
\]

so the source prefactor is protected only if

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-a_0},
\qquad
|A_2|\ge Q^{-a_2}.
\]

The \(q_0\) lower bound is plausible on a positive good patch, but the \(A_2\) or \(q''\) lower bound is not. Full-core curvature can in principle cancel the distinguished packet curvature:

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}\approx0.
\]

Thus the global target should not be split into separate anisotropy and source-factor estimates. The right theorem is the combined non-concentration bound

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The attached instruction identifies exactly this issue: even layered anisotropy is insufficient if the prefactor \(yq''\) can become super-polynomially small. 

---

## 1. Leading source factor

The live centered channel has

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

Under the centered relation

\[
q''=2A_2,
\]

we get

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\cdot 2A_2
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]

So the source factor is cubic in the relevant curvature moment.

Therefore

\[
|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

requires, at minimum, polynomial separation from

\[
q_0=0
\]

and

\[
A_2=0.
\]

The \(A_2=0\) wall is the dangerous one.

---

## 2. Distinguished packet contribution

For a centered off-line packet

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

one has

\[
A_{2,P}
=
-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3})
\]

under the source-moment normalization used in the prior packet calculations, or equivalently

\[
q''_P=2A_{2,P}
=
-8(a^{-3}+b^{-3}).
\]

Thus

\[
A_{2,P}\neq0
\]

for every nondegenerate off-line packet.

For the clean packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\]

\[
A_{2,P}
=
-\frac{7168}{27},
\]

so the distinguished-packet contribution is very far from zero.

This proves local packet visibility, but not full-core non-concentration.

---

## 3. Full-core cancellation channel

The actual source factor uses the full reduced-core quantity:

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R},
\]

or equivalently

\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R.
\]

Nothing in the current rank-two local framework prevents

\[
A_{2,R}
=
-A_{2,P}+\varepsilon
\]

with

\[
0<|\varepsilon|<e^{-Q}.
\]

Then

\[
A_2=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
q''=2\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
\sim
-\frac{q_0\varepsilon^3}{36}.
\]

This is super-polynomially small even if

\[
q_0>0
\]

and the distinguished packet itself is strongly visible.

So the obstruction is not the packet. It is cancellation between the distinguished packet and the rest of the selected core/background.

---

## 4. Does same-scale or strict core gap prevent this?

No formal prevention is currently available.

Same-scale selection says the relevant packets have comparable local distances or weights. It does not impose a sign condition on their second-jet contributions at the chosen midpoint.

For a packet centered at offset \(x\), the second derivative of

\[
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
\]

changes sign depending on the offset scale. At the packet center it is negative, but away from the center the curvature can become positive. Therefore same-scale packets at different offsets can contribute opposite curvature signs.

A strict core gap controls membership stability:

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}.
\]

It does not control the sign or magnitude of the aggregate curvature

\[
A_2=\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal C_k}A_{2,\rho}.
\]

Thus same-scale/core-gap geometry does not currently imply

\[
|A_2|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

---

## 5. Does \(q_0>0\) help?

Only partially.

The good-patch assumptions require

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0.
\]

If one also has polynomial Gram bounds

\[
Q^{-d}\le g\le Q^d,
\]

then

\[
|q_0|\ge \pi Q^{-d}.
\]

So the \(q_0\)-factor can plausibly be controlled as part of the good-patch quantitative hypotheses.

But this still leaves

\[
|A_2|^3
\]

or

\[
|q''|^3
\]

uncontrolled.

Thus the main missing source estimate is

\[
\boxed{
|q''|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
|A_2|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## 6. Finite-model falsifier

A finite \(\xi\)-like local model can preserve:

\[
q_0>0,
\qquad
g,h>0,
\qquad
\text{quartet symmetry},
\qquad
\text{positive packet kernels},
\]

while tuning the aggregate curvature small.

Take one distinguished centered packet with

\[
A_{2,P}\neq0.
\]

Add one or more same-scale packets or a smooth background contribution whose aggregate second moment is

\[
A_{2,R}
=
-A_{2,P}+\varepsilon.
\]

Then

\[
A_2=\varepsilon.
\]

Choose the background level so that

\[
q_0>0
\]

and Gram positivity are maintained. For small nonzero \(\varepsilon\),

\[
q''=2A_2=2\varepsilon\neq0,
\]

but

\[
|yq''|
\sim
\left|\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}\right|
=
O(|\varepsilon|^3).
\]

Taking

\[
\varepsilon=e^{-Q}
\]

gives

\[
0<|yq''|<e^{-2Q}
\]

or \(e^{-3Q}\)-scale depending on whether \(y\) is evaluated by its leading quadratic approximation. This defeats every polynomial lower bound.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ is false in flexible finite local models.}
}
\]

It may still be true for actual zeta data, but it would require a new arithmetic non-cancellation theorem.

---

## 7. Interaction with layered anisotropy

The global target is currently

\[
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Even if one proves

\[
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-B},
\]

the product can still be small if

\[
|yq''|\ll Q^{-A-B}.
\]

Conversely, even if

\[
|yq''|\ge Q^{-B},
\]

the layered anisotropy vector can be small.

Thus the proof needs a combined non-concentration theorem for

\[
(yq'',\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

or at least for their product.

The cleanest statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|yq''\right|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This should replace separate informal assumptions.

---

## 8. Could one exclude \(q''\approx0\) by redefining the good patch?

One can define a stronger quantitative base:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+,\mathrm{src}}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\cap
\{|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}\}.
\]

But then one must prove every RH-relevant off-line packet reaches this base.

That reach theorem is not currently available. It is essentially the same non-swallowing problem at the source-factor level.

So adding

\[
|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

to the good-patch definition is bookkeeping, not proof.

---

## 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ is not locally proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It is plausible only with new actual-zeta arithmetic input.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It is false in flexible finite local models.}
}
\]

The main missing estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
|A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|q''|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

A stronger source theorem would also control

\[
y
\]

directly, but if the leading relation

\[
y\sim-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}
\]

is stable, then controlling

\[
q_0
\]

and

\[
A_2
\]

controls \(y\).

---

# Final answer

The source prefactor must be included in the main global theorem. The right target is not merely

\[
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Using

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36},
\]

this reduces, at leading source level, to a lower bound for

\[
\boxed{
|q_0A_2^3|
}
\]

times the layered anisotropy factor.

The current local framework does not prove such a bound. Same-scale selection, strict core gap, packet visibility, and Gram positivity do not prevent rest/core curvature cancellation

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P}.
\]

Therefore the source-factor lower bound is a genuine part of the remaining zeta-specific quantitative non-concentration problem.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:23:23)

_Thought for 1m 50s_

# Agent 5 — Actual-Zeta Scale and Normalization Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scaling does not exclude the bad path; it merely rescales it.}
}
\]

In the draft’s local normalization, \(Q\) is the microscopic phase scale, with

\[
|q_0|\asymp Q,
\qquad
|q_0'|\ll Q^2,
\qquad
|q_0''|\ll Q^3,
\qquad
|q_0'''|\ll Q^4,
\]

and the microscopic disk has scale \(|s|\lesssim Q^{-1}\). Thus \(q_0,q'',q^{(4)}\) are **raw phase derivatives in the local \(t\)-variable**, not \(O(1)\)-normalized variables. The earlier toy path

\[
q_0=2,\qquad q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,\qquad q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2
\]

is therefore best read as the **normalized** model. The scale-correct raw version is obtained by taking \(q_0\asymp Q\), \(q''\asymp Q^3\), and \(q^{(4)}\asymp Q^5\). This scaled path remains compatible with the expected derivative sizes and with \(g,h>0\). Therefore the source-weighted layered lower bound still needs a genuinely zeta-specific non-concentration theorem. The attached instruction asks exactly whether scaling excludes the bad path or merely rescales it; the answer is the latter. 

---

## 1. What is \(Q\)?

In the draft’s local analytic setup, \(Q\) is the microscopic scale controlling the local window and the size of the baseline phase derivative. The relevant regime is

\[
L_I\asymp \frac{x_0}{Q},
\qquad
|q_0(t_\pm)|\asymp Q,
\]

and the microscopic block estimates use

\[
|q_0(t_\pm)|\ll Q,
\qquad
|q_0'(t_\pm)|\ll Q^2,
\qquad
|q_0''(t_\pm)|\ll Q^3,
\qquad
|q_0'''(t_\pm)|\ll Q^4.
\]

So \(Q\) is not an auxiliary small parameter. It is the local phase-frequency scale, comparable to \(q_0\), which in zeta heuristics is logarithmic in height.

---

## 2. Are \(q_0,q'',q^{(4)}\) raw or normalized?

They are raw derivatives in the local \(t\)-coordinate.

The same-point Gram block is written in raw derivatives:

\[
G_{m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q(t_\pm) & \frac12q'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12q'(t_\pm) &
\frac1{12}\bigl(q''(t_\pm)+2q(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The Gram quantities used in the order-7/order-9 analysis are therefore raw phase-jet quantities:

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\]

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right),
\]

up to the harmless factor conventions already present in the draft.

Thus

\[
q_0\sim Q,
\qquad
q''\sim Q^3,
\qquad
q^{(4)}\sim Q^5
\]

is the scale-correct hierarchy.

---

## 3. Expected sizes

Under the local scale hierarchy:

\[
q_0=O(Q),
\]

\[
q''=O(Q^3),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=O(Q^5).
\]

For the centered source relation

\[
q''=2A_2,
\]

one has

\[
A_2=O(Q^3).
\]

The leading source factor is

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\]

so

\[
y=O(Q^7).
\]

Therefore

\[
yq''=O(Q^{10})
\]

at natural scale.

This means that the meaningful non-concentration statement should be normalized. A scale-correct version is:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, one can keep the raw expression but allow the exponent \(A\) to absorb the natural powers of \(Q\). The normalized form is cleaner.

---

## 4. Scale-correct bad path

The old toy path

\[
q_0=2,
\qquad
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2
\]

corresponds to an \(O(1)\)-normalized model.

The raw scale-correct version is:

\[
q_0=\lambda Q,
\qquad \lambda\asymp1,
\]

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Substituting \(q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1\), this is

\[
q^{(4)}
=
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2)
+
6(1-q_0^2)\varepsilon_1
-
6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
\varepsilon_1,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
\varepsilon_2.
\]

For \(q_0=\lambda Q\), the main sizes are

\[
q''\sim -2\lambda^3Q^3,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}\sim 12\lambda^5Q^5.
\]

These are exactly the expected derivative sizes.

Thus the bad path is not excluded by scaling.

---

## 5. Normalized version of the bad path

Define normalized jets

\[
\widehat q_0:=\frac{q_0}{Q},
\qquad
\widehat q_2:=\frac{q''}{Q^3},
\qquad
\widehat q_4:=\frac{q^{(4)}}{Q^5}.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{\Gamma_G}{Q^3}
=
\widehat q_2
+
2\widehat q_0^3
-
\frac{6\widehat q_0}{Q^2}.
\]

So the first normalized wall is

\[
\widehat q_2
=
-2\widehat q_0^3
+
O(Q^{-2}).
\]

Similarly,

\[
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{Q^5}
=
-\widehat q_0^2\widehat q_2
-
\frac16\widehat q_4
+
O(Q^{-2}).
\]

On the first wall this gives

\[
\widehat q_4
=
12\widehat q_0^5
+
O(Q^{-2}).
\]

So the normalized bad path is:

\[
\widehat q_0=\lambda,
\]

\[
\widehat q_2=-2\lambda^3+O(Q^{-2})+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{Q^3},
\]

\[
\widehat q_4=12\lambda^5+O(Q^{-2})+\frac{\text{linear combination of }\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2}{Q^5}.
\]

This is perfectly compatible with the normalized scale hierarchy.

---

## 6. Does \(g,h>0\) exclude the path?

No.

The positivity conditions are

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
h=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)>0.
\]

The second inequality is

\[
q''>-2q_0^3.
\]

On the Gram-isotropy wall,

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
h
=
\frac1\pi\left(
\frac13q_0^3
+
\frac16(6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1)
\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(
q_0+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}
\right).
\]

So if

\[
q_0>0
\]

and \(|\varepsilon_1|\ll q_0\), then

\[
h>0.
\]

Moreover,

\[
h\asymp q_0\asymp Q.
\]

Thus the bad path lies close to the lower positivity boundary in \(q''\)-space relative to \(Q^3\), but it does **not** make \(h\) small or singular. The Gram block remains positive at natural scale.

So positivity does not rescue the estimate.

---

## 7. Are such magnitudes plausible for actual zeta jets?

At the level of scale, yes.

The required magnitudes are:

\[
q_0\asymp Q,
\]

\[
q''\asymp -Q^3,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}\asymp Q^5.
\]

These match the draft’s local derivative scale hierarchy. No scale estimate alone prevents them.

Whether actual zeta data can realize the precise near-incidence relations

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2
\]

with

\[
|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

is a genuine arithmetic/non-concentration question. It is not settled by normalization.

---

## 8. Correct scale-normalized target theorem

The raw theorem

\[
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is dimensionally awkward because the two anisotropies have different natural sizes.

A cleaner version is:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, in row-normalized form, one should bound the normalized order-7 and order-9 row coordinates separately:

\[
\boxed{
\max\left\{
\frac{|yq''\Gamma_G|}{Q^{13}},
\frac{|yq''\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^{15}}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the correct scale-aware statement.

If the proof keeps the raw theorem, the missing lower bound must be interpreted with an arbitrary power of \(Q\) absorbed into \(A\). But the normalized form is mathematically cleaner.

---

## 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scaling merely rescales the bad path.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
q_0=2
\text{ is not raw-scale relevant if }q_0\asymp Q,
}
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
q_0=\lambda Q,\quad
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,\quad
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2
}
\]

is the scale-correct bad path.

This path preserves:

\[
q_0>0,
\qquad
g>0,
\qquad
h>0,
\]

and the derivative sizes remain natural:

\[
q''=O(Q^3),
\qquad
q^{(4)}=O(Q^5).
\]

So scaling does not exclude the obstruction.

---

# Final answer

The bad path survives normalization.

The correct scale-aware theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\max\left\{
\frac{|yq''\Gamma_G|}{Q^{13}},
\frac{|yq''\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^{15}}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The scale-correct bad path is:

\[
\boxed{
q_0=\lambda Q,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2,
}
\]

so that

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Choosing

\[
0<|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|<e^{-Q}
\]

defeats every polynomial lower bound while preserving the natural \(Q\)-scales and the positivity of \(g,h\).

Thus the proof still requires a genuine zeta-specific arithmetic separation theorem. Scaling does not remove the need for it.

# Agent 5 — Scale-Correct Finite Adversary

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scaling does not block the finite \(\xi\)-like adversary.}
}
\]

The normalized bad paths have clean raw-scale analogues. In Regime A, the source factor remains naturally sized while the anisotropy vector is made exponentially small. In Regime B, the anisotropy vector remains naturally sized while the source factor is made exponentially small. Therefore the source-weighted layered lower bound is not rescued by the \(Q\)-scaling convention.

The correct conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current local architecture still needs actual zeta arithmetic beyond finite local \(\xi\)-like structure.}
}
\]

The attached instruction asks specifically whether the normalized adversary survives in the paper’s raw \(Q\)-scale. It does. 

---

# 1. Raw-scale variables

Use the raw scale

\[
q_0\asymp Q,\qquad q''\asymp Q^3,\qquad q^{(4)}\asymp Q^5.
\]

The layered anisotropies are

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The scale-normalized target should be written as

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the right object to test.

---

# 2. Regime A — anisotropy small, source live

Take

\[
q_0=\lambda Q,\qquad \lambda\asymp 1,
\]

and set

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1.
\]

Now choose \(q^{(4)}\) so that

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)},
\]

we set

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
}
\]

For \(q_0=\lambda Q\),

\[
q''
=
6\lambda Q-2\lambda^3Q^3+\varepsilon_1
\sim
-2\lambda^3Q^3,
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
\sim
6(-\lambda^2Q^2)(-2\lambda^3Q^3)
=
12\lambda^5Q^5.
\]

So the raw jet sizes are natural.

Also,

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
h
=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(
\frac13q_0^3
+
q_0
-\frac13q_0^3
+
\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}
\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(q_0+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)>0
\]

for \(|\varepsilon_1|\ll q_0\).

Thus Gram positivity is preserved.

For the source factor, use

\[
A_2=\frac{q''}{2}\sim-\lambda^3Q^3,
\]

and

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}
\sim
-\frac{\lambda Q\cdot \lambda^6Q^6}{72}
=
-\frac{\lambda^7}{72}Q^7.
\]

Therefore

\[
yq''
\sim
Q^7\cdot Q^3
=
Q^{10},
\]

so

\[
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}\asymp 1.
\]

Choose

\[
0<|\varepsilon_1|<Q^3e^{-Q},
\qquad
0<|\varepsilon_2|<Q^5e^{-Q}.
\]

Then

\[
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
<e^{-Q}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
0<
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ll e^{-Q}.
}
\]

This is the scale-correct Regime A adversary.

---

# 3. Regime B — source small, anisotropy live

Now keep

\[
q_0=\lambda Q,\qquad \lambda\asymp1,
\]

but make the source curvature small:

\[
q''=2\varepsilon,
\qquad
0<|\varepsilon|<e^{-Q}.
\]

Then

\[
A_2=\varepsilon.
\]

At leading order,

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}
=
-\frac{\lambda Q\,\varepsilon^2}{72},
\]

so

\[
yq''
=
-\frac{\lambda Q\,\varepsilon^2}{72}\cdot 2\varepsilon
=
-\frac{\lambda Q}{36}\varepsilon^3.
\]

Thus

\[
|yq''|
\ll
Qe^{-3Q}.
\]

The anisotropies are not small generically. For example, take \(q^{(4)}=0\). Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
2\varepsilon-6\lambda Q+2\lambda^3Q^3
\sim
2\lambda^3Q^3,
\]

so

\[
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3}\asymp1.
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-\lambda^2Q^2)2\varepsilon
=
O(Q^2e^{-Q}),
\]

which may be small, but the maximum is already controlled by \(\Gamma_G\).

Therefore

\[
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ll
\frac{Qe^{-3Q}}{Q^{10}}
=
Q^{-9}e^{-3Q}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
0<
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ll e^{-2Q}
}
\]

for large \(Q\). This is the scale-correct Regime B adversary.

Gram positivity is also preserved:

\[
g=\frac{\lambda Q}{\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
h=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13\lambda^3Q^3+\frac13\varepsilon\right)>0.
\]

Thus \(g,h>0\) remain valid.

---

# 4. Does the raw scale create a hidden obstruction?

No.

The bad paths have the expected raw derivative sizes:

Regime A:

\[
q_0\asymp Q,\qquad q''\asymp Q^3,\qquad q^{(4)}\asymp Q^5.
\]

Regime B:

\[
q_0\asymp Q,\qquad q''\ll1,\qquad q^{(4)}=0
\]

or otherwise controlled. Small \(q''\) is not forbidden by Gram positivity because

\[
h=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
\]

is dominated by \(q_0^3/3>0\).

Thus scale does not eliminate either failure mode.

The only possible objection is whether a finite \(\xi\)-like model with positive packet kernels and same-scale constraints can realize these raw jets. That is not a scaling issue; it is a finite-model realization issue for Agents 1–4/6.

---

# 5. Correct scale-normalized theorem

The target theorem should not be written only as

\[
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

unless the natural powers of \(Q\) are understood to be absorbed into \(A\). The cleaner statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}
\max\left\{
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3},
\frac{|\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^5}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\max\left\{
\frac{|yq''\Gamma_G|}{Q^{13}},
\frac{|yq''\Gamma_{G,2}|}{Q^{15}}
\right\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The adversaries above defeat this normalized statement.

---

# 6. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scaling-compatible adversary exists.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Regime A survives raw scaling: source live, anisotropy exponentially small.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Regime B survives raw scaling: anisotropy live, source exponentially small.}
}
\]

So scaling does not rescue the source-weighted layered lower bound.

---

# Final answer

The raw-scale adversarial formulas are:

## Regime A

\[
q_0=\lambda Q,
\]

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)q''-6\varepsilon_2,
\]

with

\[
0<|\varepsilon_1|<Q^3e^{-Q},
\qquad
0<|\varepsilon_2|<Q^5e^{-Q}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\]

while

\[
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}\asymp1.
\]

Hence the normalized product is \(O(e^{-Q})\).

## Regime B

\[
q_0=\lambda Q,
\qquad
q''=2\varepsilon,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=0,
\]

with

\[
0<|\varepsilon|<e^{-Q}.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{|yq''|}{Q^{10}}\ll e^{-2Q},
\]

while

\[
\frac{|\Gamma_G|}{Q^3}\asymp1.
\]

Again the normalized product is exponentially small.

Therefore the scale audit does **not** block the finite adversary. The proof still needs actual zeta arithmetic, not normalization, to establish the source-weighted layered non-concentration theorem.
