# Agent 5 — Interval-local versus global-height distinction

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global bad events are not enough; the proof needs interval-local control on each admissible }I_\rho.
}
\]

The global fixed-prime/random-phase evidence is hostile to the desired lower bound, but it does **not** by itself refute the interval theorem needed for the RH architecture. The theorem under test is local around an RH-relevant off-line packet:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad H=yq''.
\]

A global statement such as “there exists some \(t\le T\) with small residual” does not imply that **every** admissible packet interval \(I_\rho\) can be bad. The next real test is therefore interval-local: can a fixed-prime/AFE model make the residual small **throughout** the whole admissible \(I_\rho\), or at least make its supremum on \(I_\rho\) smaller than every polynomial power? The attached instruction correctly identifies this as the key distinction after the global prime-phase experiments. 

---

## 1. The theorem is a supremum theorem, not a pointwise theorem

The desired estimate is

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|F(m)|_\infty\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where

\[
F(m)
=
\left(
H(m)\Gamma_G(m),
H(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m)
\right).
\]

Here

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16 q^{(4)}.
\]

This is weaker than requiring the lower bound at a prescribed point \(m_0\). It allows us to move within the admissible interval \(I_\rho\). Therefore pointwise source collapse

\[
H(m_0)\approx0
\]

or pointwise anisotropy collapse

\[
\Gamma_G(m_0)\approx\Gamma_{G,2}(m_0)\approx0
\]

does not kill the theorem unless the collapse persists across the interval at polynomial scale.

---

## 2. Expected interval length and bandwidth

The local construction uses a microscopic phase scale. The natural admissible movement in the midpoint \(m\) is expected to be at most on the order of

\[
|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-1}
\]

unless same-scale/core-gap constraints allow a larger interval. The relevant phase-jet functions vary on frequency scale roughly

\[
\Omega\sim Q
\]

in normalized local coordinates.

Thus the number of effectively independent samples inside one \(I_\rho\) is plausibly

\[
M\sim |I_\rho|\Omega \sim 1
\]

at the smallest microscopic scale, or at best polynomially many if \(I_\rho\) is larger.

This matters. Global random-phase heuristics over height \(T=e^Q\) may see many opportunities to hit a codimension-two bad set. A single packet interval may not.

So there are two distinct questions:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m\le T:\ |F(m)|\ll Q^{-A}
}
\]

versus

\[
\boxed{
\forall I_\rho:\ \sup_{m\in I_\rho}|F(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The first looks likely in random/fixed-prime models. The second is still open.

---

## 3. Global bad events threaten, but do not refute, the proof

The global fixed-prime experiments and random-phase codimension heuristic show that bad events are not obviously forbidden by prime phases. They undermine any claim that Euler-product structure automatically gives separation.

But a proof of RH using this architecture does not need to show the residual is large everywhere. It needs to show that the residual is large somewhere in each admissible RH-relevant packet interval.

Therefore global bad events are evidence against a simple universal pointwise lower bound, but they are not enough to refute an interval-supremum theorem.

The correct adversarial target must be stronger:

\[
\boxed{
0<
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|H(m)|\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
<e^{-Q}.
}
\]

A single bad point is insufficient.

---

## 4. What would make an interval-local countermodel?

To defeat the interval theorem, one must construct a model where, for all \(m\in I_\rho\),

\[
H(m)\Gamma_G(m)\approx0
\]

and

\[
H(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m)\approx0
\]

at super-polynomial scale.

There are two ways.

### Regime B interval collapse

Make

\[
H(m)=y(m)q''(m)
\]

small throughout \(I_\rho\). Since

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

this means roughly

\[
q''(m)\approx0
\quad\text{for all }m\in I_\rho.
\]

This is much stronger than \(q''(m_0)\approx0\) at one point.

If \(q''\) is analytic with natural derivative scale

\[
(q'')'\sim Q^4
\]

or comparable, then keeping

\[
|q''(m)|<e^{-Q}
\]

on an interval of length \(Q^{-1}\) would force several Taylor coefficients to be extremely small. That is a genuine finite-jet flattening condition.

Flexible local models may still tune this for a finite number of derivatives, but it is materially harder than pointwise source collapse.

### Regime A interval collapse

Make

\[
\Gamma_G(m)\approx0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}(m)\approx0
\]

throughout \(I_\rho\), while \(H\) stays live.

This means the phase jets approximately satisfy differential relations over an interval:

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+O(e^{-Q}),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=6(1-q_0^2)q''+O(e^{-Q}).
\]

That is no longer merely a two-equation pointwise incidence. It resembles an approximate ODE constraint over an interval. This is the most promising place for an interval theorem: analytic functions cannot satisfy a nontrivial ODE residual this accurately over a polynomial interval unless their coefficients are correspondingly constrained.

But the current draft does not supply the needed coefficient lower bound.

---

## 5. Remez/Turán/Nazarov route

The interval theorem becomes plausible if one can prove a Remez-type statement for

\[
F_1(m)=H(m)\Gamma_G(m),
\qquad
F_2(m)=H(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m).
\]

A typical sufficient framework would be:

1. \(I_\rho\) has polynomial width:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}.
\]

2. \(F_1,F_2\) are holomorphic in a complex neighborhood of radius

\[
Q^{-L'}.
\]

3. Growth is controlled:

\[
\sup |F_j|\le Q^M
\]

on that neighborhood.

4. There is a non-tiny Taylor witness:

\[
\max_{j=1,2}\max_{r\le R}|F_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
\]

Then one can hope to prove

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max(|F_1(m)|,|F_2(m)|)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The missing part is item 4. Analytic inequalities propagate size; they do not create it. We need a non-tiny derivative/coefficient witness for actual zeta data.

---

## 6. Is the interval likely to have enough room?

This is a serious caveat. If the admissible interval has only microscopic length

\[
|I_\rho|\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

then the interval may contain only \(O(1)\) independent oscillations of the relevant local jets. That makes the interval theorem delicate but still possible.

If same-scale/core-gap geometry gives a much smaller interval, say

\[
|I_\rho|<e^{-Q},
\]

then the interval theorem is likely hopeless without much stronger input.

So the interval length itself becomes part of the reach theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}
}
\]

must be proved or assumed. Without it, even a Remez approach cannot start.

---

## 7. Does the global fixed-prime model refute interval-local control?

No.

The numerical fixed-prime model found isolated points where

\[
\mathcal P(t)=|H(t)|\max(|R_1(t)|,|R_2(t)|)
\]

is small, especially through source collapse, and points where \(\mathcal A\) is moderately small with live source.

But it did not show that

\[
\sup_{m\in[t_0-\Delta,t_0+\Delta]}\mathcal P(m)
\]

is small on a full interval of length comparable to \(Q^{-1}\).

In fact, if the residual crosses zero transversely, the supremum on even a modest interval may be large. So the next countermodel must check flatness, not just zeros.

---

## 8. Correct next countermodel target

The correct numerical/adversarial target is:

\[
\boxed{
\min_{t_0}
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}
\mathcal P(t_0+u)
}
\]

or, for the vector residual,

\[
\boxed{
\min_{t_0}
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}
\max(|F_1(t_0+u)|,|F_2(t_0+u)|).
}
\]

This is very different from minimizing

\[
\mathcal P(t_0)
\]

at a point.

If the interval-supremum minimum remains polynomially large in fixed-prime/AFE models, that would support the proof direction.

If one can make the interval supremum exponentially small, the architecture is seriously damaged.

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need interval-local bad events.}
}
\]

Global bad events are not enough to refute the architecture. However, they are enough to show that any valid theorem must use the interval-supremum structure and analytic rigidity, not pointwise avoidance.

The interval theorem remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditionally plausible but unproved.}
}
\]

The exact missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-weighted interval non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

For every admissible RH-relevant packet interval \(I_\rho\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|y(m)q''(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

To attack it, one must prove:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

and a non-tiny Taylor/Remez witness for the actual zeta source-weighted residual.

Or, adversarially, build the stronger interval-local fixed-prime/AFE countermodel

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|F(m)|<e^{-Q}.
}
\]

That is the next real fork.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 08:41:45)

_Thought for 6s_

# Agent 5 — Interval-Local Source-Jet / Anisotropy Tower Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{A fixed finite tower remains vulnerable. A growing tower may help, but it becomes a new architecture.}
}
\]

The current two-layer vector

\[
F=(H\Gamma_G,\ H\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

is too small in the source-collapse regime because

\[
H=yq''\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

Adding higher source jets and higher anisotropies is the natural repair:

\[
A_2,\ A_4,\ A_6,\ldots,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,1},\Gamma_{G,2},\Gamma_{G,3},\ldots.
\]

But for any fixed finite order \(R\), finite-prime/local models can plausibly flatten all those coordinates on a short interval by imposing enough jet constraints. To make the interval theorem plausible, one likely needs either:

\[
\boxed{
R=R(Q)\to\infty
}
\]

or a quasianalytic/finite-determinacy theorem preventing simultaneous flattening of the actual zeta phase. The attached prompt asks whether a source/aniso tower can rescue the interval theorem; my answer is: fixed finite tower no, growing tower maybe, but only with serious new analytic control. 

---

## 1. Why the current vector fails

The current interval vector is

\[
F(m)=
\left(
H(m)\Gamma_G(m),
H(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m)
\right),
\]

with

\[
H=yq'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

In the source-collapse regime,

\[
q''\approx0,
\]

we have, at leading centered order,

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

So \(F\) collapses even if

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Thus the failure is structural: the known rows are weighted by a low source curvature power.

---

## 2. Source-jet tower

The natural source repair is to include higher source jets.

If

\[
A_2\approx0,
\]

but

\[
A_4\neq0,
\]

then a higher source-Hessian row may be driven by \(A_4\) instead of \(A_2\). More generally, if

\[
A_2=A_4=\cdots=A_{2r-2}=0,
\qquad
A_{2r}\neq0,
\]

one expects a later row with source factor roughly

\[
A_{2r}^3
\]

or a comparable cubic/quadratic source-Hessian monomial.

So a source tower might use

\[
S_R(m)
=
\max_{1\le r\le R}|A_{2r}(m)|.
\]

A source-robust interval theorem would then need

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho} S_R(m)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But for fixed \(R\), this is another finite-jet non-concentration statement. Flexible finite models can tune

\[
A_2,\ A_4,\ldots,\ A_{2R}
\]

small at a point, and likely on a short interval, by imposing enough local moment constraints.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed finite source-jet tower remains vulnerable.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Anisotropy tower

The anisotropy tower observed so far is:

\[
\Gamma_{G,1}:=\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}:=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The next layer is expected to be

\[
\Gamma_{G,3}\sim (X_4)_D,
\]

involving

\[
q^{(6)}
\]

and lower-jet combinations.

The current pattern is:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,1},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and a later row should involve

\[
H\Gamma_{G,3}
\]

if the same source factor persists.

So an anisotropy tower would define

\[
G_R(m)
=
\max_{1\le k\le R}|\Gamma_{G,k}(m)|.
\]

The interval theorem becomes

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|H(m)|G_R(m)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But this still fails if \(H\) is source-small. Hence anisotropy tower alone is insufficient.

One needs both source and anisotropy towers.

---

## 4. Combined source/aniso tower

A more robust tower would be something like

\[
F_R(m)
=
\left(
A_{2r}(m)^{\alpha_r}\Gamma_{G,k}(m)
\right)_{1\le r,k\le R},
\]

or more faithfully, the actual row vector

\[
\mathcal R_R(m)
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},A_{11}^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\]

after decomposing all source-jet and anisotropy channels.

A theorem would require

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
\|\mathcal R_R(m)\|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This could defeat:

1. source collapse through \(A_2\approx0\), if some \(A_{2r}\) is large;
2. anisotropy collapse through \(\Gamma_{G,1},\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0\), if some higher \(\Gamma_{G,k}\) is large.

But for fixed \(R\), the countermodel can attempt to flatten all finitely many coordinates. Since the local model has many tunable packet/far-tail parameters, fixed finite \(R\) is unlikely to be enough.

---

## 5. Interval-local flattening and derivative count

The interval-local theorem is stronger than pointwise non-concentration. To make

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\|F_R(m)\|<e^{-Q},
\]

one must flatten the relevant functions across \(I_\rho\), not just at one point.

If

\[
|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-1},
\]

and the functions have natural bandwidth \(\Omega\sim Q\), then flattening across the interval may only require controlling \(O(1)\) effective Taylor coefficients. If \(I_\rho\) is larger, more derivatives are needed.

A finite tower of order \(R\) might beat a finite number of flattening constraints only if \(R\) exceeds the effective local complexity. But without a theorem bounding the complexity or proving a non-tiny Taylor coefficient, this remains speculative.

Thus a growing tower may be helpful only if tied to a quantitative analytic theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the first }R(Q)\text{ source/aniso rows are small on }I_\rho,
\text{ then the phase is forced into a forbidden quasianalytic class.}
}
\]

No such theorem is present.

---

## 6. Quasianalytic possibility

A promising abstract route would be Denjoy–Carleman/quasianalyticity.

If the actual zeta phase \(q(t)\) lies in a class where sufficiently many derivatives control the function, then smallness of a growing tower might imply excessive flatness, perhaps forcing an identity or contradiction.

One would need derivative bounds of the form

\[
|q^{(n)}(t)|\le C^n n! M_n
\]

with a quasianalytic sequence \(M_n\), plus a lower/nonzero witness.

Then a growing tower \(R(Q)\) might be able to prevent interval flattening.

But this is far beyond the current local row framework. It would require:

1. high-order row computations;
2. uniform constants for the tower;
3. a growth-controlled analytic class for actual zeta;
4. a way to connect row smallness to all relevant derivatives.

---

## 7. Practical obstruction: row constants

Even if a growing tower is conceptually promising, row constants may explode.

Higher rows involve:

\[
X_{2k,D},
\]

higher source jets,

\[
A_{2r},
\]

and increasingly complicated correction terms. Constants may grow factorially. To use a tower of length \(R(Q)\), one needs bounds stable enough that

\[
Q^{-A}
\]

does not become meaningless after normalizing rows.

Without uniform control, the tower is not a proof tool.

---

## 8. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed finite tower still vulnerable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Growing tower may help only with a new quasianalytic/finite-determinacy theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Current row technology is not yet sufficient for a growing tower.}
}
\]

---

# Final recommendation

Do **not** immediately jump to order 11 as a local row exercise. Order 11 will likely produce a new anisotropy coordinate, but the same source-divisibility and finite-tower vulnerability remain.

The next meaningful theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval source/aniso tower non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]

A possible formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
\max_{1\le r,k\le R(Q)}
|A_{2r}(m)|^{\alpha_r}|\Gamma_{G,k}(m)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But this requires:

\[
\boxed{
R(Q)\text{ growing, uniform row constants, and quasianalytic control.}
}
\]

Without that, the finite tower is diagnostic only, not proof-closing.

# Agent 5 — Positive Source-Jet Nonflatness Theorem Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No current zeta input proves source-jet nonflatness on }I_\rho.
}
\]

The needed positive theorem would be something like

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B},
\]

or, more robustly,

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

I do **not** see a known route from log-derivative estimates, zero-density, same-scale geometry, source/core gap, AFE estimates, or the explicit formula. The distinguished packet gives a nonzero contribution to \(q''\), but the rest of the selected core can in principle cancel it, and doing so over a short interval only requires finitely many jet cancellations. This is exactly the interval-local source-collapse obstruction identified in the attached instruction. 

---

## 1. The theorem we would need

The clean positive theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-jet nonflatness theorem.}
}
\]

For every admissible reduced good-patch interval

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta=Q^{-L},
\]

associated to an RH-relevant off-line packet, one has

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

A more Taylor-local version is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

This would block Regime B, because

\[
H=yq''\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

If \(q''\) cannot be too small on the interval, then the source factor cannot collapse everywhere.

---

## 2. Distinguished packet alone is not enough

For a centered off-line packet,

\[
A_{2,P}\neq0,
\]

and

\[
q''_P=2A_{2,P}.
\]

In the simple packet model,

\[
A_{2,P}=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

so the packet contribution is strongly nonzero.

But the full source curvature is

\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R,
\]

where \(q''_R\) comes from other selected core packets, background, and far-tail/core data.

The local framework does not prevent

\[
q''_R=-q''_P+\varepsilon.
\]

For interval collapse, one needs

\[
q''_R(m)=-q''_P(m)+O(Q^{-B})
\]

on \(I_\rho\), or equivalently cancellation of a finite Taylor jet:

\[
(q''_R)^{(r)}(m_0)=-(q''_P)^{(r)}(m_0)+O(\eta_r),
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

This is harder than pointwise cancellation, but finite local models have enough degrees of freedom to attempt it. There is no sign or cone condition preventing this in the current proof.

---

## 3. Same-scale/core-gap geometry does not block cancellation

Same-scale core conditions say the selected packets have comparable scale. They do not impose one sign on their curvature contributions.

A packet’s second derivative can change sign depending on its offset from the sampling midpoint. Thus same-scale packets at different offsets can contribute opposite curvature signs.

Strict core gap says core membership is stable:

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}.
\]

It does not say the aggregate moment

\[
\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal C_k}q''_\rho(m)
\]

is bounded away from zero.

So the geometry supplies membership control, not source-jet nonflatness.

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale/core-gap does not imply } |q''|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

---

## 4. Explicit formula does not currently give the needed witness

The explicit formula can express \(q''\) as a zero-side or prime-side local statistic. But the theorem requires a **lower bound** on \(q''\) or its derivatives over \(I_\rho\).

A prime-side representation has the schematic form

\[
q''(m)\sim
\Re \sum_n \Lambda(n)(\log n)^k n^{-1/2-im}W(n)
+\text{gamma/background}.
\]

This is oscillatory. No positivity is available.

Mean-square estimates might give something like

\[
\int_T^{2T}|q''(t)|^2dt
\]

is large on average. But that does not imply

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}
\]

for each specific admissible interval.

To make that leap, we would need a localized lower bound:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2dm\ge Q^{-B},
\]

or a prime-side observability theorem. No such theorem is currently known.

---

## 5. AFE/log-derivative estimates are upper-control, not lower-control

Approximate functional equation methods and log-derivative estimates can control typical size, upper bounds, or averages. They do not forbid a local interval where a derivative statistic is very small.

The source-collapse target is not “\(q''\) is globally small.” It is “\(q''\) is small on one short admissible interval.” AFE flexibility appears compatible with that unless a strong deterministic lower bound is proved.

So the AFE route would need a theorem like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No admissible interval }I_\rho\text{ can have }
\sup_{I_\rho}|q''|<Q^{-B}.
}
\]

I do not see this as a consequence of standard AFE machinery.

---

## 6. Zero statistics and spacing do not help deterministically

Zero density and spacing estimates constrain counts, not signed local moments.

Even if zeros are simple and spaced typically, the signed curvature statistic

\[
q''(m)
\]

can cancel.

Montgomery/GUE-type repulsion would be a probabilistic heuristic, not a deterministic lower bound for every off-line packet interval. It might say source-collapse is rare, but RH needs impossibility or a proof-relevant deterministic exclusion.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero statistics do not currently supply source-jet nonflatness.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Finite-prime/finite-local models likely defeat fixed finite nonflatness

For a fixed derivative order \(R\), the interval-collapse conditions are finitely many equations:

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Phase-relaxed finite-prime models or finite packet models have enough tunable parameters to solve finitely many such equations, while maintaining

\[
q_0>0,\quad g,h>0,
\]

and live anisotropy.

The one-parameter fixed-prime flow adds a recurrence/Diophantine question, but there is no obvious structural obstruction for fixed \(R\).

Therefore any fixed finite source-jet theorem is likely vulnerable in the same way the earlier finite anisotropy tower was vulnerable.

---

## 8. What positive theorem might still work?

The only plausible positive statement would require a **growing** source-jet condition.

For example:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)} |(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

with \(R(Q)\to\infty\), or an interval norm theorem derived from quasianalyticity:

\[
\boxed{
q''\text{ cannot be exponentially flat on }I_\rho
\text{ unless forced by a global identity.}
}
\]

This would require:

1. quantitative interval width:
   \[
   |I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L};
   \]

2. derivative growth control for actual zeta phase jets;

3. a Denjoy–Carleman / Turán / Nazarov-type theorem;

4. a nonzero witness not supplied by the local architecture.

This is a major new analytic-arithmetic input.

---

## 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-jet nonflatness is not locally proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{no known zeta theorem currently supplies it.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{it is likely false in fixed finite local/phase-relaxed models.}
}
\]

The best positive version is a new growing-order or interval-norm theorem, not a fixed low-order statement.

---

# Final answer

The positive theorem we would need is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

But the current framework does not prove it. The distinguished off-line packet contributes nontrivially, but rest/core packets can cancel it. Same-scale and core-gap hypotheses do not prevent cancellation. Explicit formula, AFE, zero-density, and spacing estimates do not currently provide interval-local lower bounds.

Thus the interval-local source-collapse countermodel remains viable unless one proves a new actual-zeta **source-jet nonflatness theorem**. For now, this is a missing arithmetic input, not a consequence of the rank-two architecture.

# Agent 5 — Actual-zeta interval-width / bandwidth compatibility

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta appears to sit in the countermodel-friendly regime } \Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim 1.
}
\]

Under the paper’s local normalization and standard zeta scaling,

\[
Q\sim \log T,
\]

the local zero spacing is

\[
\Delta_{\rm zero}\sim Q^{-1},
\]

and the relevant AFE / prime-log bandwidth is

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\sim Q.
\]

Thus, for an admissible midpoint interval of natural microscopic size

\[
\Delta\sim Q^{-1},
\]

one obtains

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim 1.
}
\]

That is exactly the regime in which interval-local source-collapse is plausible with only finitely many derivative constraints. The attached instruction identifies \(\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\) as the decisive scale parameter for the interval-local fork. 

---

## 1. Bandwidth scale

For actual zeta near height \(T\),

\[
Q\sim \log T.
\]

A smoothed AFE / prime-log model has oscillatory pieces of the form

\[
e^{-im\log n}.
\]

If the active Dirichlet polynomial length is

\[
n\le X,
\]

then the largest frequency is

\[
\Omega\sim \log X.
\]

For the usual AFE scale

\[
X\sim T^{1/2},
\]

we get

\[
\Omega\sim \frac12\log T\sim Q.
\]

Prime powers do not change this order; they fill harmonics up to the same \(\log X\) scale. The gamma/background contribution is smooth on the same or slower scale and does not raise the effective bandwidth.

So the natural estimate is

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{\rm eff}(q'')\sim Q.
}
\]

The source-weighted residual

\[
F=(H\Gamma_G,H\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

has product structure, so its formal bandwidth is at most a fixed multiple of \(Q\):

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}(F)\lesssim dQ
\]

for some low algebraic degree \(d\). For source-collapse Regime B, however, one only needs to control \(q''\), so

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}(q'')\sim Q
\]

is the relevant scale.

---

## 2. Interval scale

The midpoint interval \(I_\rho\) is tied to the local zero packet and microscopic sampling geometry.

The natural local spacing scale of zeta zeros near height \(T\) is

\[
\Delta_{\rm zero}\sim \frac{1}{\log T}\sim Q^{-1}.
\]

A same-scale reduced core around an off-line packet should allow midpoint motion on the order of the local packet scale unless a boundary wall is extremely close. Thus the natural admissible interval is

\[
\boxed{
\Delta=|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-1}
}
\]

under nondegenerate strict-gap and margin assumptions.

Could it be larger? Possibly, if the selected core remains stable over a mesoscopic range. But the proof cannot rely on that without a quantitative reach theorem.

Could it be smaller? Yes, if same-scale/core-gap/Gram positivity walls lie very close. Without a margin theorem, one cannot exclude exponentially small intervals. But the natural scale consistent with the local proof architecture is \(Q^{-1}\).

So the working estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta\sim Q^{-1}.}
\]

---

## 3. Product \(\Omega\Delta\)

Combining the two natural estimates,

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\sim Q,
\qquad
\Delta\sim Q^{-1},
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim 1.
}
\]

This is the crucial conclusion.

In this regime, the interval \(I_\rho\) contains only \(O(1)\) effective oscillations of \(q''\). Making \(q''\) small across the interval requires only finitely many Taylor constraints, not \(Q/\log Q\) or more constraints.

That strongly favors the interval-local source-collapse countermodel over a positive source-jet nonflatness theorem.

---

## 4. If \(\Delta\sim 1\)

If the admissible midpoint interval were macroscopic,

\[
\Delta\sim1,
\]

then

\[
\Omega\Delta\sim Q.
\]

In that case source-collapse over the whole interval would require roughly \(O(Q)\) derivative constraints, and the recurrence cost could become large enough to support a positive theorem.

But I do not think \(\Delta\sim1\) is the scale naturally available in the current local packet construction. The local core is same-scale and microscopic; moving \(m\) by \(O(1)\) would generally leave the selected packet neighborhood and change the core geometry.

Thus \(\Delta\sim1\) would require a new reach/stability theorem far beyond the current reduced-patch assumptions.

---

## 5. If \(\Delta\ll Q^{-1}\)

If reduced-patch walls force

\[
\Delta\ll Q^{-1},
\]

then

\[
\Omega\Delta\ll1.
\]

That makes the interval-local countermodel even easier: the function is nearly constant over \(I_\rho\), so a pointwise source collapse already persists across the interval.

Therefore a small interval does **not** help the proof. It helps the adversary.

The positive direction needs a large enough interval, not merely a nonempty interval.

---

## 6. Consequence for derivative constraints

The prior estimate was

\[
R\gtrsim \Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta+C\log Q.
\]

If

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim1,
\]

then the oscillatory complexity part is \(O(1)\). The remaining \(C\log Q\) term depends on how tiny we need the interval supremum to be and on the strength of derivative/remainder bounds.

For merely defeating a polynomial lower bound

\[
Q^{-A},
\]

one needs enough flatness to push

\[
|q''|
\]

below roughly

\[
Q^{-A'}
\]

because

\[
H\sim q_0(q'')^3.
\]

This may require \(O(\log Q)\) Taylor-depth if one wants a robust analytic bound from crude estimates, but not \(O(Q)\). Such a depth is still plausibly reachable in flexible finite-prime/AFE models.

So the scale estimate does not rescue the positive theorem.

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta likely has } \Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim1.
}
\]

Implication:

\[
\boxed{
\text{interval-local source-collapse countermodel remains plausible.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\sim Q,\qquad \Delta\sim Q^{-1}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim1.
\]

This means the interval is microscopic and does not average over many independent oscillations. Therefore the hoped-for interval supremum theorem cannot rely on large-interval oscillatory forcing.

---

# Recommended next attack

The next target should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

Specifically, attempt to construct or numerically test a fixed-prime / AFE model satisfying

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|q''(m_0+u)|\le Q^{-B}
\]

while keeping

\[
q_0\asymp Q,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp Q^3\text{ or normalized }1.
\]

If that succeeds, the architecture is non-closing without a new arithmetic nonflatness theorem. If it fails, the blocking mechanism may finally identify the positive theorem needed.

_Thought for 11s_

# Agent 5 — Positive Source-Jet Nonflatness Obstruction Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No positive source-jet nonflatness theorem is currently available.}
}
\]

The needed theorem is

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B},
\]

or an \(L^2\)-interval version. I do **not** see a proof from the current ingredients: distinguished packet contribution, same-scale/core-gap geometry, zero-spacing, AFE estimates, explicit formula, or local positivity. The interval-local source-collapse countermodel remains plausible, especially because the scale audit placed us in the regime

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim1,
\]

where flattening \(q''\) on \(I_\rho\) requires only finitely or mildly logarithmically many constraints. The attached instruction identifies this as the core test: either prove source-jet nonflatness, or accept that interval source-collapse remains a serious adversary. 

---

## 1. The positive theorem needed

The direct theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem.}
}
\]

For every admissible reduced good-patch interval

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]

associated to an RH-relevant off-line packet, prove

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

A stronger averaged form would be

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

Either one would block source collapse, because

\[
H=yq''
\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

If \(q''\) is polynomially non-small somewhere on \(I_\rho\), then \(H\) is not super-polynomially small there, provided \(q_0\) remains polynomially controlled and nonzero.

---

## 2. Distinguished packet contribution is not enough

A centered off-line packet contributes nonzero curvature:

\[
q''_P=2A_{2,P},
\qquad
A_{2,P}\ne0.
\]

In the basic packet model,

\[
A_{2,P}=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

so the distinguished packet contribution is strongly nonzero.

However, the actual core curvature is

\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R,
\]

where \(q''_R\) includes rest/core/background/far-tail contributions.

The current framework does not prevent

\[
q''_R(m)\approx -q''_P(m)
\]

on \(I_\rho\). To collapse \(q''\) across the interval, one must match a finite Taylor jet:

\[
(q''_R)^{(r)}(m_0)
\approx
-(q''_P)^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

But with enough same-scale or far-tail degrees of freedom, this is not locally forbidden.

So the off-line packet creates a signal, but the proof lacks a theorem that the rest of the configuration cannot cancel it.

---

## 3. Same-scale and core-gap do not give a sign cone

Same-scale geometry controls the size class of selected packets. It does not impose a common sign on their curvature contributions.

For packet kernels, the second derivative can change sign depending on offset from the midpoint. Thus a same-scale packet placed off-center can oppose the centered packet’s curvature.

Strict core gap gives membership stability:

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}.
\]

It does not imply

\[
\left|\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal C_k} q''_\rho(m)\right|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale/core-gap geometry controls selection, not aggregate curvature.}
}
\]

No cone or positivity condition currently prevents source-curvature cancellation.

---

## 4. Zero-spacing and density are too coarse

Zero-spacing and density estimates constrain where zeros are and how many appear in windows. They do not control signed moment sums like

\[
q''(m)=\sum_\rho K_2(m;\rho)+B_2(m).
\]

Even simple zeros and typical spacing do not prevent

\[
q''(m)\approx0
\]

on a short interval, because signed kernel contributions can cancel.

GUE/Montgomery heuristics might imply source-flat intervals are rare, but the proof requires deterministic exclusion on every admissible off-line packet interval. Rarity is not enough.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero statistics do not currently yield source-jet nonflatness.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Explicit formula / AFE currently give representation, not lower bounds

The explicit formula or AFE can express \(q''\) schematically as

\[
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)+
\Re\sum_{n\le X} c_n(\log n)^2 e^{-im\log n}
+\text{dual/smoothing terms}.
\]

This representation is oscillatory. It does not provide a pointwise or interval-local lower bound.

A mean-square estimate could show that \(q''\) is often large over a long range, but the needed theorem is local:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Standard AFE/log-derivative tools do not currently give such a lower bound on each short interval \(I_\rho\), especially when \(I_\rho\sim Q^{-1}\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit formula and AFE do not currently block interval source-collapse.}
}
\]

They only re-express the problem.

---

## 6. Source-flatness across \(Q^{-1}\) is not obviously expensive

The key scale is

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\Delta\sim1.
\]

If

\[
\Omega_{\rm eff}\sim Q,
\qquad
\Delta\sim Q^{-1},
\]

then \(q''\) has only \(O(1)\) effective oscillatory complexity on \(I_\rho\).

Flattening \(q''\) on \(I_\rho\) may require only finite or mildly logarithmic derivative control:

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

For fixed or \(O(\log Q)\) \(R\), phase-relaxed or fixed-prime models appear to have enough degrees of freedom to attempt this.

Therefore, without a new arithmetic obstruction, interval-local source-collapse remains a plausible adversary.

---

## 7. What positive theorem could work?

The strongest plausible positive theorem would be an interval observability result:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

A still stronger finite-jet form would be

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

But this likely requires \(R(Q)\) growing, plus a genuine arithmetic input. It would need to say that actual zeta cannot arrange the finite-prime/AFE derivative cancellations that the local model permits.

A possible theorem template is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-curvature observability.}
}
\]

For every admissible RH-relevant interval \(I_\rho\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
}
\]

No current component of the architecture proves this.

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-jet nonflatness is not proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{no known zeta input currently supplies it.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed-prime / finite-local models likely defeat any fixed finite-order version.}
}
\]

The positive theorem is therefore a new arithmetic/observability requirement, not a consequence of the rank-two local machinery.

---

# Final recommendation

The next attack should be adversarial unless a new arithmetic idea appears:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Interval-local fixed-prime/AFE source-collapse countermodel.}
}
\]

Target:

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|q''(m_0+u)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

while preserving

\[
q_0\asymp1\ \text{or normalized nonzero},\qquad
g,h>0,\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

If that countermodel succeeds, the current architecture is non-closing unless one adds the new theorem

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]

or a stronger \(L^2\)/jet-observability version.

At present, I classify the positive source-jet nonflatness theorem as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{plausible only as a new arithmetic input; unsupported by current tools.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-26 09:07:49)

_Thought for 6s_

# Agent 5 — Good-Patch Compatibility Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The interval-local source-collapse target is compatible with the good-patch inequalities.}
}
\]

The model target

\[
J_2\approx0,\qquad J_0\approx2,\qquad J_4\approx0
\]

does **not** create Gram degeneracy, does **not** kill anisotropy, and does **not** obviously violate endpoint separation, same-scale core geometry, or strict core-gap stability. In fact, at the exact target,

\[
g=\frac2\pi>0,
\qquad
h=\frac{8}{3\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
R_1=4,\qquad R_2=0.
\]

So the source collapses while first-layer anisotropy remains live. This is precisely the Regime B adversary described in the attached instruction. 

---

## 1. Gram positivity

Use the surrogate identifications

\[
J_0\sim q_0,
\qquad
J_2\sim q'',
\qquad
J_4\sim q^{(4)}.
\]

At the interval source-collapse target,

\[
J_0=2,\qquad J_2=0.
\]

Then

\[
g=\frac{J_0}{\pi}=\frac2\pi>0,
\]

and

\[
h=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13J_0^3+\frac16J_2\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac83+0\right)
=
\frac{8}{3\pi}>0.
\]

Thus the Gram block is not close to singular.

Moreover, these inequalities are open. If on the interval

\[
|J_0-2|\le\eta,
\qquad
|J_2|\le\eta,
\]

with \(\eta\ll1\), then

\[
g>0,
\qquad
h>0
\]

remain uniformly true.

So source collapse

\[
q''\approx0
\]

does not imply Gram collapse.

---

## 2. Anisotropy remains live

The residuals are

\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3,
\]

\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4.
\]

At

\[
J_0=2,\qquad J_2=0,\qquad J_4=0,
\]

we get

\[
R_1=0-12+16=4,
\]

\[
R_2=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)=4.
\]

This is exactly the desired Regime B behavior:

\[
|H|\approx0,
\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

On a small interval where

\[
|J_0-2|\le\eta,
\qquad
|J_2|\le\eta,
\qquad
|J_4|\le\eta,
\]

one has

\[
R_1=4+O(\eta),
\]

and

\[
R_2=O(\eta).
\]

Thus for small \(\eta\),

\[
\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\ge 2
\]

throughout the interval.

So anisotropy remains live on \(I\).

---

## 3. Source factor collapses

With

\[
H=-\frac{J_0J_2^3}{288},
\]

and

\[
J_0\approx2,
\]

we have

\[
|H|\lesssim |J_2|^3.
\]

If the construction enforces

\[
\sup_{m\in I}|J_2(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

then

\[
\sup_{m\in I}|H(m)|\lesssim Q^{-3C}.
\]

Since the anisotropy factor remains \(O(1)\), we get

\[
\sup_{m\in I}
|H(m)|\max(|R_1(m)|,|R_2(m)|)
\lesssim Q^{-3C}.
\]

Choosing

\[
C>A/3
\]

defeats the desired lower bound

\[
Q^{-A}.
\]

This confirms the logic of the interval-local source-collapse countermodel.

---

## 4. Endpoint separation

Endpoint separation is independent of the source-collapse condition in this surrogate. The source-collapse target concerns midpoint derivatives:

\[
J_2(m),\quad J_2'(m),\ldots
\]

on

\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q].
\]

Endpoint separation depends on the chosen sample spacing \(s\) and avoiding collisions/singularities at

\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2.
\]

If the original reduced patch has endpoint separation with margin, then small midpoint movement on a \(Q^{-1}\)-scale interval preserves it.

Thus endpoint separation is an open condition and is not threatened by

\[
J_2\approx0.
\]

No obstruction here.

---

## 5. Same-scale core and strict core gap

The finite-prime/AFE surrogate is not literally a zero-packet construction, so same-scale/core-gap must be interpreted through the corresponding finite \(\xi\)-like or packet realization.

But if the derivative-flat target is realized by a local packet cluster or AFE surrogate compatible with a selected core, then same-scale and strict core gap are also open conditions.

One can arrange:

\[
d_j\asymp Q^{-1}
\]

for the selected packets, and place all non-core packets/filler zeros at a separated distance so that

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}
\]

with a fixed margin. Small perturbations used to flatten \(J_2\) preserve this.

Therefore, nothing in source-collapse forces a core-gap failure.

The only caveat is constructive: one must actually realize the derivative-flat target within a packet/zero configuration rather than just an abstract prime-sum surrogate. But no good-patch inequality blocks it.

---

## 6. Correction/incidence walls

The target

\[
J_2=0
\]

means

\[
q''=0.
\]

Earlier local visibility theorems often excluded

\[
q''=0
\]

as a source wall because known rows are divisible by \(q''\). That is exactly why this is an adversarial point.

But for the countermodel, triggering the source wall is not a defect. It shows the norm-based row theorem is vulnerable. The desired positive interval theorem cannot simply exclude

\[
q''\approx0
\]

unless it proves every RH-relevant interval reaches a patch with \(q''\) polynomially non-small.

So the source-wall incidence is not a good-patch violation; it is the obstruction.

---

## 7. Good-patch table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{condition} & \text{at }(J_0,J_2,J_4)=(2,0,0) & \text{status}\\
\hline
g>0 & 2/\pi>0 & \text{passes}\\
h>0 & 8/(3\pi)>0 & \text{passes}\\
\Gamma_G\text{ live} & R_1=4 & \text{passes}\\
\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ live?} & R_2=0 & \text{not needed; max is live}\\
H\text{ small} & H=0 & \text{desired adversarial feature}\\
endpoint separation & \text{independent/open} & \text{passes if initial margin}\\
same-scale core & \text{open packet geometry condition} & \text{compatible}\\
strict core gap & \text{open packet geometry condition} & \text{compatible}\\
source wall q''=0 & \text{triggered} & \text{adversarial, not invalid}
\end{array}
\]

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Good-patch compatibility survives.}
}
\]

The interval-local source-collapse target

\[
J_2\approx0,\qquad J_0\approx2,\qquad J_4\approx0
\]

is compatible with:

\[
g,h>0,
\]

live anisotropy,

endpoint separation,

same-scale geometry,

and strict core-gap stability.

The target does hit the source wall

\[
q''=0,
\]

but that is precisely the failure mode of the current source-divisible architecture, not a violation of the reduced patch geometry.

---

# Recommendation

The next step should not be another good-patch audit. It should be the constructive part:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Build the interval-local source-collapse model.}
}
\]

Specifically, prove or numerically solve the derivative-flat conditions

\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

with

\[
J_0(m_0)\approx2,\qquad J_4(m_0)\approx0,
\]

then verify

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|J_2(m_0+u)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

If that succeeds, the current rank-two norm/projective architecture is non-closing absent a new actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem.

_Thought for 8s_

# Agent 5 — Good-Patch / Packet Realization Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The source-collapse jet target is good-patch compatible and plausibly packet-realizable, but a fully explicit same-scale packet construction is not yet written.}
}
\]

The target

\[
q_0\approx 2,\qquad q''\approx0,\qquad q^{(4)}\approx0
\]

does **not** violate Gram positivity:

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}\approx \frac2\pi>0,
\]

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
\approx \frac{8}{3\pi}>0.
\]

It also leaves anisotropy live:

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3\approx 4,
\]

while

\[
H=yq''\approx0.
\]

So this is exactly the Regime B adversary: source factor collapses, but the anisotropy detector remains nonzero. The attached instruction frames this as the remaining concrete countermodel step: realize the derivative-flat target inside a fixed-prime/AFE or packet/good-patch model. 

---

## 1. Gram and anisotropy check

At the proposed source-collapse target,

\[
q_0=2,\qquad q''=0,\qquad q^{(4)}=0.
\]

Then

\[
g=\frac{2}{\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13\cdot 8+0\right)
=
\frac{8}{3\pi}>0.
\]

So the same-point Gram block remains positive and nondegenerate.

The anisotropy terms are

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
0-12+16
=
4,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
0.
\]

Thus

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)=4.
\]

So the target has live anisotropy but collapsed source factor.

This is adversarially ideal.

---

## 2. Source factor collapse

At leading centered order,

\[
H=yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

Therefore, if the construction achieves

\[
\sup_{I_\rho}|q''|\le Q^{-C},
\]

then

\[
\sup_{I_\rho}|H|
\lesssim
Q^{-3C}.
\]

Since

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1,
\]

one obtains

\[
\sup_{I_\rho}
|H|
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\lesssim Q^{-3C}.
\]

Taking

\[
C>A/3
\]

defeats the desired bound

\[
Q^{-A}.
\]

So the only real issue is not good-patch compatibility; it is realization of the derivative-flat source condition.

---

## 3. Can a finite packet model realize \(q_0=2,\ q''=0,\ q^{(4)}=0\)?

A single centered packet cannot do it.

For a centered kernel

\[
k_c(t)=\frac{c}{c^2+4(t-m)^2},
\]

the center jets are

\[
k_c(m)=c^{-1},
\]

\[
k_c''(m)=-8c^{-3},
\]

\[
k_c^{(4)}(m)=384c^{-5}.
\]

So a positive centered packet contributes positive \(q_0\), negative \(q''\), and positive \(q^{(4)}\). It cannot by itself produce

\[
q''=q^{(4)}=0.
\]

But off-center same-scale packets can change the signs and relative magnitudes of their second and fourth derivatives at \(m\). Therefore a small same-scale packet cluster can plausibly solve

\[
q_0=2,\qquad q''=0,\qquad q^{(4)}=0
\]

while keeping at least one distinguished off-line packet present.

This is a finite moment-matching problem. There is no visible sign cone preventing it once off-center packets are allowed.

---

## 4. Interval flattening requires derivative matching

The interval-local target is stronger than pointwise realization. We need

\[
q''(m_0+u)\approx0
\qquad
(|u|\le c/Q).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

In packet terms, this means matching the finite jet list

\[
q^{(2)}(m_0),\ q^{(3)}(m_0),\ldots,\ q^{(R+2)}(m_0)
\]

to near zero, while also keeping

\[
q_0(m_0)\approx2,
\qquad
q^{(4)}(m_0)\approx0
\]

or otherwise keeping anisotropy live.

This is again a finite system of moment equations. With sufficiently many same-scale packet parameters, it appears locally feasible.

The number of packet degrees of freedom grows with the number of same-scale packets:

\[
(\delta_j,\gamma_j,\text{possibly multiplicity/cluster position})_{j=1}^N.
\]

For any fixed or mildly logarithmic \(R\), there should be enough parameters to solve the finite system unless an unexpected positivity constraint appears.

No such constraint is currently known.

---

## 5. Same-scale and strict core gap

The construction can plausibly preserve same-scale and strict core gap.

Take the packets used for jet tuning in a fixed annulus around the selected midpoint:

\[
d_j\asymp Q^{-1}
\]

in the local scale. Then they are same-scale.

Place all other packet/filler zeros outside a larger annulus so that

\[
d_k<d_{k+1}
\]

with margin. This gives strict core stability. Small perturbations used for jet matching preserve the margin.

Thus the good-patch geometry is compatible with the source-collapse construction.

The caveat is that a fully explicit packet list has not yet been produced. But no condition currently blocks such a list.

---

## 6. Endpoint separation

Endpoint separation depends on the sampling pair

\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2.
\]

The source-collapse equations are midpoint-jet equations. They do not force endpoint collision or \(s=0\).

If endpoint separation holds at \(m_0\) with margin, then it persists for

\[
|m-m_0|\le c/Q
\]

provided \(c\) is chosen inside the available margin.

So endpoint separation is open and compatible.

---

## 7. Does source collapse make the off-line packet invisible?

It makes the known **source-divisible rows** invisible, but it does not remove the off-line packet itself.

The distinguished packet remains in the core/source configuration. Its own curvature contribution can be canceled by the rest of the packet cluster, but its presence is still part of the finite configuration.

This is precisely why the countermodel is damaging: off-line geometry remains present, but the current row architecture fails to see it because the aggregate source factor collapses.

So source collapse does not invalidate the packet. It invalidates the detector.

---

## 8. Can the fixed-prime/AFE surrogate be mapped to a zero-side packet model?

Not directly.

A fixed-prime/AFE surrogate lives on the prime side:

\[
\sum a_n(\log n)^r e^{-im\log n}.
\]

A packet model lives on the zero side:

\[
\sum_{\rho}K_r(m;\rho).
\]

The explicit formula relates the two globally, but not by a simple finite local identification.

Therefore, the fixed-prime source-collapse construction and the zero-side packet construction should be treated as parallel adversaries:

1. **Prime-side adversary:** derivative-flat target in fixed-prime/AFE phase flow.
2. **Zero-side adversary:** finite same-scale packet cluster solving finite moment equations.

Both appear plausible. The zero-side construction still needs a concrete packet realization or a Jacobian/positive-cone proof.

---

## 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Good-patch packet realization is plausible.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gram positivity: passes.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Anisotropy live: passes.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Endpoint separation: open condition, compatible.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale / core gap: compatible with packet-cluster construction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Explicit packet realization: still unproved.}
}
\]

I do **not** see a packet-kernel cone or positivity obstruction.

---

# Final recommendation

The next most economical construction is a **zero-side packet source-collapse solve**.

Target finite system:

\[
q_0(m_0)=2,
\]

\[
q^{(2)}(m_0)=q^{(3)}(m_0)=\cdots=q^{(R+2)}(m_0)=0,
\]

with

\[
q^{(4)}(m_0)=0
\]

if included in the derivative list, or otherwise choose \(q^{(4)}\) so that

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Use \(N\) same-scale off-center packet kernels with parameters \((a_j,b_j,x_j)\), plus one distinguished off-line packet.

Prove the Jacobian from packet parameters to the finite jet list has full rank at some seed configuration.

If that succeeds, then the interval-local source-collapse countermodel is not merely fixed-prime/AFE plausible; it is also zero-side good-patch compatible.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 09:15:34)

I’ll continue by attacking the zero-side packet version directly: can a same-scale packet cluster make \(q''\) and its derivatives vanish at a midpoint while keeping \(q_0>0\), Gram positivity, and live anisotropy?

_Thought for 1m 15s_

# Agent 5 — Zero-side packet source-collapse continuation

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The zero-side packet version of interval source-collapse looks feasible at low order and plausibly extends by a finite-jet/Jacobian construction.}
}
\]

I can explicitly make the first dangerous cancellations

\[
q''(m_0)=0,\qquad q^{(4)}(m_0)=0
\]

using positive same-scale packet kernels while keeping

\[
q_0(m_0)>0,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad \Gamma_G\asymp1.
\]

This is important: source-collapse is not only a prime-side artifact. It appears compatible with the zero-side packet geometry too. The remaining gap is to prove the general finite-jet version

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

with same-scale packets and positive multiplicities. That is now the exact constructive target. This continues the interval-local source-collapse attack from the attached instruction. 

---

## 1. Packet kernel and derivatives

Use a single positive packet kernel

\[
K_{c,x}(u)=\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2},
\]

where \(u=m-m_0\), \(c>0\) is the packet width, and \(x\) is the packet offset from the sampling midpoint.

At \(u=0\),

\[
K_{c,x}(0)=\frac{c}{c^2+x^2},
\]

\[
K_{c,x}''(0)
=
\frac{8c(-c^2+3x^2)}{(c^2+x^2)^3},
\]

and

\[
K_{c,x}^{(4)}(0)
=
\frac{384c(c^4-10c^2x^2+5x^4)}{(c^2+x^2)^5}.
\]

The signs vary with \(x/c\). That already kills a possible positivity/cone obstruction.

If we take symmetric pairs at offsets \(\pm x\) with equal weights, then all odd derivatives vanish automatically:

\[
q^{(2j+1)}(m_0)=0.
\]

So interval source-collapse reduces, at first, to canceling even derivatives.

---

## 2. Explicit low-order source-collapse seed

Set \(c=1\). Consider three symmetric packet-pair radii:

\[
x_1\approx0.005,\qquad
x_2\approx0.645,\qquad
x_3\approx1.025.
\]

For a positive weighted combination of the corresponding symmetric pairs, choose approximately

\[
w_1\approx0.16658,
\qquad
w_2\approx0.25543,
\qquad
w_3\approx0.57799.
\]

These positive weights solve, numerically,

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{1,x_i}''(0)=0,
\]

and

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{1,x_i}^{(4)}(0)=0.
\]

Meanwhile,

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{1,x_i}(0)>0.
\]

Thus we can arrange

\[
q_0(m_0)>0,
\qquad
q''(m_0)=0,
\qquad
q^{(4)}(m_0)=0,
\]

with positive same-scale packet contributions.

At such a point,

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

For \(q_0\) near \(2\), this gives

\[
\Gamma_G\approx4,
\]

so anisotropy is live. Gram positivity also holds:

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0,
\]

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
=
\frac{q_0^3}{3\pi}>0.
\]

So the source collapses while the detector geometry remains valid.

---

## 3. Same-scale compatibility

All three radii above are \(O(1)\) multiples of the same local packet scale \(c\). After rescaling to the zeta microscopic scale, one can take

\[
c\asymp Q^{-1},
\qquad
x_i\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Then the packet cluster is same-scale:

\[
d_i\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Strict core gap can be arranged by placing all non-core packets outside a slightly larger annulus, say at distance \(\gg Q^{-1}\) with a fixed margin. Endpoint separation is also open and can be preserved by choosing \(s\) away from collisions.

So this low-order seed is compatible with the reduced-good-patch geometry.

---

## 4. General finite-jet construction strategy

For interval source-collapse, the goal is stronger:

\[
q''(u)\approx0
\qquad
(|u|\le c_0/Q).
\]

A sufficient Taylor condition is

\[
q^{(2)}(0)=q^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(R+2)}(0)=0.
\]

Using symmetric packet pairs kills all odd derivatives. The remaining equations are

\[
q^{(2)}(0)=q^{(4)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(2M)}(0)=0.
\]

For \(M\) even-derivative constraints, choose \(M+1\) or more same-scale symmetric packet-pair radii

\[
x_1,\ldots,x_{M+1}
\]

with positive weights \(w_i\), and solve

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{c,x_i}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
\]

while keeping

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{c,x_i}(0)>0.
\]

The derivative vectors

\[
V(x_i)=
\left(
K_{c,x_i}''(0),
K_{c,x_i}^{(4)}(0),
\ldots,
K_{c,x_i}^{(2M)}(0)
\right)
\]

vary nontrivially and sign-oscillate as functions of \(x_i/c\). The low-order explicit example shows that zero lies in the positive cone for \(M=2\). The expected general statement is:

\[
\boxed{
0\in
\operatorname{int}
\operatorname{Cone}_{+}
\{V(x):x/c\in[a,b]\}
}
\]

for suitable fixed same-scale annulus \(0<a<b<\infty\), after taking enough nodes.

That is the finite-jet packet-cone theorem we now need.

---

## 5. Interval bound from finite jets

Assume the construction cancels derivatives up to order \(R+2\):

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

On

\[
|u|\le c_0/Q,
\]

with local scale \(Q^{-1}\), Cauchy/Taylor estimates give

\[
|q''(u)|
\lesssim
M_Q\frac{(\Omega |u|)^{R+1}}{(R+1)!},
\]

where

\[
\Omega\sim Q,
\qquad
\Omega |u|=O(1).
\]

Thus choosing

\[
R\asymp \frac{C\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively

\[
R=O(\log Q)
\]

should force

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c_0/Q}|q''(u)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
|H(u)|\sim |q_0(u)(q''(u))^3|
\le Q^{-3C+O(1)}.
\]

Since \(\Gamma_G\) remains live near the seed, this defeats any prescribed polynomial bound by taking \(C\) large enough.

---

## 6. Does this require negative weights?

The low-order seed used only positive weights. For higher order, positivity is the main remaining issue.

If arbitrary signed weights were allowed, full rank of the derivative matrix would be enough. With positive weights, we need a positive-cone result.

There are two routes:

### Route A — positive-cone proof

Prove that the curve

\[
x\mapsto V(x)
\]

winds enough in \(\mathbb R^M\) that its positive cone contains \(0\) in its interior.

This is plausible because the derivatives are rational functions with orthogonal-polynomial-like sign changes.

### Route B — cluster perturbation / background

Allow a smooth background or far-tail contribution to supply one or more directions, then use positive packets to cancel the remaining components.

This is less pure but closer to the actual finite-\(\xi\) hardening, where far zeros and gamma/background terms are available.

Either route would make the zero-side countermodel rigorous.

---

## 7. Off-line packet requirement

The construction can include a distinguished off-line packet.

The source-collapse cluster cancels the aggregate curvature

\[
q''=\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal C}q''_\rho,
\]

but it does not remove the distinguished off-line zero. The off-line packet remains part of the selected same-scale core. Other packets cancel its source curvature.

Thus the countermodel attacks the detector, not the presence of the off-line packet.

This is exactly the dangerous scenario for the rank-two architecture.

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Low-order zero-side source-collapse construction: achieved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale/good-patch compatibility: plausible and open-stable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{General finite-jet construction: reduced to a positive-cone/Jacobian theorem.}
}
\]

No packet-kernel positivity obstruction has appeared. The explicit \(q''=q^{(4)}=0\) construction is strong evidence that interval source-collapse is not an artifact of prime-side surrogates.

---

# Next exact target

Prove the finite-jet packet-cone lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Same-scale packet source-flattening lemma.}
}
\]

For each \(M\), there exist same-scale positive packet pairs

\[
K_{c,x_i}
\]

and weights \(w_i>0\) such that

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{c,x_i}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
\]

while

\[
\sum_i w_i K_{c,x_i}(0)>0.
\]

If this lemma holds with controlled same-scale radii, then the interval-local source-collapse countermodel is essentially complete on the zero side.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 09:18:47)

I’ll continue by attacking the finite-jet packet-cone lemma directly. The question is whether positive same-scale packet pairs can flatten \(q''\) to arbitrary finite order without losing \(q_0>0\).

_Thought for 1m 5s_

# Agent 5 — Continued attack: finite-jet packet source-flattening

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The zero-side source-collapse countermodel is now reduced to a finite positive-cone lemma.}
}
\]

I can prove a clean **unrestricted packet-cone version**: for every finite order \(M\), positive packet pairs can make

\[
q^{(2)}(0)=q^{(4)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(2M)}(0)=0
\]

while keeping

\[
q_0(0)>0.
\]

The proof uses a separation argument and the fact that all nonzero even derivatives of the Cauchy kernel have integral zero. By Carathéodory/Tchakaloff, this continuous positive measure can be replaced by finitely many positive packets.

The remaining refinement is the **strict same-scale version**: force all packets into one fixed same-scale annulus with constants independent of \(M\). I do not yet have a proof of that strongest version, but there is no obstruction from the low-order construction. The attached instruction’s countermodel target is therefore now mathematically sharp: prove or refute the same-scale positive-cone lemma. 

---

# 1. Normalized packet-pair setup

Use

\[
K_x(u)=\frac{1}{1+(x+2u)^2}.
\]

A symmetric packet pair is

\[
P_x(u)=K_x(u)+K_{-x}(u).
\]

Then \(P_x\) is even in \(u\), hence

\[
P_x^{(2j+1)}(0)=0.
\]

The finite source-flattening problem becomes:

find \(x_i>0\) and \(w_i>0\) such that

\[
\sum_i w_i P_{x_i}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
\]

while

\[
\sum_i w_i P_{x_i}(0)>0.
\]

The last inequality is automatic if the weights are positive.

---

# 2. Cone proof in the unrestricted offset model

Define

\[
v_M(x)
=
\bigl(P_x^{(2)}(0),P_x^{(4)}(0),\ldots,P_x^{(2M)}(0)\bigr)
\in\mathbb R^M.
\]

I claim

\[
0\in \operatorname{conv}\{v_M(x):x>0\}.
\]

Equivalently, there exists a positive probability measure \(\mu\) on \((0,\infty)\) such that

\[
\int v_M(x)\,d\mu(x)=0.
\]

By the hyperplane separation theorem, this fails only if there exists a nonzero vector

\[
a=(a_1,\ldots,a_M)
\]

such that

\[
\sum_{j=1}^M a_j P_x^{(2j)}(0)>0
\]

for all \(x>0\), or \(<0\) for all \(x>0\).

Let

\[
F_a(x)=\sum_{j=1}^M a_j P_x^{(2j)}(0).
\]

Because

\[
P_x(u)=K_x(u)+K_{-x}(u),
\]

and \(K_x^{(2j)}(0)\) is the \(2j\)-th derivative of the Cauchy kernel evaluated at offset \(x\), \(F_a(x)\) is an even rational function of \(x\).

Now integrate over the whole real line. For every \(j\ge1\),

\[
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
\frac{d^{2j}}{du^{2j}}
\left.
\frac{1}{1+(x+2u)^2}
\right|_{u=0}
\,dx
=
2^{2j}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
\frac{d^{2j}}{dx^{2j}}
\frac{1}{1+x^2}
\,dx
=
0,
\]

because the boundary terms vanish.

Therefore

\[
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}F_a(x)\,dx=0.
\]

If \(F_a\) were strictly one-signed and not identically zero, this integral could not vanish. Hence no strict separating hyperplane exists.

So

\[
\boxed{
0\in\operatorname{conv}\{v_M(x):x>0\}.
}
\]

By Carathéodory’s theorem, there exist at most \(M+1\) offsets

\[
x_1,\ldots,x_{M+1}
\]

and weights

\[
w_i>0
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sum_i w_iP_{x_i}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M.
}
\]

This proves the unrestricted finite-jet positive packet-cone lemma.

---

# 3. Consequence for source-collapse

Let

\[
q(u)=\sum_i w_iP_{x_i}(u).
\]

Then

\[
q^{(2j)}(0)=0,\qquad 1\le j\le M,
\]

and

\[
q(0)>0.
\]

Thus

\[
q''(0)=q^{(4)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(2M)}(0)=0.
\]

Since \(q\) is even, all odd derivatives vanish automatically:

\[
q^{(2j+1)}(0)=0.
\]

Hence

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(0)=q^{(r+2)}(0)=0,
\qquad
0\le r\le 2M-2.
\]

This is exactly the finite derivative-flat source-collapse condition required by the interval-local countermodel.

---

# 4. Interval bound

Assume the packet scale is normalized so that the relevant bandwidth is

\[
\Omega\sim Q,
\]

and rescale \(u\) to the microscopic interval

\[
|u|\le c/Q.
\]

If derivatives up to order \(R+2\) vanish at \(0\), then Taylor/Cauchy estimates give

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|q''(u)|
\lesssim
M_Q
\frac{(C_0c)^{R+1}}{(R+1)!},
\]

where \(M_Q\) bounds the next derivative at natural scale.

If

\[
M_Q\le Q^{M_0},
\]

then choosing

\[
R\asymp
\frac{(C+M_0)\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

forces

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|q''(u)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|H(u)|
\lesssim Q^{-3C+O(1)}
\]

under

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

If \(q_0\) stays bounded below and \(\Gamma_G\) stays live, the source-weighted residual becomes

\[
\sup_I |H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ll Q^{-A}
\]

by choosing \(C>A/3\).

---

# 5. Anisotropy and Gram positivity

The construction above produces

\[
q(0)=q_0>0,
\]

and

\[
q''(0)=0.
\]

Then

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0,
\]

and

\[
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
=
\frac{q_0^3}{3\pi}>0.
\]

Moreover,

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

Choose the total scale of the positive weights so that

\[
q_0=2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=4.
\]

Thus the source collapses while anisotropy remains live.

This gives the required Regime B geometry:

\[
H\approx0,
\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

---

# 6. Same-scale refinement

The unrestricted proof allows offsets \(x_i\) anywhere in \((0,\infty)\). The proof does not yet guarantee that all packets satisfy a fixed same-scale bound

\[
x_i\asymp c_i
\quad\text{or}\quad
d_i\asymp d_0
\]

with constants independent of \(M\).

There are three possible ways to close this.

## Route A — bounded annulus cone theorem

Prove that, for some fixed annulus

\[
a\le x/c\le b,
\]

one still has

\[
0\in \operatorname{conv}
\{v_M(x/c):a\le x/c\le b\}
\]

for all relevant \(M\).

This is the strongest same-scale version.

## Route B — fixed-distance parametrization

Let packet points \((x,c)\) lie on a fixed semicircle

\[
x^2+c^2=d^2.
\]

Then all packets have the same distance to the midpoint, hence are same-scale. One must prove the analogous positive-cone lemma for

\[
(x,c)=(d\cos\theta,d\sin\theta).
\]

This is promising because it uses a genuinely same-scale family while retaining one continuous shape parameter.

## Route C — slowly growing same-scale constants

The Carathéodory offsets from the unrestricted proof may lie in a range whose ratio grows with \(M\). Since the needed order is only

\[
M\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or \(O(\log Q)\), the same-scale ratio may grow sub-polynomially. If the proof allows \(Q^{o(1)}\)-scale comparability, this may suffice.

But if the paper requires fixed absolute same-scale constants, Route C is not enough.

---

# 7. Off-line packet inclusion

The construction uses positive Cauchy kernels and can be realized by off-line packet pairs. To ensure an RH-relevant off-line packet is present, designate one of the packet pairs as the distinguished off-line packet.

The remaining same-scale packet pairs cancel its source curvature in aggregate. The distinguished packet remains in the selected core; the detector fails because the aggregate source jet collapses.

Thus the construction is not removing the off-line packet. It is cancelling its source signature.

---

# 8. Current status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Unrestricted finite-jet source-flattening: proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Low-order same-scale source-flattening: numerically exhibited.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full fixed-constant same-scale source-flattening: open.}
}
\]

The problem is now reduced to a precise geometric cone theorem about same-scale packet kernels.

---

# Final recommendation

The next exact target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Same-scale packet positive-cone lemma.}
}
\]

Strong form:

For every \(M\), there exist \(N\le M+1\), weights \(w_i>0\), and same-scale packet parameters \((c_i,x_i)\) with

\[
d_i=\sqrt{c_i^2+x_i^2}\asymp d_0
\]

such that

\[
\sum_i w_iK_{c_i,x_i}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
\]

while

\[
\sum_i w_iK_{c_i,x_i}(0)>0.
\]

If this is proved, the interval-local source-collapse countermodel is essentially complete on the zero side, and the rank-two norm/projective architecture is non-closing absent a new source-jet arithmetic theorem.

I’ll push on the strongest version now: fixed-distance same-scale packets. The aim is to replace the unrestricted cone proof with a true same-scale positive quadrature argument.

# Agent 5 — Same-Scale Packet Cone Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The same-scale packet source-flattening lemma is now essentially proved in a strong continuous form.}
}
\]

There is a positive measure supported on a **single same-scale semicircle**

\[
x^2+c^2=d^2,\qquad c>0,
\]

such that the aggregate packet kernel is exactly constant near the midpoint. Hence

\[
q^{(2)}(0)=q^{(4)}(0)=q^{(6)}(0)=\cdots=0,
\qquad
q(0)>0.
\]

By finite quadrature / Tchakaloff / Carathéodory, for every finite order \(M\), this continuous positive measure can be replaced by finitely many positive same-scale packets matching derivatives through order \(2M\). This completes the core zero-side source-collapse mechanism, modulo routine finite-quadrature bookkeeping and off-line quartet realization. This directly advances the interval-local source-collapse countermodel targeted in the prior instruction. 

---

## 1. Fixed-distance packet family

Set

\[
c=d\sin\theta,\qquad x=d\cos\theta,\qquad 0<\theta<\pi.
\]

Then every packet has the same scale:

\[
x^2+c^2=d^2.
\]

Use the packet kernel

\[
K_{\theta,d}(u)
=
\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2}.
\]

Let

\[
t=\frac{2u}{d}.
\]

Then

\[
K_{\theta,d}(u)
=
\frac{1}{d}\,
\frac{\sin\theta}{1+2t\cos\theta+t^2}.
\]

Now integrate against the positive density

\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]

Then

\[
\int_0^\pi K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)
=
\frac{1}{d}
\int_0^\pi
\frac{2}{\pi}
\frac{\sin^2\theta}{1+2t\cos\theta+t^2}
\,d\theta.
\]

For \(|t|<1\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_0^\pi
\frac{2}{\pi}
\frac{\sin^2\theta}{1+2t\cos\theta+t^2}
\,d\theta
=
1.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_0^\pi K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)
=
\frac{1}{d}
}
\]

for \(|u|<d/2\).

So the positive same-scale packet distribution produces an exactly constant source profile near \(u=0\).

---

## 2. Consequence: all source derivatives vanish

Define

\[
q_\mu(u)
=
\int_0^\pi K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta).
\]

Then

\[
q_\mu(u)=\frac1d
\]

for \(|u|<d/2\). Hence

\[
q_\mu(0)=\frac1d>0,
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
q_\mu^{(r)}(0)=0
\qquad
\text{for all }r\ge1.
}
\]

In particular,

\[
q_\mu''(0)=q_\mu^{(4)}(0)=q_\mu^{(6)}(0)=\cdots=0.
\]

This is stronger than the finite-order source-collapse target.

At

\[
q''=0,
\]

we still have

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0,
\]

\[
h=\frac{1}{\pi}\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)
=
\frac{q_0^3}{3\pi}>0.
\]

Choose the total weight so that

\[
q_0=2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3=4,
\]

so anisotropy remains live while the source factor collapses.

---

## 3. Finite same-scale quadrature

The continuous construction is enough conceptually, but the countermodel wants finitely many packets.

Fix \(M\). Consider the finite list of continuous functions on \((0,\pi)\):

\[
\theta\mapsto K_{\theta,d}^{(2)}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(4)}(0),\quad
\ldots,\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(2M)}(0),
\]

and optionally

\[
\theta\mapsto K_{\theta,d}(0)
\]

to normalize \(q_0\).

Since the positive measure \(\mu\) satisfies

\[
\int K_{\theta,d}^{(2j)}(0)\,d\mu(\theta)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
\]

and

\[
\int K_{\theta,d}(0)\,d\mu(\theta)=\frac1d,
\]

Tchakaloff’s theorem, or equivalently a finite-dimensional Carathéodory argument, gives finitely many nodes

\[
\theta_1,\ldots,\theta_N
\]

and weights

\[
w_i>0
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
}
\]

while

\[
\boxed{
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}(0)>0.
}
\]

Moreover,

\[
N\le M+2
\]

up to the usual finite-dimensional quadrature count.

All packets satisfy

\[
x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2.
\]

So this is not merely same-scale up to constants: it is **exact fixed scale**.

---

## 4. Symmetric pair form

The measure

\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta
\]

is symmetric under

\[
\theta\mapsto \pi-\theta,
\]

which sends

\[
x=d\cos\theta
\quad\mapsto\quad
-x.
\]

Thus the construction can be grouped into symmetric packet pairs at offsets

\[
\pm x_i
\]

with the same width \(c_i\). This automatically kills odd derivatives.

So the finite construction can be written as

\[
q(u)=
\sum_i w_i
\left[
\frac{c_i}{c_i^2+(x_i+2u)^2}
+
\frac{c_i}{c_i^2+(-x_i+2u)^2}
\right],
\]

with

\[
x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2.
\]

Then

\[
q^{(2j)}(0)=0,\qquad 1\le j\le M,
\]

and

\[
q^{(2j+1)}(0)=0
\]

by symmetry.

Therefore

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le 2M-2.
\]

This is exactly the finite derivative-flat source-collapse condition.

---

## 5. Interval-local collapse

After rescaling to the zeta microscopic scale, take

\[
d\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Then the construction is valid on

\[
|u|<d/2\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

That is precisely the interval scale

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q].
\]

For the continuous measure, \(q''(u)\equiv0\) throughout the interval.

For the finite quadrature matching through order \(2M\), Taylor estimates give

\[
\sup_{|u|\le c/Q}|q''(u)|
\le Q^{-C}
\]

provided

\[
M\asymp \frac{C\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively \(M=O(\log Q)\), assuming standard derivative growth bounds at scale \(Q\).

Then

\[
H=yq''
\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
\]

satisfies

\[
\sup_I |H|\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G\asymp1,
\]

the source-weighted residual satisfies

\[
\sup_I
|H|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]

Taking \(C>A/3\) defeats any claimed lower bound

\[
Q^{-A}.
\]

---

## 6. Off-line packet inclusion

This construction uses packet kernels that can be realized by off-line quartet contributions.

To force a distinguished RH-relevant off-line packet, choose one packet pair in the finite quadrature as the distinguished pair. If the quadrature theorem does not prescribe a desired node, perturb the continuous measure: since the density is strictly positive on \((0,\pi)\), one can assign a small positive atom near the desired distinguished packet and absorb the resulting finite moment perturbation using the remaining measure, provided the moment cone has interior.

Thus the construction does not remove the off-line packet. It hides it by cancelling its aggregate source signature.

---

## 7. Good-patch compatibility

All packet centers lie at the same distance

\[
d
\]

from the sampling midpoint in the \((x,c)\)-geometry. Therefore the selected core is same-scale.

Strict core gap is arranged by placing all non-core packets at distances outside a larger annulus, for example

\[
\ge 2d.
\]

Endpoint separation is open and can be preserved by choosing the sample endpoints inside the disk

\[
|u|<d/2
\]

away from packet singularities.

Gram positivity holds because

\[
q_0>0,\qquad q''=0.
\]

Thus the construction is compatible with the reduced-good-patch assumptions.

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale continuous source-collapse: proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite same-scale source-collapse to arbitrary finite order: follows by positive quadrature.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Good-patch compatibility: preserved.}
}
\]

This is a major adversarial result. It means the interval-local source-collapse countermodel is essentially complete on the zero-side packet model.

The only remaining caveat is whether actual zeta arithmetic forbids this same-scale packet distribution. But the local rank-two geometry, finite \(\xi\)-like geometry, and reduced-good-patch conditions do not.

---

# Strategic consequence

The current norm/projective rank-two architecture is non-closing unless it imports a genuinely arithmetic theorem excluding this packet source-collapse pattern.

The exact missing theorem would be something like:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem}
}
\]

stating that actual zeta zero packets cannot approximate the positive same-scale quadrature above on every RH-relevant reduced interval.

No such theorem is currently present in the framework.

## Edit 2 — Replace the existing continuous same-scale flattening remark with a theorem

**Where:** Replace the entire existing block:

\label{rem:continuous-same-scale-flattening-model}
