**Replace with:**

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Continuous same-scale source-flattening model]
\label{thm:continuous-same-scale-source-flattening-model}
Fix \(d>0\).  For
\[
c=d\sin\theta,\qquad x=d\cos\theta,\qquad 0<\theta<\pi,
\]
consider the same-distance packet kernel
\[
K_{\theta,d}(u)
=
\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2}.
\]
Let
\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]
Then, for \(|2u/d|<1\),
\[
\boxed{
\int_0^\pi K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)=\frac1d.
}
\]
Consequently,
\[
q_\mu(u):=\int_0^\pi K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)
\]
satisfies
\[
q_\mu(0)=\frac1d>0,
\qquad
q_\mu^{(r)}(0)=0
\quad (r\ge1).
\]
In particular,
\[
q_\mu^{(2)}(0)=q_\mu^{(4)}(0)=q_\mu^{(6)}(0)=\cdots=0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Put
\[
t=\frac{2u}{d}.
\]
Then
\[
K_{\theta,d}(u)
=
\frac1d
\frac{\sin\theta}{1+2t\cos\theta+t^2}.
\]
Hence
\[
\int_0^\pi K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)
=
\frac1d
\int_0^\pi
\frac{2}{\pi}
\frac{\sin^2\theta}{1+2t\cos\theta+t^2}
\,d\theta.
\]
For \(|t|<1\), the elementary Poisson-kernel identity
\[
\int_0^\pi
\frac{2}{\pi}
\frac{\sin^2\theta}{1+2t\cos\theta+t^2}
\,d\theta
=
1
\]
gives the claim.  Therefore \(q_\mu(u)=1/d\) on a neighborhood of the
origin, and all positive-order derivatives at the origin vanish.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Finite same-scale source flattening to arbitrary finite order]
\label{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}
For every \(M\ge1\), there exist finitely many angles
\[
0<\theta_1,\ldots,\theta_N<\pi
\]
and positive weights \(w_i>0\) such that, with
\[
c_i=d\sin\theta_i,\qquad x_i=d\cos\theta_i,
\]
one has
\[
x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2
\]
for every \(i\), and
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}^{(2j)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le j\le M,
\]
while
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}(0)>0.
\]
Equivalently, a finite positive same-distance packet cluster can satisfy
\[
q^{(2)}(0)=q^{(4)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(2M)}(0)=0
\]
while retaining
\[
q_0=q(0)>0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Tchakaloff's theorem, or finite-dimensional Carath\'eodory reduction, to
the positive measure \(\mu\) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:continuous-same-scale-source-flattening} and the finite list
of continuous functions
\[
K_{\theta,d}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(2)}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(4)}(0),\ldots,K_{\theta,d}^{(2M)}(0).
\]
The continuous measure has the prescribed moments.  A positive finite
quadrature rule reproduces the same finite list of moments.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Uniform same-scale caveat]
\label{rem:uniform-same-scale-caveat}
The construction above is same-scale in the strong fixed-distance sense
\(x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2\).  If a later argument requires the additional uniform
angular condition
\[
\epsilon\le \frac{c_i}{d}\le 1-\epsilon
\]
with \(\epsilon>0\) independent of \(M\), then one still needs a strengthened
annular positive-cone lemma.  The present result is already enough to show
that finite source-jet flattening is not excluded by positive same-distance
packet geometry.  Thus any proof-closing lower bound for \(q''\) must use
additional actual-zeta arithmetic, not merely same-scale positivity.
\end{remark}
```

**Case for insertion:** This is the strongest new result from the latest attack. The current draft only sketches it as a remark. It should be promoted to theorem/corollary form because it materially sharpens the no-go: finite same-scale positive packet geometry itself can flatten all finite source jets. turn69file17

---

## Edit 3 — Insert an interval-collapse corollary after the new same-scale theorem

**Where:** Insert immediately after the new `\end{remark}` from Edit 2 and before:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[No-go for the current rank-two norm route]
\label{prop:no-go-current-rank-two-norm-route}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Interval-local source collapse from finite quadrature]
\label{cor:interval-local-source-collapse-from-quadrature}
Fix \(A>0\).  Assume the packet scale is microscopic,
\[
d\asymp Q^{-1},
\]
and let
\[
I=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q]
\]
with \(c>0\) fixed sufficiently small.  For every \(C>A/3\), a finite
same-distance positive packet cluster can be chosen so that
\[
\sup_{m\in I}|q''(m)|\le Q^{-C},
\]
while
\[
q_0(m)\asymp1,\qquad g(m)>0,\qquad h(m)>0,
\]
and
\[
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}\asymp1
\]
on \(I\), after a harmless normalization of the total weight.

Consequently, at leading source order,
\[
H=yq''\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
\]
satisfies
\[
\sup_{m\in I}|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ll Q^{-3C},
\]
and therefore can be made smaller than \(Q^{-A}\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}, choose the packet
cluster so that
\[
q^{(2)}(m_0)=q^{(4)}(m_0)=\cdots=q^{(2M)}(m_0)=0.
\]
Symmetric placement also kills odd derivatives at \(m_0\).  Thus
\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)=0
\]
for all \(r\) up to the corresponding finite order.  Taking
\[
M\asymp \frac{C\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]
or more conservatively \(M=O(\log Q)\), the standard Taylor--Cauchy estimate at
scale \(d\asymp Q^{-1}\) gives
\[
\sup_I |q''|\le Q^{-C}.
\]
Normalizing the total mass so that \(q_0\) is close to \(2\), one obtains
\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}>0,
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right)>0,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3=4+O(Q^{-C}).
\]
Hence the anisotropy factor remains bounded below while the source factor
collapses cubically in \(q''\).
\end{proof}
```

**Case for insertion:** This converts the same-scale quadrature theorem into the exact interval-local countermodel needed by the proof-state discussion. It also makes explicit that the no-go is not pointwise only; it survives on a microscopic interval.

## Edit 4 — Add the corrected projective-transport obstruction formula

**Where:** Insert after the existing `\begin{remark}[No-go ledger after the source-collapse push]...\end{remark}` block, before the next subsection `\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Corrected projective transport obstruction]
\label{rem:corrected-projective-transport-obstruction}
One possible response to source divisibility is to pass to the projective ratio.
In the idealized factorized model
\[
A_7=HG_1,\qquad A_9=HG_2,\qquad H=yq'',
\]
one has
\[
[A_7:A_9]=[G_1:G_2].
\]
In the present setting \(G_1\) and \(G_2\) are represented by
\[
G_1\sim \Gamma_G,
\qquad
G_2\sim \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]
Thus projectivization formally cancels the common source factor \(H\).

However, the actual corrected rows may have the form
\[
A_7=HG_1+R_7,
\qquad
A_9=HG_2+R_9,
\]
where \(R_7,R_9\) denote line, background/core, normalization, or other
correction-row contributions not known to be \(H\)-divisible.  On the chart
\(A_7\ne0\), put
\[
Z=\frac{A_9}{A_7}.
\]
Then
\[
\nabla Z
=
\frac{A_7\nabla A_9-A_9\nabla A_7}{A_7^2},
\]
and substitution gives
\[
\begin{aligned}
A_7\nabla A_9-A_9\nabla A_7
={}&
H^2(G_1\nabla G_2-G_2\nabla G_1)\\
&+H(G_1\nabla R_9-G_2\nabla R_7)\\
&+H(R_7\nabla G_2-R_9\nabla G_1)\\
&+(\nabla H)(R_7G_2-R_9G_1)\\
&+(R_7\nabla R_9-R_9\nabla R_7).
\end{aligned}
\]
Therefore the clean source-normalized identity
\[
\nabla\left(\frac{A_9}{A_7}\right)
=
\nabla\left(\frac{G_2}{G_1}\right)
\]
is valid only if the correction rows vanish or are themselves
\(H\)-divisible.  If non-\(H\)-divisible corrections remain, then near
\(H=0\)
\[
[A_7:A_9]\to [R_7:R_9],
\]
not
\[
[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}].
\]
Thus the projective branch is coherent only after a correction-divisibility or
correction-absorption theorem, or after enlarging the projective coordinate to
\[
[A_7:A_9:R_7:R_9:\cdots].
\]
No global projective endpoint, holonomy, or index theorem is presently known
for that enlarged object.
\end{remark}
```

**Case for insertion:** The draft currently says projectivization is not proof-closing, but the exact derivative formula is the cleanest way to show why correction rows break the naive ratio. This is a valuable no-go “goodie” from the conversation. turn69file5

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Fixed-prime toy diagnostics]
\label{rem:fixed-prime-toy-diagnostics}
In the fixed-prime toy model
\[
L_P(t)=\sum_{p\le P}(\log p)p^{-1/2}e^{-it\log p},
\]
with
\[
J_0=B_0+\Re L_P,\qquad
J_2=B_2+\Re L_P'',\qquad
J_4=B_4+\Re L_P^{(4)},
\]
the residuals
\[
R_1=J_2-6J_0+2J_0^3,
\]
\[
R_2=(1-J_0^2)J_2-\frac16J_4,
\]
and
\[
H=-\frac{J_0J_2^3}{288}
\]
exhibit both failure modes of the source-weighted lower bound.

In scans with \(P=200\), source-collapse points with
\[
|H|\ll1
\]
and live anisotropy occurred repeatedly; full products
\[
|H|\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)
\]
near \(10^{-16}\) were observed in the toy model.  Targeted anisotropy
optimization also produced source-live approaches, for example
\[
|H|\approx 3.75\times 10^{-2},
\qquad
\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\approx 2.58\times 10^{-3},
\]
and another cleaner source-live point with
\[
|H|\approx 1.98\times 10^{-1},
\qquad
\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\approx 6.75\times 10^{-3}.
\]

These numerical values are not evidence about actual zeta zeros and should not
be used as proof.  Their role is diagnostic: fixed coefficients and the
one-parameter prime phase flow do not visibly enforce the desired local
source-weighted lower bound in simple finite-prime surrogates.  The positive
route must therefore identify an actual-zeta arithmetic obstruction rather
than rely on fixed-prime rigidity at the level of this toy model.
\end{remark}
```

**Case for insertion:** The current remark says experiments support source collapse, but it does not capture the concrete diagnostic values from the conversation. This insertion records them explicitly while clearly marking them non-proof data.

## Edit 6 — Add a terminal architecture decision theorem/remark before the appendix

**Where:** Insert immediately before:

```latex
\appendix
```

currently after `\end{remark}` for the proof frontier.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Terminal status of the current architecture]
\label{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}
The present proof architecture has reached the following decision point.

\begin{enumerate}
\item The original scalar Bottleneck-C closure route is blocked: the active
\(\eta\eta\)-row is \(S\)-visible and cannot be removed by source
repackaging, quotienting, split readout, line-bundle transport, or
transform-faithful normal-form counterterms.

\item The rank-two fixed-sector bundle is the correct local language for the
remaining obstruction.  It gives a coherent reduced-base connection and a
conditional affine forcing equation, but it does not supply a global
contradiction without an additional boundary, holonomy, index, or quantitative
non-concentration theorem.

\item The local packet-visibility problem is substantially improved by the
layered order-seven/order-nine theorem:
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0\Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]
modulo named correction incidence.  This is a local visibility theorem, not a
proof of \(\RH\).

\item The norm-based rank-two route is source-divisible.  The established rows
have schematic form
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H=yq''.
\]
Since
\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]
an interval on which \(q''\) is small collapses the known row vector even when
the anisotropy factor remains live.

\item The projective route cancels \(H\) formally, but it loses magnitude,
remains singular at
\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]
and is not cleanly defined for the corrected row vector unless correction rows
vanish or are \(H\)-divisible.  No global projective endpoint, holonomy, or
index theorem is currently available.

\item The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that finite
same-scale positive packet geometry does not itself prevent source collapse.
Consequently, an actual proof must use information not already present in the
local Hadamard/quartet packet geometry.

\end{enumerate}

Thus the current framework should be treated as a precise local obstruction
and diagnostic architecture.  To turn it into a proof of \(\RH\), one still
needs at least one genuinely new input:
\[
\boxed{
\text{actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness,}
}
\]
for example
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B},
\]
or a stronger finite/growing-jet interval theorem;
or else
\[
\boxed{
\text{a source-robust row/invariant,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{a global projective/affine transport index theorem.}
}
\]
Absent such an input, the present architecture is non-closing.
\end{remark}
```

**Case for insertion:** This gives the paper a clean final ledger after a very long technical section. It records the positive local results and the decisive no-go in one place.

The key late result not yet captured at theorem strength is the **same-scale positive packet quadrature construction**, which turns the source-collapse no-go from a heuristic into a precise local countermodel against finite packet geometry. The other important missing item is the exact **corrected projective derivative formula**, which explains why projectivization remains diagnostic rather than proof-closing. The final status ledger prevents the paper from overclaiming and records the current architecture accurately: strong local obstruction framework, not yet an RH proof.

```latex
This approach is not aimed at discovering new direct relations among primes. ```latex
```
```latex
\begin{remark}[Arithmetic source-curvature observability program]
\label{rem:arithmetic-source-curvature-observability-program}
The remaining positive theorem should now be formulated as a source-curvature
observability problem.  The first task is to fix a canonical actual-zeta
normalization for the source curvature
\[
q''(m).
\]
One needs both a zero-side representation
\[
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_\rho K_2(m;\rho)
\]
and a prime-side or explicit-formula representation of the schematic form
\[
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
b_n(\log n)^2 e^{-im\log n}
+
\text{dual/gamma/error terms},
\]
with \(b_n\) specialized to the actual zeta coefficients, not arbitrary
Dirichlet-polynomial coefficients.

The cleanest positive theorem to aim for is an interval \(L^2\)-observability
bound:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]
A weaker but still useful form is
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]
The countermodel analysis shows that such a theorem cannot follow from local
same-scale packet geometry alone.  In zero-side terms, it must say that the
actual zeta zeros near an off-line packet cannot arrange themselves into the
same-scale positive quadrature distribution of
Theorem~\ref{thm:continuous-same-scale-source-flattening-model}.  In
prime-side terms, it must say that the fixed-coefficient AFE/log-derivative
sum cannot approximate \(-B_2(m)\) too well on every RH-relevant packet
interval.

Thus the next arithmetic branch is not the full nonlinear residual
\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]
It is the narrower and more tractable source-curvature problem
\[
q''(m)\not\approx0
\quad\text{on }I_\rho.
\]
A possible theorem name is:
\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Off-line-packet source-curvature observability.}
}
\]
\end{remark}
```

**Reason:** This is the “ammo for the next attack.” The current paper says the missing theorem is \(\sup |q''|\ge Q^{-B}\), but it does not yet lay out the attack object: zero-side representation, prime-side representation, \(L^2\) version, and packet-quadrature obstruction. This insertion makes the next branch precise.

## Edit 1 — Fix the finite quadrature corollary’s statement/proof to match the current stronger version

**Why:** The current corollary states finite quadrature can match **all** derivatives \(1\le r\le M\). That is defensible because the continuous averaged profile is constant, but the prior proof is cleaner if it explicitly says this is a finite list of all derivatives, not only the even source jets. The title says “source flattening,” but the statement should emphasize this stronger finite-jet result and its consequence for \(q''\). This supports the same-scale packet no-go described in the latest Big Picture summary: same-scale positive packet quadrature can flatten source curvature to arbitrary finite order while preserving \(q_0>0\), Gram positivity, and live \(\Gamma_G\). 

**Where:** In `\begin{corollary}[Finite same-scale source flattening to arbitrary finite jet order]`, replace the paragraph beginning:

```latex
For every \(M\ge1\), there exist finitely many angles
...
```

through the end of that corollary, but not its proof.

**Replace with:**

```latex
For every \(M\ge1\), there exist finitely many angles
\[
0<\theta_1,\ldots,\theta_N<\pi
\]
and positive weights \(w_i>0\) such that, with
\[
c_i=d\sin\theta_i,\qquad x_i=d\cos\theta_i,
\]
one has
\[
x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2
\]
for every \(i\), and
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le r\le M,
\]
while
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}(0)>0.
\]
Equivalently, a finite positive same-distance packet cluster can satisfy
\[
q^{(r)}(0)=0,\qquad 1\le r\le M,
\]
while retaining
\[
q_0=q(0)>0.
\]
In particular, taking \(M\ge R+2\) gives
\[
(q'')^{(r)}(0)=0,\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]
```

**Reason:** This makes the “all derivatives” consequence explicit and avoids ambiguity about whether the quadrature is only even-order. It also directly links the corollary to the interval-local source-collapse target.

---

## Edit 2 — Fix the prime-side representation to include the critical-line weight

**Why:** The current “Canonical source-curvature representation problem” writes the prime-side model as
\[
\Re\sum_n b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-im}.
\]
That is too bare and can be misread as omitting the critical-line \(n^{-1/2}\), smoothing, and AFE normalization. The latest Big Picture explicitly says the arithmetic object should be fixed with a zero-side formula and a prime-side/AFE avatar before proving source-curvature observability. 

**Where:** In:

```latex
\begin{definition}[Canonical source-curvature representation problem]
\label{def:canonical-source-curvature-representation-problem}
```

find:

```latex
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\Re\sum_n b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-im}
+
\text{\rm dual/gamma/error terms}.
```

**Replace with:**

```latex
q''(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2-im}W(n/T)
+
\text{\rm dual/gamma/error terms}.
```

Then immediately after the sentence:

```latex
The coefficients \(b_n\), the smoothing, the dual term, the gamma/background
contribution, and the error terms must be specified in the same normalization
used by the rank-two local rows.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
In an actual-zeta normalization one expects \(b_n\) to be fixed by the zeta
coefficients, for example by \(\Lambda(n)\)-type log-derivative weights after
the chosen smoothing and completion conventions are fixed.  The point of the
definition is to forbid replacing this arithmetic object by an arbitrary
Dirichlet polynomial with freely tunable coefficients.
```

**Reason:** This makes the arithmetic theorem precise enough to attack next.

---

## Edit 3 — Add a concise “attack order” remark after the observability subsection

**Why:** The paper has the theorem target, but it does not yet state the practical next attack sequence. The Big Picture summary says the right attack order is: canonical source-curvature representation, actual-zeta numerical scan, packet-quadrature obstruction, local \(L^2\) observability, and only then prime-log nonrecurrence if needed. 

**Where:** Insert after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Finite-jet version of the arithmetic problem]
\label{rem:finite-jet-source-nonflatness-problem}
...
\end{remark}
```

and before:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Terminal status of the current architecture]
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Recommended arithmetic attack order]
\label{rem:recommended-arithmetic-attack-order}
The remaining arithmetic problem should be attacked in the following order.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Fix the exact source-curvature object.}  First prove a canonical
representation for \(q''\) in the chosen normalization:
\[
q''=B_2+P_2+\text{dual/gamma/error}.
\]
This must be done both on the zero side and on the prime/AFE side.

\item \emph{Test actual zeta numerically.}  Compute
\[
\sup_{m\in I}|q''(m)|
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\int_I |q''(m)|^2\,dm
\]
for actual zeta data on intervals of length comparable to \(Q^{-1}\).  This
checks whether source-flat intervals are common or rare in the true object,
rather than only in surrogates.

\item \emph{Attack the packet-quadrature obstruction.}  The same-scale
quadrature theorem shows that finite packet geometry can flatten \(q''\).  An
actual-zeta theorem must explain why the true zero configuration cannot
approximate this positive same-distance quadrature distribution near an
off-line packet.

\item \emph{Seek a local \(L^2\) observability estimate.}  The most plausible
positive theorem is
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
This is quadratic in a linear source statistic and is substantially more
tractable than the full nonlinear source-weighted residual.

\item \emph{Use prime-log nonrecurrence only if forced.}  If numerical and
zero-side evidence suggests actual source-flat intervals are absent, then one
may try to prove a nonrecurrence theorem for the fixed-coefficient prime-log
flow.  This currently appears to be the hardest route.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

**Reason:** This is “ammo” for the next attack without adding new speculative proof claims.

---

## Edit 4 — Mark the older “current proof frontier” as a historical ledger

**Why:** The paper now has both `Current branch decision`, `Current proof frontier after the local package audits`, and `Terminal status of the current architecture`. The middle ledger is still useful, but its title can read as if it is the latest frontier. Add one sentence at the start to prevent stale interpretation.

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current proof frontier after the local package audits]
\label{rem:current-proof-frontier-after-local-package-audits}
The current proof frontier is as follows.
```

**Replace that sentence with:**

```latex
This is the proof frontier after the local package audits and before the final
source-collapse reduction.  It is retained as a ledger of local dependencies;
the terminal status is given in
Remark~\ref{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}.
```

**Reason:** This avoids a stale “current frontier” collision with the terminal architecture ledger.

---

## No further edits I would make

I would **not** change the same-scale theorem, interval-collapse corollary, corrected projective transport obstruction, fixed-prime/AFE surrogate remark, prime-log recurrence remark, or terminal architecture ledger. Those are already integrated and aligned with the latest state. The only substantive missing “next attack” content is the short attack-order remark in Edit 3.
